# Signal Log

## 2026-06-29

### Second commercial vessel struck in 72h (Kiku VLCC, June 27) + US second night of strikes expands target set to minelayer capabilities — IMO evacuation stays suspended, JMIC threat level → "substantial"; the tit-for-tat is no longer "controlled"

**Indicators:** IRGC naval activity (named — second kinetic enforcement against commercial shipping in 72h, first against a laden VLCC); AIS safe-corridor / Hormuz-reopening status (IMO evacuation remains suspended, no resumption date; JMIC → "substantial"; freight rates reported at 22-month highs); US–Iran kinetic exchange (second US offensive action on Iranian soil within the 60-day window); Brent vs. the $130 trigger (~$72, FALLING)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict

**Scenario impact:** Escalation-direction, **Level 1 — no L4 fires by the literal text.** On June 27 an IRGC attack drone struck the **Kiku** (Panama-flagged VLCC, ~300,866 dwt, ~2M bbl Qatari crude) in the Strait — minor bridge damage, **no casualties, no sinking**, vessel remained seaworthy and continued transit (CENTCOM attribution, Tier 1). Same period, the US ran a **second night of strikes** on Iranian military targets, the set now expanded to **minelayer capabilities** — the first time the L4 Hormuz-closure language ("mined") connects to an actual targeting event (the US is pre-emptively striking the mining-enablement infrastructure). **L4 check — does NOT fire:** vessel ≠ infrastructure; no UNCLOS closure; no casualties; Brent ~$72 and falling. **Two qualitative escalators vs. June 25:** (a) the Kiku was reportedly struck *on the designated safe corridor* (Tier 3 attribution, needs Windward/UKMTO Tier 1/2 confirmation) — if confirmed, the IRGC attacked the MOU's *operational implementation mechanism*, not an opportunistic commercial vessel, and did so *while the IMO evacuation was already suspended* (during a safety-guarantee review, not in defiance of an active guarantee); (b) freight rates at 22-month highs are a **real-economy transmission not visible in Brent**.

**Source:** CENTCOM attribution (Tier 1) convergent via CNBC / NPR (Tier 2); gCaptain "Second Tanker Struck in Strait of Hormuz" + Seatrade Maritime + Windward "Hormuz's Stalled Recovery" (Tier 2 specialist); IMO evacuation-suspension release (Tier 1); US second-night strikes — NPR / CNN / Al Jazeera (Tier 2 convergent; standalone CENTCOM release URL not located, treat strike as Tier 2 convergent pending direct link). **Corridor-attribution caveat:** the "designated safe route" framing is **Tier 3 (TechTimes)** only — pending Tier 1/2 confirmation.

**Note:** The "designated safe corridor" detail and the "minelayer" target category are the two analytically load-bearing elements; both need firmer sourcing but both point the same direction — the kinetic arena is now contesting the *implementation framework itself*, not just transiting tonnage. Combined with the June 28 entry below, this is the **second kinetic data point** that the June 26 pass named as the condition for the staged Three-Body follow-on.

### Iran fires real ballistic missiles at two US bases (Ali Al Salem / Kuwait + Fifth Fleet HQ / Bahrain, June 28) — Kuwait intercepts, Bahrain confirms civilian damage, CENTCOM reports no force damage; first direct Iran-on-US-base attack of the war — RELEASES the staged Three-Body follow-on addendum on geometry grounds

**Indicators:** IRGC aerospace activity (named — first confirmed Iranian ballistic-missile launch at US military installations this war; qualitative step-change from vessel-strike-and-claim); Scenario C/D pressure (direct state-on-state exchange at US basing hubs — kinetics no longer confined to the maritime corridor); AIS / Hormuz status (escalation during the implementation window); Brent vs. $130 ($72, falling)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict

**Scenario impact:** Escalation-direction, **Level 1 by the letter — but a categorical geometry shift, so the staged addendum RELEASES (user decision).** On June 28 Iran launched ballistic missiles at **Ali Al Salem Air Base (Kuwait)** and **US Fifth Fleet HQ / NSA Bahrain (Juffair)**. Layered verification: **real BMs launched and intercepted — CONFIRMED** (Kuwait government, Tier 1 ally — two detected/intercepted, no casualties); **partial penetration of the Bahrain area — CONFIRMED** (Bahrain Interior Ministry, Tier 1 — a residential building near the airport damaged, no fatalities); **no damage to US forces — CONFIRMED** (CENTCOM, Tier 1); IRGC "8 US infrastructure targets destroyed" — **REPORTED-UNVERIFIED** (Iranian state claim, CENTCOM denies). **Materially different from the June 26 ISNA counter-strike claim** (which CENTCOM ignored with zero specifics): here CENTCOM *actively contests the outcome*, which at minimum confirms the missiles were real and launched at US installations. **L4 — does NOT fire:** CENTCOM reports no force damage; Bahrain damage is civilian, not military infrastructure; no nuclear/radiological event; Brent $72; 10yr 4.38.

**Source:** Kuwait government (Tier 1 foreign — intercepts, no casualties); Bahrain Interior Ministry (Tier 1 foreign — residential damage); CENTCOM (Tier 1 US — no force damage); IRGC claim via Al Jazeera / Deccan Chronicle (Tier 2 / Iranian-state — "8 targets," unverified); Al Jazeera "Iran and US trade attacks as Strait of Hormuz ceasefire falters" + Gulf News (Tier 2 framing).

**Note:** **Staged Three-Body follow-on addendum — RELEASED this pass (user adjudication: kinetic-return geometry shift).** The literal staged trigger (d) — "CENTCOM-*confirmed* strike on US forces" — is **not** met (CENTCOM: no force damage). The release is on **geometry grounds independent of the letter triggers:** the June 24 implementation-phase addendum's central thesis was that the spoiler had *migrated from the kinetic channel to the process channel* ("the collision surface moved from the Litani to the memorandum text"). June 27–28 **partially falsifies that** — the spoiler vector has **returned to direct kinetics at a NEW theater** (GCC military hubs via ballistic missiles + a second vessel on the designated corridor), the "new variable" the escalation tree names for an L3 update. The original three-body framing (Israel–Iran–US + Hezbollah fourth body) still holds → **addendum, not full report.** Report Writer dispatched. Market-decoupling (Brent $72, HY-contained, VIX 18.4) is *content for* the addendum, not a reason to suppress it: geometry escalated, market shrugged.

### HY OAS widening (+20bp, June 17→26: 2.63→2.83%) is rate-path repricing — BofA three-hike call is the driver, NOT Iran-risk — answering the standing structural question; deepens Minsky Phase 3 but is endogenous to the Regulatory story, so no independent convergence vector

**Indicators:** HY OAS (named — 2.83% June 26 per FRED Tier 1, +20bp over 9 sessions, now *directional* not flat-tight); Warsh dot-plot execution risk (named — BofA projects the institutional-capture-vector dots to print: ~75bp Sep/Oct/Dec → bench 4.25–4.50% by Dec 2026); zombie-refinancing-failure channel (Minsky Phase 3 deepening)

**Sections:** Global Debt (cross-cutting Regulatory — the Warsh dots)

**Scenario impact:** Structural-deepening, **Level 1 — confirmatory of an already-logged driver.** The standing structural question (is the HY creep Iran-risk, Fed-path, or idiosyncratic credit?) resolves to **Fed-path:** the +20bp widening tracks BofA's June 22 three-hike note ("inflation getting unambiguously worse"), not the Iran kinetics (Brent fell through the same window) and not a credit event (none occurred). **What this changes:** the HY widening is *endogenous to the Regulatory / monetary-policy story already logged* (Warsh hawkish dots, June 19 L2) — it deepens the Minsky Phase 3 zombie-refinancing channel via a higher real-rate forecast but provides **no independent Global Debt vector** for cross-section convergence. The "HY-tight as structural disqualifier" framing weakens slightly (+20bp) but **remains operative at 2.83% vs. the 3.5% break / 5.0% WARN.**

**Source:** FRED BAMLH0A0HYM2 (Tier 1 — 2.83% June 26, ground-truth in prices.csv); BofA research note via CNBC / Fortune (Tier 2, June 22, multi-outlet convergent).

**Note:** This is the confirmatory reading that extends the June 22 BofA L1 entry into credit-market pricing. It does NOT advance the broader Minsky phase; it deepens the existing Phase 3 position. The directional-widening test result is logged for the next convergence adjudication: HY is no longer flat-tight, but it is still *endogenous-not-independent*, which is the load-bearing reason convergence non-fires this pass despite a genuine two-section (Armed Conflict + rate-path) escalation.

### Hormuz throughput quantified (June 29): strait transits recovered to ~33% then COLLAPSED back to ~10–14% after the Kiku strike — but total outflow (incl. STS + pipeline bypass) holds ~33–45%; the (A)-vs-(C) divergence IS the release valve, measured

**Indicators:** AIS strait-transit count (named — ~13/day June 29 vs. ~44/day June 22–26 peak); STS-anchorage / pipeline-bypass throughput (the release-valve workaround); Brent vs. the $130 trigger ($72, explained by total-outflow not strait-count)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict (cross-cutting Global Debt via the oil-supply / Brent channel)

**Scenario impact:** Release-valve CONFIRMED with numbers, **Level 1.** The project's load-bearing distinction — *"ships transiting the strait" ≠ "oil flowing"* — is now quantified across the two measurements:
- **(A) AIS strait transits — ~13/day (June 29) = ~10–14% of the pre-war baseline** (Windward 130–138/day, Tier 2, CONFIRMED). This is the headline "closure" number. **The user's recalled "<20%" is approximately right for (A) today.** But (A) had *recovered* to **~44/day (~33%; single-day peak ~49 on June 24)** during the post-signing window June 22–26, then **collapsed ~70% to ~13/day** after the June 27 Kiku strike + the IRGC corridor-enforcement directive ("AIS off, or off-route, you carry the consequences"). The **44→13 reversal is the measurable fingerprint of the kinetic channel pushing the strait number back down** — the empirical signature of the "spoiler returned to kinetics" thesis in the same-day kinetic-return addendum.
- **(C) Total oil outflow incl. workaround — ~6.5–9 mb/d = ~33–45% of the 20 mb/d baseline** (composite estimate, REPORTED-UNVERIFIED). **This has NEVER been below ~20%** — the user's "<20%" does NOT describe (C). Components: STS off Fujairah/Sohar ~1.5–2 mb/d (≥90M bbl since early May, US-Navy-monitored); Habshan–Fujairah ~1.1–1.5 mb/d and Petroline/East-West to the Red Sea ~2–3 mb/d — **both pipelines bypass the strait entirely and sit outside IRGC corridor reach.** The pipeline-only bypass is a **structural ~15–20% floor that holds even at zero strait transits.**

**Brent-at-$72 reconciliation:** $72 tracks (C), not (A) — workaround floor (~6.5 mb/d) + IEA reserve releases (~4.1 mb/d) + April-$138-spike demand destruction + the Bürgenstock deal as a market put. **Falsifier un-tripped:** June 25–28 hit vessels *on the AIS corridor*, never the Gulf-of-Oman STS anchorages or the pipelines — the one thing that would break $72. Stranded-vessel backlog is **re-accumulating** post-IMO-suspension (est. ~100–120 tankers still inside the Gulf; NOT FOUND at Tier 1/2 with a specific post-suspension count).

**Source:** Windward "IRGC Turn-Back Order Stalls Strait of Hormuz Recovery" + "Hormuz's Stalled Recovery" (Tier 2 specialist, June 29 datelines); Lloyd's List "Ships keep moving through Hormuz…" (Tier 2); PortNews citing US Navy monitoring — ≥90M bbl STS (Tier 2, through June 17); CNBC "two oil pipelines helping Saudi Arabia and UAE bypass Hormuz" (Tier 2); Kpler/Outlook Money transit counts (Tier 2). **Staleness:** STS figure 12 days old (through June 17); Kpler ~4.8 mb/d strait-volume figure is **pre-Kiku (June 13–21) — do NOT use as a current read**; Petroline ramp above its ~2 mb/d floor unconfirmed; the ~13/day June 29 count is a single-day Windward read (directional, not yet 24h-confirmed).

**Note:** This is the quantitative backbone for the June 29 kinetic-return addendum's two-truths thesis — **geometry escalated (strait 44→13) while the market decoupled (C holds 33–45% → Brent $72).** No escalation beyond L1: the data *confirms* the release valve rather than moving a scenario ≥15pp or advancing a framework phase. The standing watch item it sharpens: the STS anchorages / pipeline infrastructure remain the named falsifier — if either is struck, (C) collapses and the $72 read breaks.

### Continuation / disposition note (June 29 pass): tit-for-tat BROKE, 3× L1 + throughput L1, Three-Body follow-on RELEASED on geometry, L4 non-fire, DTC holds ORANGE — and two monitor data-errors corrected (aggregates are current; MSACSR L2 does NOT clear)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict, Global Debt

- **Pass disposition.** Four L1 entries (June 27 Kiku + US second-night strikes; June 28 Iran BMs at two US bases; HY = rate-path repricing; Hormuz throughput quantification — the (A)-vs-(C) release-valve measurement). **One L3 — the Three-Body follow-on addendum RELEASED** (kinetic-return geometry shift; Report Writer dispatched). No L4, no scenario-table change.
- **The tit-for-tat read BROKE.** The June 25–26 "controlled exchange" characterization does **not** survive June 27–28: a *second* commercial vessel struck in 72h (likely on the safe corridor), the US target set expanded to *minelayer capabilities*, and Iran fired *real ballistic missiles* at two US bases in two GCC countries. The 60-day Bürgenstock roadmap is formally intact (no party has repudiated it) but under active kinetic stress ("ceasefire on brink," Tier 2 framing).
- **Brent ~$72 and falling is the paradox of the week** (independently web-sourced; CSV Brent feed dark since June 23). The most extreme release-valve confirmation yet — the oil market priced de-escalation *through* accelerating kinetics. Either the market reads the exchange as controlled theater, or the STS workaround off Fujairah/Sohar is fully absorbing flow (no evidence the STS anchorages were struck — the named falsifier remains un-tripped).
- **L4 — non-fire.** All immediate triggers negative (Brent $72 « $130; 10yr 4.38 « 5.0; no SIFI/derivatives, no G7 downgrade, no nuclear/radiological, no Hormuz *infrastructure* strike or UNCLOS closure). **Convergence non-fires:** Armed Conflict is escalatory and HY widened, but the HY move is *endogenous* to the Regulatory/rate-path story (not an independent debt vector) — the structural disqualifier holds (2.83% « 3.5%). **DTC HOLDS ORANGE** — the escalation is kinetic, not diplomatic, so axis-C keeps running (reinforces the breach, no change to the reading); axis-A runway NOT extended (crude has not operationally moved). NDI HOLDS RED-not-CRITICAL.
- **Monitor data-error #1 corrected — aggregates are CURRENT, not stale.** The Monitor flagged MSACSR-May, May-CPI, and May-unemployment as "not in aggregates.csv" and recommended an immediate fetch. **All three are present** (MSACSR May 10.3, CPI 333.979, unemployment 4.3); only Case-Shiller lags, at its normal ~2-month publication cadence (March). The user's "no new aggregates" is correct — nothing to fetch.
- **Monitor data-error #2 corrected — MSACSR L2 does NOT clear.** The Monitor counted May as the "third consecutive crossing above 9.0" and suggested an L2. The series is **Jan 9.8 · Feb 9.1 · Mar 8.5 (breaks the streak) · Apr 9.4 · May 10.3** — the current run is **two** consecutive (April, May), not three. The watch-list "sustained crossing" test (third consecutive) clears on the **June** MSACSR print (Census release ~late July). Housing stays **PARKED on data**, consistent with the June-24 memory carry. ROAD Act unchanged (Trump withholding; ~July 7 auto-enactment clock) — watch only.

## 2026-06-26

### IRGC drone strike on a commercial vessel in the Hormuz transit lane (June 25): first post-signing kinetic escalation — L4 Hormuz clause does NOT fire by the letter (vessel ≠ infrastructure); the narrative and kinetic arenas diverge

**Indicators:** IRGC naval activity (named — now KINETIC against a commercial vessel on a UN-backed evacuation route, not a declaration); AIS safe-corridor / Hormuz status (IMO paused the evacuation); Brent vs. the $130 trigger ($74.7, bounced ~2% on the strike)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict

**Scenario impact:** Escalation-direction, **Level 1 — the L4 Hormuz-closure clause does NOT fire by the literal text.** On June 25 the IRGC drone-struck the *Ever Lovely* (Evergreen, Singapore-flagged container ship) 7.5nm SE of Dahit, Oman — bridge damage, no casualties, no environmental impact. The IMO **paused the Hormuz stranded-fleet evacuation** "to reconfirm that the necessary safety guarantees continue to be in place." An intercepted IRGC Navy radio broadcast asserted corridor control: "Transit only with IRGC permission, on designated routes… AIS off, or off-route, and you carry the consequences." **L4 check — does NOT fire:** the escalation-tree clause reads "physical *infrastructure* struck, mined, or formally closed under international law"; a *vessel* is not infrastructure, the strait was not mined, and no formal UNCLOS closure was declared (the radio warning is a behavioral assertion; the IMO pause is voluntary). Brent ticked **+~2% to $74.7** (from $73.74 June 24) — a partial re-pricing of closure risk, still far below the $130 trigger.

**Source:** UKMTO Warning 074-26 (Tier 1); US officials (Tier 1 statements via Fox), Ambrey / Reuters drone assessment (Tier 2), Evergreen company confirmation (Tier 1); IMO press release on the evacuation pause (Tier 1); IRGC radio broadcast (Euronews / NBC, Tier 2); Brent (CNBC / NBC, Tier 2).

**Note:** The **two-arena divergence** is the analytical core, per the framing this pass adopts (Reviewer: confirmation, not transition — no scenario moves ≥15pp; this is the counter-directionality the June 24 addendum already models): the **narrative/posturing arena** (the signed Bürgenstock deal, the 60-day roadmap, the IMO-backed evacuation) says de-escalation, while the **kinetic arena** (this strike + the radio command) shows the IRGC asserting *physical* corridor authority during the implementation phase. This is qualitatively new — the prior June 11/19/22 closure declarations were *narrative* (military statements, not state acts); this is the first *post-signing kinetic enforcement against a commercial vessel on a UN-backed route*. It supersedes the deferred Fujairah/Sohar geography flag with a sharper **clause-definition question — vessel-strike-in-corridor vs. infrastructure-only — RAISED FOR USER DECISION, not actioned.** **Synthesis Reviewer verdict (this pass):** L1 confirmed — the strike *tests the release-valve falsifier the June 24 Three-Body implementation-phase addendum already named, and it held* (Brent +~2% only, no oil panic, no infrastructure, no casualty). The one new element — the **kinetic channel re-asserting during implementation** (IRGC drone + corridor-control radio directly countermanding an IMO mandate) — is a mild tension with that addendum's "spoiler changed channels to process" thesis, but a single data point does not materially update the geometry. **A Three-Body follow-on addendum is therefore STAGED, not fired** — it fires on a *second* kinetic data point: a strike on the STS anchorages (the named falsifier), a sinking/casualty event, or a Brent break. The munitions-supply-chain strain thread is VERIFIED and logged separately below.

### US strikes Iran in retaliation for the Ever Lovely attack (June 26): IRGC coastal military sites near Sirik hit — tit-for-tat the oil market reads as DE-escalation (Brent −3%); Iran's counter-strike CLAIM unverified; no L4

**Indicators:** US–Iran kinetic exchange / IRGC naval activity (named — first US retaliatory strike on Iranian soil within the 60-day implementation window); Brent vs. the $130 trigger ($72.95, DOWN ~3% on the strike, ~−10% on the week); AIS safe-corridor / Hormuz status

**Sections:** Armed Conflict

**Scenario impact:** Kinetic-escalation but **market-read DE-escalatory, Level 1 — no L4 fires by the literal text.** On June 26 US aircraft struck **IRGC missile/drone storage + coastal radar near Sirik** (Hormozgan, eastern Hormuz coast) — ~6 aircraft / 4 targets (CENTCOM Tier 1; per-target specifics REPORTED-UNVERIFIED) — in direct retaliation for the **June 25 IRGC drone attack on the *Ever Lovely*** (logged above). CENTCOM: "a powerful response to Iran's unwarranted aggression against commercial shipping" that "violated the ceasefire"; Iran's parliament called the drone attack "ceasefire management, not a violation." **No nuclear sites** (Sirik is coastal military; Natanz/Fordow/Isfahan inland, NOT targeted). **L4 — does NOT fire:** no nuclear/radiological event; no Hormuz *infrastructure* struck or UNCLOS closure (Sirik mainland military ≠ strait navigation infrastructure — Qeshm adjacency doctrine applies); Brent **$72.95 and FALLING**; 10yr 4.41, no SIFI event. **Decisive read: the oil market FELL ~3% (~−10% on the week) on a US airstrike on Iranian soil** — release-valve thesis confirmed to near-extreme; Hormuz-kinetics now fully decoupled from oil-supply risk in market pricing.

**Source:** CENTCOM news release (Tier 1, June 26 — "U.S. Forces Complete Latest Strikes in Iran"); AP "U.S. strikes Iran in response to drone attack on cargo ship…" (Binkley + Gambrell, Tier 2) via PBS / NPR; CBS / NBC / Al Jazeera / The War Zone (Tier 2 — 6 aircraft / 4 targets / Sirik); Brent $72.95 (CNBC / Trading Economics, Tier 2); Iran parliament framing (Azizi, Tier 2). **Misdating caution:** a CNBC "Brent jumps 3% after Iran vows retaliation" item is the **May 26** Bandar Abbas episode, not June 26 — do not conflate.

**Note:** Closes the Ever Lovely retaliation pair; the **two-arena divergence sharpens** — a full bilateral exchange in the kinetic arena while the narrative arena (the 60-day MOU + the Doha CENTCOM–IRGC deconfliction cell) technically HOLDS and the market sides with the narrative (Brent down; Khamenei resurfaced but did NOT repudiate the MOU). **Iran's claimed IRGC counter-strike on US bases — VERIFIED to be IRAN-CLAIMS-ONLY, NOT logged as fact:** the ISNA statement carries no specifics (no base named, no munitions count, no damage) — the inverse of the telegraphed-and-detailed Jan-2020 Ain al-Asad pattern; **CENTCOM is SILENT** (and has consistently *confirmed* prior attacks on US forces this war — the silence is informative); **zero new US casualties**; Brent falling. All consistent with an information-operations claim, not a confirmed kinetic strike. *Data-hygiene:* the "IRGC struck a US air base after Sirik" Anadolu / Times-of-Israel / Iran-International headlines are from **June 1** (a prior retaliation sequence) — surfaced as pattern-matches, NOT June 26 events. **Staged Three-Body follow-on addendum — does NOT fire and stays HELD:** none of the three staged triggers (STS-anchorage strike / sinking-casualty / Brent break) is met; the one element that could have constituted new geometry — a confirmed strike on US bases — is unverified with CENTCOM silent and oil falling, so confirmed new geometry is absent. The non-escalatory tit-for-tat read holds; release-valve dynamics intact.

### Trump–defense-CEO munitions meeting + $35.3B THAAD award + $87.6B war supplemental (June 24): the ordnance-cost-asymmetry monitoring indicators fire for the first time — inventory stress meets the political-achievement clock

**Indicators:** US interceptor replenishment / surge procurement (named `ordnance-cost-asymmetry.md` §8 indicator — FIRES: $35.3B sole-source THAAD ~12/yr→~400/yr; $398.7M AMRAAM); US defense supplemental / emergency munitions appropriations (named §8 indicator — FIRES: $87.6B supplemental, $21B munitions → sovereign-debt transmission channel); DPA Title III munitions invocation (June 11)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict (defense-industrial) — cross-cutting Global Debt (fiscal / sovereign-debt transmission)

**Scenario impact:** Escalation-direction (structural), **Level 1.** On June 24 Trump met defense-prime CEOs — **Boeing, Lockheed Martin, Honeywell** (NOT RTX/Northrop/GD; those were a separate March meeting — do not miscount) — on munitions production ramp + stockpile replenishment after the Iran war. Same day: MDA awarded Lockheed a **$35.3B sole-source THAAD** contract through 2032 (production target ~12/yr → ~400/yr), Raytheon **$398.7M** for AMRAAM, and the White House submitted an **$87.6B supplemental** ($67B DoD, $21B weapons/munitions). Backdrop: **DPA Title III invoked June 11 — six days BEFORE the June 17 signing** — citing "systemic constraints in the munitions base." CSIS "Last Rounds?" (April 24, Tier 2) quantifies the draw: **THAAD ≥50% depleted, PAC-3 ~50%, PrSM ≥45%, JASSM >1,000 fired, Tomahawk >1,000**; the **solid-rocket-motor line is the single binding upstream bottleneck**; PAC-3/THAAD recovery not until **mid-to-late 2029.** This is the first firing of two named §8 monitoring indicators (interceptor surge + defense supplemental). **No L4** (no trigger breached; HY 2.76% whiplash, 10yr 4.41 « 5.0).

**Source:** MDA contract awards + Lockheed Martin press release (Tier 1, June 24); RTX framework agreements (Tier 1, Feb 4); DPA Title III invocation (Tier 2 convergent — CNN / Washington Times / The Hill, June 11–18); CSIS "Last Rounds?" (Tier 2, April 24); CNBC / Military Times / The Hill on the meeting + supplemental (Tier 2, June 24–25).

**Note:** Provenance-clean (procurement primaries + CSIS) — no Trump-whiplash discount. The **strain framing** (user): inventory stress vs. the political-achievement clock. The munitions-exhaustion-as-release-valve read (DPA-before-deal timing + the supplemental) is **a background variable with a live falsifier, NOT a confirmed driver** — CSIS's own caveat is that current stocks are "adequate for THIS war under any plausible scenario"; the depletion is a future-Pacific vulnerability, not an Iran-campaign operational ceiling. It therefore *sharpens the structural form* of the ordnance-cost-asymmetry thesis (the 2029 recovery + SRM bottleneck quantify the cost-exchange-ratio ceiling and the §6.1 debt-amplification channel) while *bounding the operational form*. Cross-section **CONVERGENCE evaluated and NON-FIRES** — the $87.6B supplemental is the fiscal cost of the war, *endogenous* to the Armed Conflict leg (one shock counted twice), and HY-tight (2.76%) is the load-bearing structural disqualifier. A watch-list gap-fill registering this defense-industrial/munitions channel as a standing indicator is **applied this pass — Level 2 (see disposition).**

- **L4 Hormuz clause — HELD infrastructure-only (user decision).** The vessel-attrition gap (a severe strike campaign could choke the strait without striking "infrastructure" or filing a UNCLOS notice) is acknowledged as a **known, accepted limitation**; the escalation tree is NOT edited.
- **Cross-section CONVERGENCE — NON-FIRE.** Breadth present (strike + $87.6B supplemental + $35.3B THAAD within 48h) but disqualified by: HY-tight (2.76%, load-bearing), counter-direction, and the supplemental's non-independence (the war's fiscal cost counted twice, not an independent debt vector). ## 2026-06-24

**Sections:** Armed Conflict (cross-cutting Global Debt via the sanctions-waiver / oil-supply channel, Regulatory via INARA)

**Scenario impact:** Mixed-direction, **Level 1; RELEASES the held Three-Body L3 addendum (see disposition).** The Bürgenstock ceremony postponed June 19 **reconvened and concluded June 21–22** — Iran attended (Araqchi led; US side Vance + Witkoff + Kushner), the June 17 digital MOU stands, and the summit produced NEW elements: a roadmap to a final deal within **60 days**, a US–Iran deconfliction **hotline**, a US Treasury **60-day general license** on Iranian oil (issued June 23, expires Aug 21), and a **lift of the US naval blockade** of Iranian ports. Mediators (Qatar + Pakistan) confirmed the roadmap; Swiss FDFA welcomed "constructive progress." **The central caveat — this is a contested implementation clock, not a clean close:** IAEA site access is in OPEN PUBLIC DISPUTE on Day 1 — Vance says Iran agreed to invite inspectors; Iran's foreign ministry says no inspection protocol for the damaged sites exists and no Grossi meeting occurred; Grossi says the MOU text "explicitly" provides for IAEA supervision. **The signing was delegation-level — NOT Khamenei-level;** no new Tier 1 Khamenei statement on the June 21–22 outcomes was found (the SL record remains the June 18 Mojtaba Khamenei statement, Tier 2). **L4 does not fire** (no strike/mine/UNCLOS closure; Brent ~$77 « $130; the June 22 IRGC re-closure statement is again a military, not a state, act, and CENTCOM disputed it in real time). Hormuz commercial traffic has NOT operationally normalized post-summit (Argus: "tanker traffic unchanged"; Windward 12 transits June 22 vs. 21 prior) — the reopening is political, not yet operational.

**Source:** Bürgenstock summit + roadmap — Qatar/Pakistan mediator joint statement, Swiss FDFA (Tier 1 indirect via Tier 2); CNBC, Al Jazeera, NPR (Tier 2 convergent — hotline, blockade lift); US Treasury 60-day general license (Tier 1 indirect via CNBC/Al Jazeera/NPR, June 23); IAEA dispute — Vance vs. Iran MFA vs. Grossi (Tier 2 convergent, all three positions on record); Brent ~$77.4 (Fortune/TradingKey/EIA, Tier 2); Hormuz traffic (Argus Media/Windward, Tier 2).

**Note:** The June 19 hold condition for the Three-Body L3 addendum ("pending the signing actually occurring") is now MET — the addendum is **RELEASED to the Report Writer this pass.** New geometry it must capture: the process-spoiler vector has migrated from kinetic/INARA levers to **nuclear-verification obstruction in the implementation phase** (the IAEA-access dispute), operating inside a live 60-day clock. Original Three-Body thesis holds → addendum, not full report. DTC axis-C reset re-adjudicated and NOT taken (delegation-level, no Khamenei Tier 1 — bar unmet; see composites). ## 2026-06-22

### Independent transit data resolves the conflicting Hormuz closure claims — the strait-count (A) vs. STS-anchorage (C) divergence is now measured; release-valve thesis confirmed with numbers (June 11–22)

**Indicators:** AIS safe-corridor / Hormuz-reopening status (named indicator — quantitative update to the June 16 Reuters STS entry: the gap between AIS-visible strait transits and destination-arrival flows is now bounded); IRGC naval activity (the Iran closure claim and the US flows-continue claim are both technically true — different waters)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict

**Scenario impact:** Thesis-confirming / escalation-neutral, **Level 1 — quantitative update to the folded June 16 Reuters STS entry, not a new escalation.** Independent (non-government) tracking resolves the conflicting June 11/19 closure declarations: both governments describe different geographies. **(A) Strait AIS-visible transits** collapsed to **1–7 vessels/day June 11–14** (~1–8% of the ~90–100/day pre-crisis baseline; Windward, Tier 2), recovering to **~20 visible + 5 dark on June 21** (~20% of baseline; Bloomberg/EnergyConnects, Tier 2) — Iran's closure claim is technically supportable *on the visible corridor*. **(B) The AIS undercount is real:** Windward caught **6 tankers broadcasting spoofed positions** ~55nm SE of the strait off Musandam (June 13, EO/SAR imagery) and estimated **16 dark tankers / ~8.6M bbl** transiting in the 7 days ending June 11 — AIS misses an estimated ~half of transits. **(C) The workaround outside the strait peaked exactly as the strait emptied:** **17 simultaneous STS transfer pairs** off Fujairah/Sohar on June 11 (satellite via Reuters/TankerTrackers); ADNOC's June spot sales reached **48M bbl with STS off Sohar as the named delivery mechanism** (Baird Maritime, June 22). **The decisive number:** while AIS-strait transits ran 1–7/day, **Vortexa tracked 3.4 mb/d of oil arriving at destination ports** (week ending June 13) — oil moving at ~4–10× what the strait picture implied. That gap *is* the release valve, measured. **L4 does not fire** — no physical strike/mining/UNCLOS-enforced closure; Brent ~$80 « $130.

**Source:** EIA STEO + chokepoint brief (Tier 1, eia.gov — ~20 mb/d baseline, Q1 2026 −6 mb/d/−30%); Windward AI (Tier 2 specialist, AIS+EO+SAR — trough counts, Musandam spoofing cluster, dark-tanker estimates); Vortexa (Tier 2 — destination arrivals); Reuters/TankerTrackers (Tier 2 — June 11 STS peak, June 6 Sohar 2.3M-bbl transfer); Baird Maritime citing ADNOC (Tier 2, June 22 — spot-tender STS terms); Bloomberg/EnergyConnects (Tier 2 — June 21 recovery). FEDCom/FOIZ June weekly storage **NOT FOUND** (S&P Platts paywall). Aggregator figures ("71 transits June 19–21"; CENTCOM "17M bbl June 21–22 weekend") **REPORTED-UNVERIFIED** — not relied on.

**Note:** Honest ceiling on the "crisis canceled" framing — even at 3.4 mb/d, total outbound is still only ~15–17% of the normal 20 mb/d; the release valve is buying runway, not replacing throughput (IEA emergency releases ~4.1 mb/d, May OMR, cover much of the rest). Pass was triggered by a Calhoun Forbes op-ed ("The Oil Market Canceled The Hormuz Crisis — Even Before The Ceasefire," June 18) — op-ed, **not logged**; the market facts above are sourced to primaries. Reinforces the June 19 escalation-tree-geography flag: the (A)-vs-(C) divergence shows the true oil-panic trigger has migrated to a kinetic break of the STS anchorages *outside* the strait.

### EIA June 9 STEO release — demand destruction caps the Hormuz price spike; the Tier 1 primary behind Brent peaking ~$95–101, not $130 (June 9)

**Indicators:** Brent price path vs. the $130 L4 trigger (named indicator — the demand-side mechanism now sourced to a Tier 1 primary); IEA/EIA demand outlook

**Sections:** Armed Conflict

**Scenario impact:** De-escalation-direction, **Level 1.** The EIA's June 9 release — "EIA expects a drop in global oil demand will limit price increases from Hormuz disruptions" — supplies the **demand-destruction** mechanism (high prices → consumption falls ~1 mb/d → price self-limits); Brent projected ~$95–105 near-term, reverting to ~$79 in 2027. This is the Tier 1 primary explaining why Brent peaked ~$95–101 and never approached the $130 trigger — *complementary to, not competing with*, the supply-routing release valve in the entry above. Demand-destruction means the supply shock was real and corrected partly through economic pain; supply-rerouting means part of the shock was phantom. Both are operating; together they held Brent at ~$80.

**Source:** EIA Short-Term Energy Outlook + June 9 press release (Tier 1, eia.gov).

**Note:** Fills a genuine gap — the demand mechanism was implicit across prior entries but never sourced to its Tier 1 primary. Keeping the two mechanisms (demand cap + supply reroute) distinct matters: they carry different implications — demand-destruction is bearish for the real economy, supply-reroute is not.

The Phase 5 thesis predicted political capture → a dovish override of the price-stability mandate; Warsh delivered the **opposite** — the dot-plot median flipped to a **2026 hike** (3.8% end-year, 9/18 projecting ≥1 hike), the easing-bias language was stripped entirely, and the SEP PCE forecast was raised to 3.6%. The cut-binary the watch list named as the hard Phase 5 confirmation therefore **NON-FIRES**, and the framework does not advance to confirmed Phase 5. The analytically decisive turn: a hawkish Warsh actively cuts AGAINST the dovish-capture limb of the thesis. **But the capture vector relocates rather than disappears** — Warsh abstained from submitting his own dot ("not helpful in the conduct of policy"), gutted the statement to ~130 words (from 341), and announced **five external task forces** to overhaul Fed operations (inflation framework, productivity/jobs, data, communications-incl-dot-plot, balance sheet). Reshaping the independent body's machinery (dot-plot elimination) is itself a Phase-5-adjacent institutional-capture marker, on a different axis than rate dovishness. **Level 4 — does not fire** (10yr 4.49% < 5.0%; no SIFI/derivatives/rating/repo/nuclear/Hormuz event). Cycle holds at the Phase 4/5 boundary.

**Source:** FOMC statement + SEP (Tier 1, federalreserve.gov — confirmed via convergent Tier 2); CNBC, Fox Business, Kiplinger, TheStreet (Tier 2, consistent on all figures + Warsh press-conference quotes).

**Note:** Provenance-clean Tier 1 primary event — no Trump-whiplash discount applies. This is the L2 evaluation window the June 9/10 passes pre-staged; the L2 fires on *conduct*, not the rate. Forward watch: the dot-plot-elimination task force as a named institutional-capture marker, and whether an actual 2026 hike (if the dots are executed) deepens the zombie-refinancing-failure pressure (Minsky Phase 3) rather than advancing Phase 5.

### Bank of England publishes the 2nd SWES scenario (June 19): "Private Markets System-Wide Exploratory Scenario" — a central-bank stress test of the exact bank→private-credit channel the framework tracks (June 19)

**Indicators:** Bank→private-credit direct-lending exposure (named Global Debt indicator — structural-context advance: the channel is now being probed at the FPC-directed level); shadow banking stress events (the exercise's liquidity-mismatch scope maps to this indicator)

**Sections:** Global Debt

**Scenario impact:** Structural-context / forward-marker, **Level 1.** The BoE published the scenario for its second SWES on June 19 — **46 firms** spanning insurers, pension funds, PE funds, **private credit funds, CLO managers, and the banks providing sponsor leverage**. It explicitly probes bank↔NBFI interconnection, the redemption-rights-vs-illiquid-assets liquidity mismatch, and "layer-cake" leverage (borrower/fund/sponsor) — i.e. the named "Bank→private-credit direct-lending exposure" channel. Severe scenario params: leveraged-loan spreads +390bp, VIX 40, FTSE −35%, "more severe than the financial crisis," built around an energy/supply-shock geopolitical premise (structurally adjacent to the live Hormuz thesis). **This is a stress *exercise*, not a stress *event*** — no phase advance; results are 12–18 months out (final 2027). Two reasons to log it: (1) **convergent regulator focus** — BoE + Fed (May FSR) + ECB (May FSR special feature) all independently flagged private credit, strengthening the structural Phase-3 record; (2) **interim findings land in the July 2026 FSR, which overlaps the late-July DTC×NDI×EOPL convergence window.**

**Source:** BoE publication (Tier 1, bankofengland.co.uk — direct fetch 403'd; multiple Tier 2 institutional/legal outlets citing the primary release: finance-monthly, Macfarlanes June 17, City AM); Fed May FSR + ECB May FSR (Tier 2 via Macfarlanes).

**Indicators:** NDI sub-index N5 (argument-rebuttal frequency — first named Tier 1/2 institution publishing bull and bear AI theses in a single analytical voice); NDI sub-index N3 (sell-side power-cost flag — *not* fired)

**Scenario impact:** **Level 1.** Goldman's head of institutional equities (Covello) stated June 2 that enterprise buyers, model companies, and hyperscalers still show no clear AI-spend returns, even as Goldman's own model lifts 2026 hyperscaler capex to ~$527B and projects $7.6T of cumulative AI spend through 2031 against a returns gap it characterizes as spending "outrunning returns." This deepens **N5** at the highest-tier source yet (previously confirmed at Tier 2–3 via Bloomberg/Fortune/Axios), but it is a *returns/economics* critique — **not the N3 power-cost flag** the NDI CRITICAL trigger requires. **NDI RED-not-CRITICAL holds;** CRITICAL still requires a Mag-7 guidance miss attributed specifically to input costs or power (Broadcom's 06-05 miss was a demand miss — wrong cause).

**Source:** Goldman Sachs podcast / institutional commentary, June 2, 2026 (Tier 2 — Goldman primary voice); Fortune, June 2026 (Tier 2). Secondary summaries (Tier 3) corroborate.

**Note:** The watch is for a Goldman (or peer) sell-side note explicitly attributing a Mag-7 *earnings* risk to power or input costs — that would fire N3 and trigger a Level 2 NDI move. Until then this is N5 reinforcement within the existing RED zone.

### Broadcom Q3 AI-chip guidance miss triggers tech-led selloff: AVGO −12.6%, SOX −5.2%, index ~−3%, VIX 15.4 → 21.5; Goldman flags decade-scale Mag-7 de-grossing (June 5)

**Scenario impact:** Advances the NDI within its existing RED zone; does **not** flip NDI to CRITICAL. But this is the first named Market Behavior event in which the AI narrative took visible public-market damage from a capex-to-revenue mismatch — exactly the overextension N2 was built to detect — and the Goldman de-grossing note advances the Stage 4 smart-money-exit signal from principal/aggregate evidence to institutional-risk-reduction-as-market-event. **Structural-vs-whiplash test: whiplash.** HY OAS moved only 2.74% → 2.76% (2bp) across the selloff; the brief's test (HY must widen alongside for a structural read) disqualifies this as Minsky/forced-deleveraging. Casualty salience (first confirmed mass casualties on Gulf soil in the June cluster) raises Scenario C/D pressure materially but does not cross an L4 line — the tree turns on *what was struck*, not *how bad it was*.

It also extends the C2-strike precedent (Bandar Abbas May 28, Sirik Island June 1) one node closer to the Strait; the threshold question warrants continued monitoring, as a follow-on strike on Hormuz navigation infrastructure would fire Level 4 immediately.

### Hezbollah independently rejects the Israel–Lebanon ceasefire (June 4); Araghchi reaffirms cross-front linkage — Lebanon↔Hormuz coupling confirmed (Level 3 addendum staged)

The June 1 Synthesis Reviewer pass staged a Three-Body addendum on the Lebanon↔Hormuz coupling "to be written only if the coupling confirms rather than reverses." June 3–4 confirms it: (1) Israel and Lebanon agreed a US-brokered conditional ceasefire June 3, contingent on Hezbollah withdrawing south of the Litani; (2) Hezbollah formally rejected the deal June 4 — leader Naim Kassem framing any withdrawal under fire as "surrender, defeat"; (3) Iranian FM Araghchi reaffirmed Lebanon sits inside the ceasefire envelope with the US, any violation "on one front… a violation across all fronts." The new geometry the three-body model (US/Iran/Israel) does not capture: Hezbollah acting as an *independent* veto-holder on the Lebanon front, not a dependent Iranian instrument — even if Tehran wished to decouple Lebanon from Hormuz talks, Hezbollah's autonomous rejection keeps the factual predicate for Iran's precondition alive. This is the L3 "new actor enters the three-body problem" trigger.

## 2026-06-01

### Japan JGB long-end at record highs: 40-yr 4.33%, 30-yr 3.93%, 10-yr 2.65–2.78%; Japanese institutions sold $29.6B USTs in Q1 2026 — largest quarterly reduction in four years; BOJ holds rates amid June hike debate

**Indicators:** Sovereign credit spread widening in high-debt G7 members (Japan) (named watch list indicator — the Japan long-end is the primary named global-debt sovereign signal; 40-yr JGB reached 4.33% on May 18, 2026, a record high since the 40-year maturity's 2007 debut and the first time any Japanese government maturity cleared 4% in more than 30 years; 30-yr JGB reached 3.93% as of June 1, 2026; 10-yr JGB reached 2.78–2.80% in mid-May, the highest since 1999, and has partially retreated to ~2.65% on June 1 amid BOJ policy uncertainty); 10-year Treasury yield (named watch list indicator — secondary cross-cutting: Japanese institutional investors sold $29.6B in US government-linked debt in Q1 2026, the largest quarterly reduction in nearly four years; March 2026 saw the largest monthly inflow on record into Japanese sovereign bond funds; a continued repatriation trend would sustain upward pressure on the US 10-yr, which sits at 4.45–4.50% per prices.csv — below the 4.75% WARN but sensitive to foreign-holder flows; the JGB long-end now yields enough for domestic institutions to earn competitive returns without absorbing USD currency risk)

**Sections:** Global Debt

**Scenario impact:** Confirms existing, advancing. The JGB long-end yield trajectory is the watch list's named Japan sovereign stress indicator. The 40-yr at 4.33% (record), 30-yr at 3.93% (multi-decade high), and 10-yr approaching 2.78% (highest since 1999) together constitute a structural steepening that is running well ahead of BOJ normalization pace — the BOJ short-term policy rate sits at 0.50%–0.75%, meaning the 40-yr / policy-rate spread exceeds 350bp. The analytical significance for the framework: the steepening is simultaneously (a) a fiscal-dominance signal for Japan (the world's highest debt-to-GDP sovereign at ~227% gross / ~110% net finds its refinancing costs rising structurally), (b) a global-debt contagion vector via institutional repatriation (Japanese investors are the largest single foreign holder of USTs at ~$1.1T; $29.6B Q1 reduction is directional, not yet disruptive at ~2.7% of the stock, but the stated preference shift — "new money won't go into US Treasuries" per BlueBay CIO — is a forward-flow signal), and (c) a carry-trade unwind risk (the USD/JPY carry at 0.50–0.75% borrow vs ~4.50% UST yield is being compressed; yen ~159.5/USD on May 29, approaching the 160 threshold that has historically triggered MOF intervention). BOJ is scheduled for its June 2026 meeting, and ING maintains expectations for a June rate hike (+25bp), which would compress the carry further and accelerate repatriation pressure. No Level 4 immediate trigger fires: the US 10-yr at 4.45–4.50% (prices.csv) remains below the 4.75% WARN line; the escalation-tree Level 4 trigger names the US 10-yr at 5.0%, not the JGB; no G7 sovereign rating action on Japan confirmed. BOJ April 28 meeting held rates steady while raising inflation forecasts, citing Iran-war energy price uncertainty — a hawkish hold that keeps the June hike probability elevated.

**Source:** Trading Economics / Japan MOF, Japan 40-Year Bond Yield, May 18, 2026 — tradingeconomics.com/japan/40-year-bond-yield (Tier 2 — confirms 4.33% on May 18, 2026); Trading Economics, Japan 30-Year Bond Yield, June 1, 2026 — tradingeconomics.com/japan/30-year-bond-yield (Tier 2 — confirms 3.93% on June 1, 2026); Nikkei Asia, "Japan long-term bond yields hit record highs amid fiscal concerns" — asia.nikkei.com (Tier 2 — confirms record-high framing and fiscal concern attribution); Fortune / Reuters, "The top foreign holders of US debt may soon dump Treasury bonds," May 17, 2026 — fortune.com/2026/05/17/us-debt-japan-investors-treasury-bonds-top-foreign-holders-repatriation-jgb-treasury-yields/ (Tier 2 — confirms $29.6B Q1 2026 UST sell-off, largest quarterly reduction in ~4 years, and March record JGB-fund inflow); Benzinga, "Japan Reduces US Treasury Holdings," May 2026 — benzinga.com/Opinion/26/05/52809886/japan-reduces-us-treasury-holdings (Tier 2 — confirms directional repatriation framing and BlueBay CIO quote); CNBC, "Bank of Japan keeps policy rate steady while raising inflation forecast on Iran war worries," April 28, 2026 — cnbc.com/2026/04/28/bank-of-japan-keeps-policy-rate-steady-cpi-iran-war-gdp.html (Tier 2 — confirms BOJ hawkish hold and energy-price uncertainty rationale); ING Think, "Japan's stronger-than-expected GDP supports June BoJ rate hike" — think.ing.com (Tier 2 — confirms June 2026 hike expectation and 50bp total 2026 hike forecast). Note: the BOJ June 2026 rate decision has not yet occurred as of this entry; the ING/market expectation is forward-looking. No Tier 1 BOJ statement on June 2026 action is yet available. The 40-yr yield level is confirmed across Tier 2 sources; the Tier 1 MOF auction results for May 20, 2026 (20-yr JGB) are available at mof.go.jp but specific bid-cover and tail figures were not confirmed via the search in this pass.

**Note:** The Japan JGB long-end trajectory is the watch list's most advanced named G7 sovereign stress signal. What this cluster of data changes in the framework: the repatriation channel identified in May 2026 market coverage is no longer speculative — $29.6B in Q1 confirmed flows document an active rotation already underway. The mechanism is now: JGB yields rise (BOJ normalization + fiscal deficit) → domestic institutions find home-market returns competitive without USD hedging cost → UST selling accelerates → US 10-yr yield sustains upward pressure. This is the cross-cutting linkage the watch list explicitly names under "10-year Treasury yield sustained above 4.75%." The US 10-yr is not yet at the WARN threshold (4.45–4.50% per prices.csv), but the structural demand-side pressure is building from a $1.1T holder now in active rotation mode. Flag: the BOJ June meeting (likely mid-June 2026) is a binary — a confirmed hike would accelerate both the yen repatriation dynamic and JGB long-end supply pressure, warranting a follow-on pass. The 40-yr / 30-yr JGB levels are at or near multi-decade records and represent a genuine fiscal-stress signal for a sovereign at 227% gross debt-to-GDP.

### UK 10-year gilt breached 5.0% (May 5–12); 30-year gilt reached 5.76% highest since 1998; Starmer political crisis drove fiscal-credibility repricing; yields partially recovered to ~4.85% / ~5.60% by end-May / June 1 after Spending Review relief

**Indicators:** Sovereign credit spread widening in high-debt G7 members (named watch list indicator — the UK is not explicitly named in the watch list's parenthetical list of "Japan, Italy, France, US" but is the highest-borrowing-cost G7 sovereign on 10-/20-/30-yr debt as of mid-May 2026; the move is structurally relevant as a G7 sovereign long-end stress signal); 10-year Treasury yield (cross-reference: the UK 10-yr gilt at 5.0–5.08% in early May is a G7 fiscal-stress analogue; while the watch list's Level 4 trigger specifies the US 10-yr, the UK 10-yr breaching 5.0% is a named-threshold analog for a G7 fiscal-credibility event; note that it does NOT fire the escalation-tree Level 4 trigger, which is US-specific); Brent crude trajectory (secondary: the March 2026 Bloomberg report explicitly quantified that the Iran war-driven gilt yield surge erased ~£3B of Reeves's £23.6B fiscal headroom — the oil shock is transmitting into UK sovereign borrowing costs through the inflation/rate-expectations channel)

**Sections:** Global Debt

**Scenario impact:** Confirms existing, with a new political-credibility dimension not previously logged. The UK gilt market experienced two distinct stress episodes within the 72-hour lookback window extended to ~30 days for fiscal/budget events: (1) May 5–12 political-crisis episode: 10-yr gilt reached 5.082% (highest since 2008) and 30-yr gilt reached 5.76% (highest since 1998) as 70+ Labour MPs called on PM Starmer to resign after local-election losses; the UK held the highest government borrowing costs in the G7 simultaneously on 10-, 20-, and 30-year debt above 5%. Citi noted potential for a "leftwards fiscal shift" under a Starmer successor (Rayner or Burnham), driving an explicit political-risk premium. (2) Late May / Spending Review relief: yields recovered to 10-yr ~4.85%, 30-yr ~5.60% by end-May (CNBC May 26) after Burnham, a potential successor, publicly attempted to placate bond markets; a Spending Review announcement (date confirmed via cityam.com search results) produced a gilt dip — 10-yr fell from 4.61% to 4.55% in the minutes following publication. Current level: 30-yr gilt at 5.60% as of June 1 (up 0.09pp from prior session per Trading Economics). The UK fiscal position: OBR March 2026 forecast headroom £23.6B (revised upward from November); Iran war yield surge erased ~£3B of that headroom via debt-service costs; 30-yr yield over 5% means one of the world's highest financing costs for a major sovereign on long-dated issuance; gross debt interest spending forecast at £98.5B–£109.7B for 2025-26. No Level 4 trigger fires: the escalation tree's immediate trigger specifies "10-year Treasury yield breaches 5.0%" — this is a US instrument; the UK 10-yr crossing 5.0% does not fire the Level 4 trigger. No UK sovereign rating downgrade by a major agency was found in the search window.

**Source:** CNBC, "UK borrowing costs surge to highest since 1998 as bond market braces for election fallout," May 5, 2026 — cnbc.com/2026/05/05/uk-local-election-bond-yields-borrowing-costs-uk10y-starmer-reeves.html (Tier 2 — confirms 10-yr gilt at 5.082%, highest since 2008, pre-election); CNBC, "'Starmer drama': UK borrowing costs hit post-2008 peak as leadership fears hit bond markets," May 12, 2026 — cnbc.com/2026/05/12/uk-gilts-borrowing-costs-keir-starmer-pressure-resign.html (Tier 2 — confirms 30-yr gilt at 5.76%, highest since 1998, and UK holding highest G7 borrowing costs on 10-/20-/30-yr debt simultaneously); Bloomberg, "UK Gilts Drop as Labour's Starmer Faces Calls to Resign After Election Losses," May 12, 2026 — bloomberg.com/news/articles/2026-05-12/gilts-slump-with-uk-prime-minister-under-pressure-to-stand-down (Tier 2 — Bloomberg confirms gilt slump and resignation pressure); CNBC, "UK's would-be PM tries to placate bond markets after sell-off," May 18, 2026 — cnbc.com/2026/05/18/burnham-gilts-inflation-starmer-interest-rates-bonds.html (Tier 2 — confirms Burnham market-placation attempt and partial yield recovery); CNBC, "UK gilt yields retreat from multi-decade highs as political drama mellows, rate hike expectations ease," May 26, 2026 — cnbc.com/2026/05/26/uk-gilt-yields-ease-political-drama-mellows-rate-hikes-ease.html (Tier 2 — confirms 10-yr at ~4.85% on May 26, "five-week lows"); City AM, "Spending Review: Gilt yields dip in relief for Rachel Reeves" — cityam.com/spending-review-gilt-yields-dip-in-relief-for-rachel-reeves/ (Tier 2 — confirms 10-yr fell 4.61%→4.55% at Spending Review publication); Bloomberg / OBR, "Rising Gilt Yields Push UK Borrowing Costs to Highest Since 2008," March 20, 2026 — bloomberg.com/news/articles/2026-03-20/reeves-to-lose-3-billion-of-fiscal-buffer-amid-gilts-selloff (Tier 2 — confirms £3B fiscal-headroom erosion from Iran-war yield surge); Trading Economics / DMO, UK 30-Year Bond Yield, June 1, 2026 — tradingeconomics.com/united-kingdom/30-year-bond-yield (Tier 2 — confirms 5.60% on June 1, up 0.09pp). Note: the Tier 1 Bank of England yield-curve daily data (bankofengland.co.uk/statistics/yield-curves) and DMO historical data were not directly fetched during this pass; the quantitative yield levels are drawn from Tier 2 sources consistent across Bloomberg, CNBC, and Trading Economics. No Tier 1 DMO auction-tail or OBR statement specifically covering June 2026 gilt stress was found; a DMO issuance calendar fetch would resolve this gap.

**Note:** The UK episode advances the watch list's "sovereign credit spread widening in high-debt G7 members" indicator in a way the framework had not previously logged for the UK specifically. The 2022 LDI/mini-Budget gilt crisis is the template: that episode was triggered by a Chancellor's credibility loss; this May 2026 episode was triggered by a PM's credibility loss — same mechanism (political fiscal-credibility shock → gilt long-end repricing), different political vector. The episode resolved without a policy reversal or Chancellor change; the Spending Review produced temporary relief. However, the UK 30-yr remains at 5.60% on June 1 — 160bp above the same maturity's 2024 level and above the 2022 LDI-crisis peak of ~5.1–5.2% on 30-year (some sources cite the September 2025 peak at 5.7%). The structural elevation matters for debt service: OBR gross debt interest at £98.5–109.7B in 2025-26 was computed at lower yield assumptions; £3B of headroom was already erased as of March 2026. The June 1 re-escalation of the Iran conflict (talks suspension + Sirik Island kinetics) is a direct upside risk to the UK gilt long-end through the inflation/rate-expectations channel — the oil shock that drove the March 2026 yield surge has not resolved and has now worsened. The UK is not named in the watch list's G7 sovereign list alongside Japan/Italy/France/US, but this episode documents it belongs in that monitoring set. Recommend the Synthesis Reviewer consider whether to add the UK explicitly to the named sovereigns in the "sovereign credit spread widening" indicator.

**Sections:** Global Debt, Market Behavior

**Scenario impact:** Confirms existing. Goldman Sachs BDC's −3.7% NAV and −$39.3M unrealized depreciation joins Investcorp Credit Management BDC (NAV per share $4.25 → $3.65), Kayne Anderson BDC (−$0.14/share unrealized loss), and APS BDC (−$21.0M net unrealized losses) in the Q1 2026 10-Q filing wave — the sharpest quarterly hit to BDC NAV since 2022 per ABF Journal analysis. What this adds to the framework: the May 22 entry established the Q1 sector-level net-outflow milestone via Bloomberg/Stanger (Tier 2); the Goldman Sachs BDC 10-Q (Tier 1, SEC EDGAR) now provides Tier 1 corroboration of the underlying NAV pressure driving those outflows, confirming that the redemption pressure is tracking deteriorating portfolio fundamentals, not merely sentiment. A Tier 1 filing from a Goldman Sachs-affiliated vehicle now confirms the markdown at the individual-fund level, tightening the evidentiary chain between portfolio stress and redemption pressure. The watch list's "Bank→private-credit direct-lending exposure" hook (a) remains unfired: the 10-Q does not document a bank-credit-line drawdown; GSBD's credit facility utilization is not the subject of the markdown.

### Consumer revolving-credit stress: Q1 2026 FRED DRCCLACBS confirmed 2.92% (Tier 1, updated May 19); smaller-bank rate 6.43%; NY Fed 90+ DPD stock rate 13.1% provenance gap resolved

**Indicators:** Consumer revolving-credit stress — NY Fed CCP credit-card 90+ DPD stock rate (named watch list indicator — the watch list carries a provenance caveat: "13.12% reached via secondary coverage of the Q1 2026 HHDC — NY Fed PDF returned 403, so Tier 1 in origin but NOT yet directly confirmed"; the NY Fed press release URL is now confirmed accessible at newyorkfed.org/newsevents/news/research/2026/20260512, resolving the provenance gap); FRED DRCCLACBS (named canonical Tier 1 series — Q1 2026 = 2.92%, updated May 19, 2026 per FRED release tables at fred.stlouisfed.org/release/tables?eid=148470&rid=231, consistent with the 2.92% figure in aggregates.csv and confirming the "falling from 3.2% 2024 peak" trajectory the watch list notes); FRED DRCCLOBS (smaller-bank card delinquency — 6.43% in Q1 2026, a new data point not previously logged: stress at smaller institutions is more than double the all-bank rate, advancing the distributional-stress framing)

**Sections:** Global Debt

**Scenario impact:** Confirms existing distributional framing; resolves provenance caveat. The Q1 2026 FRED delinquency release (updated May 19) confirms DRCCLACBS at 2.92% — flat versus the prior read in aggregates.csv, continuing the "falling from peak" trajectory. The 13.1% NY Fed CCP 90+ DPD stock rate is confirmed accessible via Tier 1 (NY Fed press release May 12), resolving the watch list's PDF-403 provenance caveat; the figure remains below the 13.7% 2010 peak threshold named as the watch list trigger. The new analytical detail is the DRCCLOBS (smaller banks) at 6.43% — more than double the 100-largest-bank rate, which is near 2.3–2.5% based on the DRCCLACBN series, confirming that the below-prime stress distribution is also a small-institution concentration. The ABA Banking Journal confirms household debt held at $18.8T and aggregate delinquency at 4.8% of outstanding debt — no systemic deterioration. The CNBC framing of the 90+ DPD stock rate as a "15-year high" is accurate (it is the highest since the GFC recovery) but does not change the analytical conclusion: the watch list threshold (13.7% 2010 peak crossing) remains unmet. The JPMorgan FY2026 charge-off guidance of 3.6–3.9% (vs. 3.47% Q1 actuals) — the second-order migration path to SLOOS tightening already noted in the watch list — remains the forward indicator.

**Source:** FRED, Delinquency Rate on Credit Card Loans, All Commercial Banks (DRCCLACBS), Q1 2026 release tables — fred.stlouisfed.org/release/tables?eid=148470&rid=231 (Tier 1 primary — FRED/Federal Reserve, updated May 19, 2026; confirms 2.92%); FRED, Delinquency Rate on Credit Card Loans, Banks Not Among the 100 Largest (DRCCLOBS) — fred.stlouisfed.org/series/DRCCLOBS (Tier 1 — confirms 6.43% Q1 2026 for smaller institutions); Federal Reserve Bank of New York, "Household Debt Balances Rise Slightly as Delinquency Transition Rates Hold Steady," May 12, 2026 — newyorkfed.org/newsevents/news/research/2026/20260512 (Tier 1 — confirms 13.1% 90+ DPD stock rate, $18.8T total household debt, 4.8% aggregate delinquency; resolves the NY Fed PDF-403 provenance caveat in the watch list); CNBC, "Credit card debt dips to $1.25 trillion — but maintains 'K-shaped' pattern, New York Fed research shows," May 12, 2026 — cnbc.com/2026/05/12/new-york-fed-credit-card-debt-stands-at-1point25-trillion.html (Tier 2 — confirms "K-shaped" distributional framing and "15-year high" characterization).

**Note:** The primary value of this entry is provenance resolution, not a new signal. The watch list's consumer-revolving-credit indicator was added May 29 with an explicit caveat that the 13.12%/13.1% NY Fed figure was "Tier 1 in origin but NOT yet directly confirmed" due to a PDF-403 response. The NY Fed press release URL is now confirmed accessible, removing the Tier 1 provenance uncertainty. The DRCCLOBS 6.43% smaller-bank rate is the only genuinely new data point: it documents that the distributional stress the watch list describes as "concentrated below-prime and at smaller issuers" has a named Tier 1 series that can be tracked, and the current 6.43% reading quantifies the institutional-concentration dimension of that stress. Recommend adding DRCCLOBS to the fetch_aggregates.py tracking infrastructure alongside the already-planned DRCCLACBS/CORCCACBS additions.

### Iran suspends US talks and threatens complete Hormuz closure plus Bab el-Mandeb activation; DTC axis C at day 11 of 14

**Indicators:** IRGC naval activity (named watch list indicator — escalation signal direction: Iran's suspension of "talks and exchange of texts through mediators" is explicitly framed around Lebanon as a violated ceasefire precondition; the Tasnim statement also places "complete blockade of the Strait of Hormuz and activation of other fronts including Bab el-Mandeb" on Iran's stated agenda as punitive measures — this advances the IRGC naval activity indicator from active-standoff to publicly stated intent to escalate); AIS mine clearance progress (named watch list indicator — escalation signal direction: the talks suspension forecloses any near-term mine-clearance corridor announcement; Ghalibaf explicitly stated Lebanon ceasefire compliance is a precondition for resumed talks, and that condition is not met; the de-escalation conditions "US CENTCOM announces verified safe corridor; commercial insurers re-enter market" move further from realization); Brent crude trajectory (named watch list indicator — Brent rebounded to ~$96.42 as of June 1 morning per Fortune/Reuters, reversing the May 29 $92.05 close; the deal-narrative decline that drove the -19% May drawdown partially reverses as the deal-proximity narrative collapses; WTI moved to ~$93, up ~5% from Friday close); DTC axis C (DTC composite — axis C clock stands at day 11 since the Khamenei "broad template" May 21–22; the talks suspension is not a substantive diplomatic advance; June 3 breach at day 14 is now 48 hours away; with the talks formally suspended rather than merely stalled, the breach is near-certain absent a same-day reversal)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict (primary), Global Debt (secondary — the deal-suspension reverses the oil-price path for June CPI; the May monthly -19% Brent decline was entirely deal-narrative; that narrative has now collapsed and Brent is rebounding; June CPI oil contribution reinstated as upside risk)

**Scenario impact:** The Iran talks suspension is the clearest structural break in the negotiating channel since the May 27 Shamkhani "fantasy" characterization, but is categorically more significant: it is a formal operational statement by Iran's chief negotiator (Ghalibaf) withdrawing from the document-exchange process itself, not a rhetorical characterization. The stated rationale — Lebanon ceasefire violation — directly links the Lebanon front (see Israeli incursion entry below) to the Hormuz resolution track: Iran has made Lebanese ceasefire compliance an explicit precondition, and Israel's Litani crossing provides the factual basis for that claim. The paired Tasnim threat — "complete blockade of Hormuz and activation of other fronts including Bab el-Mandeb" — is stated intent, not a confirmed kinetic action; it does not meet the Level 4 immediate trigger ("Strait of Hormuz physical infrastructure struck, mined, or declared formally closed by Iran under international law") as it is a Tasnim semi-official media statement and not a formal Iranian government declaration under international law. However, it materially changes the scenario framework: Scenario B ("managed naval standoff") has been operationally sustained since April 8 by the ceasefire envelope; the talks suspension and Bab el-Mandeb threat suggest Iran is evaluating a move to Scenario C/D escalation posture. The confounding-factors rule applies: the Tasnim statement could be a pressure tactic designed to force US action on Lebanon rather than a genuine operational order. Monitor for (a) a Khamenei or IRGC-level directive confirming the Bab el-Mandeb activation threat, (b) any Houthi/Ansar Allah naval activation in the Red Sea, or (c) any hardening of the Hormuz transit denial. If either (a) or (b) confirms within 48 hours, Level 4 convergence trigger assessment is warranted.

**Source:** CNN, "Live updates: Iran suspends talks with US over Israel's strikes on Lebanon, state media reports," June 1, 2026 — cnn.com/2026/06/01/world/live-news/iran-trump-lebanon-war-news (Tier 2 — CNN live blog; confirms Tasnim report and Ghalibaf statement); ABC News, "Iran live updates: Iran walks away from talks, Tasnim says," June 1, 2026 — abcnews.com/International/live-updates/iran-live-updates-irgc-claims-airbase-attack-after/?id=133475855 (Tier 2 — confirms Tasnim/Ghalibaf framing and Lebanon precondition language); CBS News, "Live Updates: Trump says 'it will all work out well' as new U.S. and Iranian strikes test ceasefire," June 1, 2026 — cbsnews.com/live-updates/iran-war-us-trump-strikes-ceasefire-lebanon-israel/ (Tier 2 — confirms Ghalibaf Lebanon precondition and Bab el-Mandeb threat); WION News, "Kuwait says air defences intercept missiles, drones as IRGC launches retaliatory strikes on US bases," June 1, 2026 — wionews.com (Tier 2 — confirms broader June 1 escalation cluster); Fortune, "Current price of oil as of June 1, 2026" — fortune.com/article/price-of-oil-06-01-2026/ (Tier 2 — confirms Brent $96.42 and WTI ~$93 at 8:30am ET June 1). Note: no Tier 1 Iranian MFA press release or IRGC operational order confirming the Bab el-Mandeb activation as an executed directive has been found; the Tasnim report is semi-official (Tier 2); the threat is logged as stated intent, not confirmed operation.

**Note:** The talks suspension changes the DTC analytical status in two ways. First, it makes the June 3 axis C breach effectively certain absent a same-day reversal — axis C measures days since the last substantive diplomatic movement, and a suspension of talks is the opposite of substantive movement. Second, and more structurally, the linkage Ghalibaf explicitly draws — Lebanon compliance as a precondition for resumed Hormuz talks — introduces a new coupling between the Lebanon front and the Hormuz resolution track that the framework had not previously named. The watch list's Armed Conflict indicator table names "Netanyahu coalition stability" (escalation signal: "coalition calls for Litani as permanent border; Lebanon ops intensify") as a watch-list indicator; Israel crossing the Litani and Netanyahu confirming permanent presence (see entry below) simultaneously activates that indicator and provides Iran with the factual predicate for the talks suspension. The two events are causally linked on June 1: the Lebanon incursion is the triggering condition Iran cited for suspending negotiations. This is a cross-cutting signal: the Netanyahu coalition stability watch-list indicator (Armed Conflict section) is now directly connected to the Hormuz resolution track through Iran's stated precondition. Flag for Synthesis Reviewer: recommend evaluating whether the Lebanon-Hormuz coupling constitutes a new geometry warranting a Level 3 addendum to the Three Body Problem or Three Blockade Problem analysis files.

### IRGC retaliatory strike on US air base following US strike on Sirik Island telecommunications tower; fresh US-Iran kinetic exchange June 1

**Indicators:** IRGC naval activity (named watch list indicator — escalation signal direction: the IRGC Aerospace Force destroyed the air base from which the US struck a telecommunications tower on Sirik Island in Hormozgan Province, directly adjacent to the Strait of Hormuz; IRGC warned "any subsequent attacks will trigger a response different in scale and nature" — a stated escalation ladder beyond the tit-for-tat exchange pattern); AIS mine clearance progress (named watch list indicator — escalation signal: kinetic exchange at Sirik Island, a strategic position near the strait entrance, directly in the mine-clearance operating corridor, makes any corridor announcement more remote)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict

**Scenario impact:** The Sirik Island exchange is the third distinct US-Iran kinetic event in five days (following the May 28 Bandar Abbas exchange). The geographic significance is notable: Sirik Island is in Hormozgan Province on the Iranian coast immediately flanking the Strait of Hormuz approach — the US struck a telecommunications/radar node there, which the IRGC interpreted as a strike on Hormuz-monitoring infrastructure and retaliated against the originating air base. NBC News confirmed the US struck "Iranian drone and radar command-and-control sites" in self-defense. The IRGC's warning about responses "different in scale and nature" follows its May 28 warning about "more decisive" responses — both warnings use escalatory language suggesting Iran is moving up its declared response threshold. The exchange is contained (no confirmed casualties, infrastructure damage limited) but the accumulation of three kinetic exchanges in five days is the pattern the May 22 watch-list note flagged as the condition under which Scenario C probability would rise. No Level 4 immediate trigger fires: Sirik Island is a telecommunications/radar site, not the Strait's physical infrastructure (mines/navigation aids/PGSA vessels); the exchange does not meet the "Hormuz physical infrastructure struck, mined, or declared formally closed" threshold.

**Source:** CGTN, IRGC statement on Sirik Island retaliation, June 1, 2026 — news.cgtn.com/news/2026-06-01/ (Tier 2 — CGTN citing IRGC public statement; confirms IRGC Aerospace Force strike on originating airbase); IranIntl, "IRGC says it struck base used in US attack on Sirik Island," June 1, 2026 — iranintl.com/en/202606019946 (Tier 2 — Iran International; independent confirmation of IRGC statement); Al Jazeera, "Iran's IRGC launches retaliatory strike after US attacks," June 1, 2026 — aljazeera.com/news/2026/6/1/ (Tier 2 — Al Jazeera wire; confirms exchange); NBC News, "U.S. and Iran trade strikes amid talks to end war," June 1, 2026 — nbcnews.com/world/middle-east/us-says-struck-iranian-drone-radar-sites (Tier 2 — NBC citing US official characterization of "drone and radar command-and-control sites"; confirms US self-defense framing). No Tier 1 CENTCOM press release confirming the Sirik Island strike parameters was found at entry filing time.

**Note:** The kinetic exchange sequence — Bandar Abbas May 28, Sirik Island June 1 — shows a geographic progression: the May 28 exchange was near Bandar Abbas Airport (an Iranian logistics hub); the June 1 exchange involves Sirik Island, a position directly adjacent to the Strait entrance and its monitoring infrastructure. The IRGC's escalating response language ("more decisive" on May 28, "different in scale and nature" on June 1) is a stated ladder that, if operationalized, would represent a qualitative shift in IRGC targeting doctrine from defensive-retaliatory to offensive-deterrent posture. This is a Level 1 entry; if a third kinetic exchange occurs within 48 hours at or near Hormuz physical infrastructure (mines, navigation aids, PGSA vessels, or the strait transit corridor itself), it would warrant immediate Synthesis Reviewer escalation assessment.

### Kuwait air defense intercepts hostile missiles and drones, June 1; civil aviation disrupted; IRGC context confirmed

**Indicators:** IRGC naval activity (named watch list indicator — escalation signal direction: Kuwait's military confirmed interception of "hostile" missiles and drones at 0300 GMT June 1; Kuwait's Foreign Ministry condemned "Iran's latest attacks" as "a dangerous escalation and direct assault on the security and stability of the State of Kuwait," providing the strongest official attribution available at this entry's filing time; the intercept occurs simultaneously with the Sirik Island IRGC exchange, suggesting a coordinated or sequenced Iranian strike package); Brent crude trajectory (named watch list indicator — Gulf energy-infrastructure proximity: Kuwait hosts the Mina al-Ahmadi refinery complex (~460,000 bpd production capacity) and is a GCC energy-infrastructure node; missile/drone interceptions near Kuwaiti energy facilities reinforce the oil supply risk premium)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict, Global Debt (secondary — Brent's June 1 rebound to $96.42 is compounded by physical Gulf-security risk from the Kuwait incident; if interceptions fail in future attacks and energy infrastructure is struck, the Brent trajectory reverses sharply upward)

**Scenario impact:** The June 1 Kuwait intercept is a distinct event from the April 2026 Iranian strikes on Kuwaiti oil facilities (already logged under those dates; not duplicated here). The June 1 event involves Kuwait's active air defense engagement, civil aviation disruption (holding patterns over Kuwait International Airport confirmed), and Kuwait's Foreign Ministry formal condemnation. The key sourcing uncertainty: Kuwait's military stated "hostile missiles and drones" were intercepted without identifying the launch point; Kuwait's Foreign Ministry attributed the attacks to Iran. The IRGC context (simultaneous Sirik Island retaliatory strike) is circumstantially consistent with Iranian origin. No confirmed damage to energy infrastructure was reported; the National (UAE) confirmed the military's characterization as interceptions with no confirmed casualties. The event advances the IRGC naval activity indicator (escalation direction) by extending kinetic activity into Kuwaiti airspace within the same operational window as the Sirik Island exchange. The accumulation of three simultaneous or same-day events (Iran talks suspension + Sirik Island kinetics + Kuwait intercept) on June 1 is the cross-sectional pattern the escalation tree names as a convergence candidate condition.

**Source:** The National (UAE), "Kuwait attacked by missiles and drones as US and Iran trade strikes in Gulf escalation," June 1, 2026 — thenationalnews.com/news/mena/2026/06/01/ (Tier 2 — The National is an Abu Dhabi-based Tier 2 regional wire; confirms Kuwaiti military statement and Foreign Ministry condemnation); ABC News, "Kuwait says its air defenses have opened fire to intercept drones and missiles," June 1, 2026 — abcnews.com/US/wireStory/kuwait-air-defenses-opened-fire-intercept-drones-missiles-133475100 (Tier 2 — ABC News wire; confirms intercept and 0300 GMT timing); Xinhua, "Kuwaiti army says air defences intercept missile, drone attacks," June 1, 2026 — english.news.cn/20260601/ (Tier 2 — Xinhua is state media but corroborates the military statement); Khaleej Times, "Kuwait army says air defences intercept 'hostile' missiles, drones," June 1, 2026 — khaleejtimes.com (Tier 2 — Gulf regional wire; confirms "hostile" language). Note: no Tier 1 Kuwaiti Ministry of Defense official press release with confirmed Iranian attribution was found at entry time; Kuwait's Foreign Ministry condemnation is the strongest government-level statement available (Tier 1 government source for the condemnation's existence, Tier 2 for the factual claim of Iranian origin). Pending Tier 1 CENTCOM or Kuwaiti MoD confirmation of launch origin.

**Note:** The Kuwait air defense intercept on June 1 differs analytically from the April 2026 strikes in one key respect: those strikes caused confirmed damage to the Mina al-Ahmadi refinery and Kuwait Petroleum headquarters; this intercept was successfully countered with no confirmed infrastructure damage. The distinction matters for the Brent trajectory indicator: the April strikes moved Brent because they produced actual production disruption; the June 1 intercept moves Brent because of proximity risk and deal-collapse narrative, not confirmed physical damage. The watch list's Level 4 trigger "Brent crude sustained above $130/bbl for 48+ hours" remains distant (current ~$96.42), but the risk premium re-expansion trajectory — from $92.05 on May 29 to $96.42 on June 1 morning — has a plausible escalation path if the Sirik Island/Kuwait cluster continues. The June 3 DTC axis C breach and the June 3–4 Armed Conflict counter-directional entry roll-off are now 48 hours away; the Armed Conflict section is no longer internally counter-directional as of June 1 (all entries in the rolling 7-day window from May 25 onward are escalation-direction with no de-escalation counterweight — the May 26–27 MOU/Brent-deescalation entries age out on June 2–3).
