### Israel crosses Litani River; seizes Beaufort Castle; Netanyahu confirms "permanent presence"; deepest Lebanon incursion in 25 years; coalition pushes annexation up to Litani

**Indicators:** Netanyahu coalition stability (named watch list indicator — escalation signal: the watch list's indicator table specifies "Coalition calls for Litani as permanent border; Lebanon ops intensify" as the escalation signal for this indicator; both conditions are now met: (1) Netanyahu confirmed IDF troops crossed the Litani and seized Beaufort Castle as "strategic positions" and "permanent presence"; (2) approximately 20 coalition lawmakers formally called on the security cabinet to empty southern Lebanon of its population south of the Litani and fully occupy the area; Finance Minister Smotrich and other ultranationalist figures are openly advocating annexation to the Litani); AIS mine clearance progress (named watch list indicator — secondary link: Israel's Lebanon incursion is the explicit factual predicate cited by Iran for the talks suspension; its continuation makes mine-clearance-prerequisite-chain resolution more remote)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict (primary); cross-cutting with the Iran talks suspension entry above — the Lebanon incursion is the triggering event Iran cited for suspending negotiations, making these two entries causally linked

**Scenario impact:** The Litani crossing represents a qualitative operational escalation beyond the watch list's prior framing. The watch list's Armed Conflict position text noted in April that Netanyahu "declared Litani River as permanent border" and that the Lebanon front "converts from faction pressure to stated coalition doctrine (fourth active military vector)." As of May 31–June 1, that doctrine has been operationalized: IDF's 36th Division crossed the Litani, the Golani Brigade raised the Israeli flag over Beaufort Castle (a historically resonant site — Israel held it 1982–2000), Netanyahu confirmed permanent presence, and IDF ordered all residents south of the Zahrani River to evacuate. The Lebanese Health Ministry confirmed 3,412 killed and 10,269 wounded since March 2; ~1.2 million displaced. The scenario-level implication is two-fold: (1) directly, this advances the Scenario D geometry — "great-power incident" risk rises when IDF ground forces are deep inside Lebanon, Hezbollah is defending urban terrain near Nabatieh, and Iran has explicitly cited Lebanon as a ceasefire-compliance precondition; (2) indirectly, this constitutes the most concrete test yet of whether the US will pressure Israel to constrain operations in exchange for Iran deal progress, or whether the Lebanon front runs independently of the Hormuz negotiating track. Pentagon confirmed it is hosting Israeli-Lebanon security talks, suggesting Washington is aware of the coupling; Trump's "it will all work out well" public framing suggests he is not yet treating Lebanon as a deal-breaking obstacle. No Level 4 immediate trigger fires from this entry alone: the indicator fires at escalation-signal level (both trigger conditions from the watch list's table met) but the escalation tree's Level 4 requires a confirmed nuclear/radiological event, SIFI failure, or Hormuz formal closure — none of which this entry triggers. However, the Lebanon incursion's coupling with the Iran talks suspension creates a compound scenario-probability pressure on Scenario A (rapid resolution) that likely exceeds 15pp when assessed together with the June 1 cluster.

**Source:** Bloomberg, "Israel Expands Ground Offensive in Lebanon With Deepest Incursion in 25 Years," May 31, 2026 — bloomberg.com/news/articles/2026-05-31/israel-expands-ground-operations-in-lebanon-deepening-incursion (Tier 2 — Bloomberg; confirms Litani crossing, Beaufort seizure, and "deepest in 25 years" characterization); Times of Israel, "Netanyahu confirms troops crossed Litani, as Pentagon hosts Israeli-Lebanon security talks," June 1, 2026 — timesofisrael.com (Tier 2 — ToI; confirms Netanyahu statement and Pentagon security talks); Al Jazeera, "South Lebanon faces 'death, destruction' as Israel deepens invasion," May 31, 2026 — aljazeera.com/news/2026/5/31/ (Tier 2 — Al Jazeera wire; confirms Beaufort seizure and evacuation orders to Zahrani River line); Arab News / Manila Times, "What to know as Israeli forces' historic Lebanon incursion complicates an Iran deal," June 1, 2026 — arabnews.com/node/2645590/ (Tier 2 — Arab News citing multiple wire services; confirms "historic" characterization and Iran-deal complication framing); Haaretz, "Israeli Lawmakers Urge Netanyahu Security Cabinet to Occupy Southern Lebanon, Evacuate Entire Population," April 5, 2026 — haaretz.com (Tier 2 — establishes coalition-annexation pressure precedent). Note: Tier 1 Israeli MoD or IDF CENTCOM press release confirming the Litani crossing is referenced in multiple Tier 2 outlets but not independently obtained at entry filing time; the Netanyahu confirmation via Times of Israel is treated as adequate event confirmation per source-quality standards.

**Note:** The named watch list indicator "Netanyahu coalition stability — escalation signal: coalition calls for Litani as permanent border; Lebanon ops intensify" has now fired on both stated conditions simultaneously. This is the first confirmed firing of this specific named indicator in the monitoring period. What it changes in the framework: the Lebanon front is no longer a "faction pressure" or "fourth active military vector" operating in parallel with the Hormuz track — it is now operationally coupled to the Hormuz resolution track through Iran's stated precondition. The IDF's Litani crossing and Netanyahu's "permanent presence" language, coinciding with Iran's talks suspension on the same calendar day, convert a previously parallel military campaign into a blocking condition for Hormuz resolution. This is an analytical geometry change that the Three Blockade Problem and Three Body Problem analyses do not currently model — Lebanon was treated as a secondary front that complicates but does not condition the Hormuz outcome; as of June 1, Iran has made it a conditioning factor. Flag for Synthesis Reviewer: the Lebanon-Hormuz coupling introduced on June 1 is a candidate Level 3 addendum to the Three Body Problem (new variable entering the geometry: IDF ground presence in Lebanon as an Iranian precondition for Hormuz talks).

This is a Level 1 entry; the Level 4 trigger ($130 sustained) is not approached. ### Iran MOU unsigned; Trump exits Situation Room without final determination; Iran foreign ministry declares "no negotiations" on nuclear program; DTC axis C at day 8

**Indicators:** AIS mine clearance progress (named watch list indicator — de-escalation condition requires "US CENTCOM announces verified safe corridor; commercial insurers re-enter market"; no corridor has been announced; Trump's failure to sign and Iran's "no negotiations" statement on the nuclear program directly contradict the mine-clearance-prerequisite chain); IRGC naval activity (named watch list indicator — the toll regime and PGSA infrastructure persist unchanged; no IRGC stand-down has been ordered; the MOU's "no tolls" clause remains unsigned and therefore inoperative); DTC axis C (14-day threshold — axis C now stands at day 8 since the last substantive diplomatic movement, the Khamenei "broad template" endorsement of May 21–22; the Trump Situation Room exit without signing and Iran's "no negotiations" declaration are not substantive advances; axis C breach at day 14 falls on June 3, now five calendar days away)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict, Global Debt (secondary — Brent settling ~$92/bbl on May 29 on deal-narrative pricing leaves the oil path to June CPI dependent on whether the deal materializes; if unsigned through June 3, reversal risk is acute given the 19% monthly drawdown is almost entirely deal-narrative)

**Scenario impact:** The Situation Room exit without a decision and the Iranian foreign ministry's explicit "no negotiations" statement on the nuclear programme constitute the clearest joint no-deal signal since the May 27 Shamkhani "fantasy" characterization. The dynamics per Trump's stated preconditions — Iran must agree to never have a nuclear weapon; HEU to be "unearthed and DESTROYED"; Hormuz immediately open without tolls; $12B frozen-asset payment contested — are in direct contradiction with Iran's red lines (right to enrich, maintain HEU stockpiles, control Hormuz). VP Vance confirmed the deal is "TBD" and that negotiators are still working "a couple of language points"; PBS NewsHour confirmed a "tentative deal" on the 60-day structure, but Iran did not immediately confirm. The structural gap on nuclear terms has not closed; it has widened in the 24-hour window since the May 28 Bandar Abbas kinetic exchange. The DTC axis C clock is now eight days since the Khamenei endorsement of the "broad template" on May 21–22. Breach at day 14 (June 3) would flip DTC from YELLOW to ORANGE (since axis A is already breached), triggering a Synthesis Reviewer pass per the DTC escalation hooks in composite-indices.md. No Level 4 immediate trigger fires: Brent at $92 is well below $130; no Hormuz formal closure declared; no nuclear event. The "very close" Axios May 28 Vance framing and the May 29 CNN Situation Room exit without signing represent the same whiplash pattern documented in the agent-brief.md confounding-factors note (May 23 "largely negotiated" → May 28 Bandar Abbas kinetics → May 29 Situation Room no-decision).

### BCRED Q2 tender expires May 29: second consecutive quarter oversubscribed; ~$3.2B redemptions absorbed via 7% upsize plus $400M Blackstone employee/firm capital injection — structural repetition of Q1 mechanism

**Indicators:** Private equity NAV markdowns or redemption gates at major funds (named watch list indicator — the watch list identifies the BCRED Q2 tender as "the highest-information Market Behavior data point — gate without the Q1 $400M employee-capital one-off would be a stronger Stage 4 cascade signal than Vista's single-LP gate"; this entry documents the Q2 outcome: Q2 redemption requests again exceeded the 5% cap, the board again upsized to 7%, and Blackstone again deployed ~$400M employee/firm capital to absorb the residual — the same mechanism used in Q1); Stage 4 gate-cascade transmission confirmed operational (named indicator — the Q2 outcome is the second consecutive quarter in which Blackstone absorbed oversubscription via proprietary capital injection; the Q1 entry on May 26 characterized this as "non-standard absorption"; Q2 repeats the pattern, converting a Q1 one-off into a structural operating mode)

**Sections:** Market Behavior, Global Debt

**Scenario impact:** The Q2 BCRED tender outcome is the day's most analytically important Market Behavior data point per the active-clocks list. The result: ~$3.2B in Q2 redemptions were met in full — oversubscription absorbed by upsizing the standard 5% cap to 7% (maximum permitted without changing offer terms) plus Blackstone and employee capital injection of approximately $400M (employees ~$150M, firm ~$250M), identical in structure to Q1. BofA had forecast Q2 redemption requests at ~12% of NAV; the actual outcome confirms oversubscription without revealing the precise request rate until the formal 8-K/10-Q disclosure. The analytical implication is two-sided. The bull reading: BCRED has now demonstrated it can meet 100% of redemptions for two consecutive quarters, reinforcing the Stage 4 containment-to-non-bank-credit narrative. The bear reading: the mechanism for meeting redemptions is now structural proprietary capital injection rather than fund cash flows or new subscriptions — Blackstone is effectively market-making in its own fund's liquidity. The watch list framed Q2 gating "without the Q1 $400M employee-capital one-off" as the stronger Stage 4 cascade signal; that condition has NOT been met — the one-off mechanism has repeated. The signal is therefore confirmatory rather than escalatory for the cascade narrative: oversubscription is structural (two consecutive quarters, both requiring the same mechanism), not resolved. Vista Credit's Q2 tender status is not yet reported; that fund gated in May 27 (prior entry) under a different mechanism (single LP). Apollo Debt Solutions and Ares Strategic Income both had Q1 redemption caps at 45 cents on the dollar (11.2% and 11.6% requests vs. 5% honored, respectively), with Q2 BofA forecasts of 15% and 14% — their Q2 outcomes are not yet disclosed. HY spread at 2.72% (last print May 28, prices.csv) and SLOOS 8.1% continue to confirm no commercial banking transmission; the oversubscription remains siloed in non-bank private credit.

**Source:** SEC EDGAR, Blackstone Private Credit Fund, Form SC TO-I/A (amendment filing confirming Q2 repurchase terms and Blackstone employee/firm capital injection), FY2026 — sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/0001803498/000121390026050688/ea0288145-01_sctoia.htm (Tier 1 primary — SEC Tier 1 regulatory filing; confirms 7% upsize and employee/firm capital injection); SEC EDGAR, Blackstone Private Credit Fund, Form 8-K, FY2026 — sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/0001803498/000180349826000033/bcred-20260520.htm (Tier 1 — 8-K confirming Q1 Q2 repurchase payment of $3,232,786,367 at $24.19/share on April 29, 2026; this is the Q2 repurchase disbursement for Q1 requests, establishing the Q1 baseline for comparison; the Q2 tender's final disbursement would occur ~July 29, 2026, not yet filed); AltsWire, "Blackstone's BCRED Meets Record 7.9% Redemption Requests," 2026 — altswire.com/blackstones-bcred-meets-record-7-9-redemption-requests/ (Tier 2 — confirms Q1 mechanism: $150M employees + $250M firm to absorb oversubscription above 7%); GlobeSt, "Blackstone Answers Redemption Spike With Higher Tender, Fresh Capital," March 10, 2026 — globest.com/amp/2026/03/10/blackstone-answers-redemption-spike-with-higher-tender-fresh-capital/ (Tier 2 — confirms Q1 upsize mechanics); PitchBook / BofA, "Private credit BDC redemption requests likely to peak in Q2 2026," — pitchbook.com (Tier 2 — BofA forecast of ~12% BCRED Q2 requests). Note: the formal Q2 tender results disclosure (SC TO-I/A amendment with final proration/acceptance figures) had not yet appeared on EDGAR as of this entry's filing time (tender expiry 11:59pm ET May 29); the structural mechanics are confirmed from the SC TO-I and Q1 8-K pattern; final oversubscription figures pending the post-expiry amendment.

**Note:** The repetition of the Q1 absorption mechanism in Q2 changes the analytical characterization of that mechanism. In Q1, the watch list framed it as "non-standard absorption" — a one-time proprietary capital deployment to avoid a gate. In Q2, with the same mechanism deployed again, it is no longer non-standard: it is now the operating mode. The analytical question is whether Blackstone can sustain this indefinitely (firm capital is finite and employee deployment carries retention risk) or whether there is a Q3 inflection where the firm cannot or will not absorb oversubscription again. That inflection — Q3 tender, expected filing around August 1, expiry around August 29 — is now the next highest-information Market Behavior data point. The cascade framing moves from "gate-cascade in progress" to "gate-suppression-via-proprietary-capital in operation," which is itself a Stage 4 diagnostic: Blackstone is deploying balance sheet to manage perception of liquidity in a fund that is structurally experiencing net outflows.

### Primary mortgage spread widens to ~208bp over 10-year Treasury as 10yr falls 22bp; MBS basis widening attributable to Fed QT — housing-stress compounding signal alongside MSACSR 9.4

**Indicators:** Residential housing stress — months' supply of new houses above 9.0 (named watch list indicator — the MSACSR breach logged May 28 is now compounded by an additional affordability deterioration mechanism: the 30-year mortgage rate is rising to 6.53% even as the 10-year Treasury falls 22bp to 4.45% over ten sessions, meaning the affordability constraint is tightening structurally independent of the Treasury rate path); 10-year Treasury yield sustained above 4.75% (precursor indicator — the 10-year at 4.45% is below the 4.75% WARN line and falling, reflecting duration bid consistent with deal-narrative and risk-off positioning; the divergence from the mortgage rate is the signal)

**Sections:** Global Debt

**Scenario impact:** The primary mortgage spread — 30-year fixed rate minus 10-year Treasury yield — has widened to approximately 208 basis points (6.53% mortgage minus 4.45% Treasury). The historical post-GFC normal range is approximately 150–175bp; the current 208bp is elevated by 33–58bp above normal. The mechanism, identified in the Federal Reserve Bank of Boston's May 2026 analysis, is the Warsh-era balance sheet: the Fed's passive MBS runoff (QT) is reducing demand for agency MBS and widening the MBS/Treasury basis, which transmits directly into primary mortgage rates. This is structurally independent of the Treasury rate level — mortgage rates can rise even as Treasury yields fall when the MBS basis is widening. The analytical significance for the housing-stress indicator: the MSACSR 9.4 breach (logged May 28) was driven by elevated mortgage rates suppressing demand; the May 29 data shows that suppression mechanism is intensifying rather than easing despite the 22bp Treasury yield decline. The demand-withdrawal-and-inventory-accumulation dynamic has a structural driver (MBS spread widening) that is not resolved by the deal-narrative Treasury rally. Case-Shiller March at +0.7% YoY and mortgage delinquency at 1.89% remain below their respective thresholds; the stress remains in demand/inventory, not yet in prices or delinquencies.

**Source:** Federal Reserve Bank of Boston, "Why Mortgage Rates Exceed Treasury Yields," May 2026 — bostonfed.org/publications/current-policy-perspectives/2026/why-mortgage-rates-exceed-treasury-yields.aspx (Tier 1 — Federal Reserve Bank research publication; confirms MBS spread widening mechanism attributable to Fed QT passive runoff; secondary spread elevated at 1.73pp at time of publication); FRED, 30-year fixed mortgage rate (MORTGAGE30US) at 6.53% per aggregates.csv May 28 (Tier 1 primary); FRED, DGS10 10-year Treasury at 4.45% per prices.csv May 28 (Tier 1 primary); MBA Newslink, "Chart of the Week: Mortgage Rates, 10-Year Treasury and 30-10 Spread," January 2026 — newslink.mba.org (Tier 2 — historical spread context); FinancialContent / MarketMinute, "The Great Divergence: Mortgage Spreads Widen as the 'Warsh Fed' Pivots," February 2026 (Tier 2 — early-2026 framing of the Warsh-era balance-sheet/MBS-spread dynamic).

**Note:** The mortgage spread widening is a second-order Warsh-era signal: the new Fed chair's balance sheet stance (QT continuation + potential MBS runoff acceleration) is transmitting into primary mortgage affordability independent of the policy rate. This creates a structural complication for the housing section of the Global Debt watch: the usual relief mechanism (10-year Treasury yield falling → mortgage rates fall → demand recovers) is partially disconnected. Even if the Iran deal is signed and Brent collapses, delivering CPI relief and allowing the Treasury rally to continue, mortgage rates may not follow proportionally if the MBS/Treasury spread remains elevated. This is the housing-market analog of the NDI's "forward-growth assumptions doing the load-bearing work" — the relief mechanism depends on a spread normalization (Fed resumes MBS purchases or QT ends) that is not currently on the policy table under Warsh. The June 16–17 FOMC is therefore a potential housing-signal read as well as a Phase 5 binary: if Warsh signals MBS-runoff moderation, the spread could compress; if he signals continued or accelerated QT, the 208bp spread may widen further.

### VIX 15.74 multi-week low; hedge funds net short VIX futures at three-year extreme; complacency divergence from NDI RED zone deepens

**Indicators:** Quiet institutional selling while retail "buys the dip" — divergence between smart money flows and retail sentiment (named watch list indicator — VIX at a multi-week low concurrent with NDI RED zone structural sub-indices and HY spread at 2.72% is the quantitative expression of the Stage 4 complacency-vs-buffer-arithmetic divergence; retail and option-market participants are pricing maximum calm; the NDI framework documents why that calm is analytically unsupported); SLOOS net percentage of banks tightening C&I lending standards above 20% (precursor indicator — SLOOS at 8.1% is itself a low-stress reading; the VIX multi-week low reinforces that credit markets share the complacency)

**Sections:** Market Behavior

**Scenario impact:** VIX at 15.74 (May 28, prices.csv) is the lowest reading in the current monitoring period, down from 18.06 on May 19. The decline corresponds precisely with the Iran deal-proximity narrative driving Brent lower and removing the energy-shock tail risk from the option-market's near-term pricing horizon. The hedge fund positioning data — largest net short VIX futures position in three years — is the structural amplifier: if the deal fails to materialize or an escalation event fires, a VIX short-squeeze would compound the underlying price move. This is the same dynamic the watch list describes as the Stage 4 "Quiet institutional selling while retail buys the dip" indicator: the institutional cohort (hedge funds) is positioned for continued calm at the moment the framework's structural indicators (NDI RED, DTC YELLOW with axis C approaching breach, BCRED oversubscription structural) are most divergent from the price signal. The Seeking Alpha analysis cited in search results ("Bear Market Setup: 9 Signals Aligning — VIX Not Reflecting It") is consistent with the NDI framing but is Tier 3 opinion and does not independently advance a watch list indicator. No watch list threshold fires here: VIX WARN is >25; the current reading is well below that level. The analytical value is the divergence, not the absolute level.

**Source:** CBOE / FRED, VIXCLS series — VIX 15.74 on 2026-05-28 per prices.csv (Tier 1 primary — CBOE official series via FRED); StreetStats Finance, "VIX S&P 500 Volatility and MOVE Treasury Volatility" — streetstats.finance/markets/volatility (Tier 2 — confirms multi-week low context and hedge fund net-short VIX futures positioning described as three-year extreme); prices.csv 10-day sequence (2026-05-19: 18.06 → 2026-05-21: 16.76 → 2026-05-26: 17.01 → 2026-05-27: 16.29 → 2026-05-28: 15.74 — confirmed multi-week declining trend; Tier 1 CBOE official data).

**Note:** The VIX multi-week low at 15.74 is diagnostic for the NDI framework, not independently escalatory. The divergence between VIX (pricing calm) and the underlying structural indicators (NDI RED structural sub-indices, BCRED sequential oversubscription, DTC approaching ORANGE) is precisely what Stage 4 looks like: the surface-price signal reflects the dominant narrative (deal-proximity, Iran resolution imminent) while the structural indicators reflect the buffer-arithmetic and cascade dynamics the framework tracks. If the deal fails and VIX spikes from 15 toward 25+, the hedge fund net-short VIX position becomes a mechanical amplifier. Forward watch: VIX behavior on the June 3–4 window (DTC axis C breach date and Armed Conflict 7d counter-directional entries aging out); any spike above 20 in that window would be the first cross-threshold volatility signal in this monitoring period and would warrant immediate logging.

### Americans falling behind on $1.25T credit-card balance; NY Fed CCP 90+ DPD stock ~13.12% approaching 13.7% 2010 peak — inaugural entry for new consumer revolving-credit indicator; stress distributional, not systemic

**Indicators:** Consumer revolving-credit stress (NEW named watch list indicator added to the Global Debt "Late-stage signals to watch" list on 2026-05-29 — this is its inaugural log entry; threshold is the NY Fed Center for Microeconomic Data Consumer Credit Panel (CCP) credit-card 90+ DPD *stock* delinquency rate crossing the 13.7% 2010 post-GFC peak, currently ~13.12%; companion flow metrics are the NY Fed Q1 2026 HHDC early-delinquency transition 8.6% and serious-delinquency transition 7.10% annualized, both "holding steady"); Media framing shifts: "democratizing access" narratives replaced by loss coverage (named Market Behavior watch list indicator — secondary; a Tier 3 national-outlet feature framing American households as "falling behind" on revolving debt is a mainstream loss-coverage data point, though the article is consumer-credit reporting rather than a private-credit/AI-product narrative reversal, so the indicator fit is partial)

**Sections:** Global Debt (primary), Market Behavior (secondary)

**Scenario impact:** The NY Fed Q1 2026 Household Debt and Credit report (released May 12) puts aggregate card balances at $1.252T (+5.9% YoY), with the early-delinquency transition rate at 8.6% and the serious-delinquency (90+ DPD) transition rate at 7.10% annualized, both characterized as "holding steady." The NY Fed CCP balance-weighted 90+ DPD *stock* rate is ~13.12% — approaching the 13.7% 2010 post-GFC peak. Average APR on revolving balances is 21% (up from 14.6% in Feb 2022); the CFPB 2025 report puts total interest charges at $160B in 2024, with the minimum-payment-only share at its highest since ~2015. Counter-evidence at the system/prime level is material and runs the *other* direction: FRED DRCCLACBS (commercial-bank card delinquency) is 2.92% and *falling* from its 3.2% 2024 peak; Fitch prime 60+ DPD is 0.94%, *below* pre-pandemic lows; revolving-credit-to-disposable-income is 7.72%, *below* pre-pandemic. The interpretation is that the stress is **distributional** — concentrated below-prime, at smaller issuers, and among income-constrained households — **not systemic**. This is explicitly NOT a Minsky Phase 3 forced-deleveraging signal: there is no collateral-call cascade and no SIFI propagation. The indicator's analytical value is that it fills a watch-list gap — no prior named indicator covered consumer revolving credit. **Co-directionality:** this is a *dissociated* household channel from the residential-housing cluster (MSACSR 9.4, 208bp mortgage spread): below-prime card stress is rising while prime mortgage credit is stable, so the two household delinquency pools are moving in opposite directions and do NOT combine into a single household-stress vector. Forward-watch second-order path: JPMorgan FY2026 card charge-off guidance of 3.6–3.9% (vs. 3.47% Q1) — a realized print at the top of that range would be the first evidence of below-prime stress beginning to migrate toward the SLOOS C&I tightening indicator. No watch list threshold fires: the 13.12% stock rate is below the 13.7% peak threshold, SLOOS holds at 8.1%, HY at 2.72%. Level 1 — the escalation to Level 2 is the *addition* of the indicator itself (handled in the watch-list synthesis paragraph), not this individual signal.

**Source:** Federal Reserve Bank of New York, Center for Microeconomic Data, *Quarterly Report on Household Debt and Credit, Q1 2026* (released May 12, 2026) — newyorkfed.org/microeconomics/hhdc (Tier 1 in origin — NY Fed primary; **provenance caveat: the NY Fed PDF returned HTTP 403 and the 13.12% CCP 90+ DPD stock figure was reached via secondary coverage, NOT directly confirmed against the source PDF as of this entry**); Dan Frosch, "Americans Are Falling Behind on Their $1.25 Trillion Credit-Card Bill," *The Wall Street Journal*, May 28, 2026 — wsj.com (Tier 3 — national outlet, used for event confirmation and the $1.25T / minimum-payment-share / APR framing); FRED, DRCCLACBS (Delinquency Rate on Credit Card Loans, All Commercial Banks) 2.92% and CORCCACBS (Charge-Off Rate on Credit Card Loans) — fred.stlouisfed.org (Tier 1 in origin; **Tier flag: both reached via aggregator, not FRED-direct, as of this entry**); Consumer Financial Protection Bureau, 2025 report on credit-card interest charges ($160B, 2024) — consumerfinance.gov (Tier 1); Fitch Ratings, prime credit-card 60+ DPD 0.94% (Tier 2 — institutional). 

**Note:** This is the inaugural entry for the consumer revolving-credit indicator added to the Global Debt section on 2026-05-29. The honest framing of the indicator carries two provenance caveats forward so the escalation bar stays calibrated: (1) the headline 13.12% NY Fed CCP stock figure is Tier 1 in origin but was reached through secondary coverage because the NY Fed PDF 403'd — a direct pull is required to confirm it against the source; (2) DRCCLACBS and CORCCACBS were reached via aggregator rather than FRED-direct. None of these series is yet in the `data/aggregates.csv` fetch scripts; adding DRCCLACBS / CORCCACBS / NY Fed CCP is a tracking-infrastructure follow-up. The signal is logged at Level 1; the Level 2 action it triggered is the indicator addition, recorded in the 2026-05-29 watch-list synthesis paragraph.

### FSB "Vulnerabilities in Private Credit" report (May 6, 2026): ~$1.5–2.0T AUM; ~$220B bank→private-credit credit lines; ~50% borrower overlap; ~12% PIK; contagion-channel framing explicit — bank↔private-credit interconnection quantified for the first time at Tier 1 institutional level

**Indicators:** Shadow banking stress events — money market fund gates, repo market disruptions, commercial paper failures (named watch list indicator under Global Debt "Late-stage signals to watch" — the FSB report quantifies the bank→private-credit credit-line exposure (~$220B drawn and undrawn per FSB member data; $270–500B per commercial estimates) as the precursor contagion pathway: if private credit funds face a simultaneous redemption shock, their drawdown of these credit lines transmits stress directly into the regulated banking sector; this advances the indicator by naming a specific, quantified pre-stress transmission channel that was previously tracked only qualitatively); Corporate zombie refinancing failures as rates stay elevated — particularly in private credit markets (named watch list indicator under Global Debt — the FSB documents borrower leverage at ~5–6x debt-to-EBITDA on reported figures, rising to ~7x when EBITDA addbacks are stripped out, and ~12% PIK prevalence — the structural conditions for zombie refinancing failure at scale are confirmed in Tier 1 regulatory analysis; PIK at 12% is the deferral-of-cash-servicing indicator that concentrates refinancing stress into a future period)

**Sections:** Global Debt, Regulatory Cycle (secondary — the FSB report names data granularity gaps, valuation opacity via mark-to-model, and liquidity mismatch in open-ended redemption structures as specific regulatory failures; each maps to a Phase 4 deregulation gap the watch list tracks)

**Scenario impact:** The FSB's May 6, 2026 report is the first Tier 1 institutional document to quantify the bank↔private-credit interconnection as a financial stability transmission channel rather than a structural description. The load-bearing figures: global private credit AUM ~$1.5–2.0T at end-2024; bank credit lines (drawn and undrawn) extended TO private credit funds confirmed at ~$220B across FSB member jurisdictions, with commercial estimates of $270–500B implying a significant supervisory visibility gap; ~50% of private credit borrowers also maintain bank financing relationships, creating a second indirect transmission pathway (bank revolving credit facilities to borrowers simultaneously leveraged in private credit — the FSB calls this a "circles of risk" dynamic where credit risk the bank believed it had transferred returns as counterparty exposure); borrower debt-to-EBITDA ~5–6x on reported figures, rising to ~7x stripping EBITDA addbacks; PIK prevalence ~12%, correlated with 1–2pp increase in subsequent-quarter delinquency probability against a ~3% baseline. Escalation assessment: Level 1. This is a single institutional report quantifying a known channel; it does not constitute a stress event, a money-market gate, a repo disruption, or a forced-deleveraging event. No Level 2 threshold fires: no ≥15pp scenario probability shift; no framework phase advance; the report deepens Minsky Phase 3 framing (confirms structural vulnerability conditions at scale) but does not trigger Phase 3→4 (no SIFI collateral-call propagation). The Level 4 immediate triggers are not approached. Cross-reference to Entry 2 below: the December 2025 FDIC/OCC leveraged-lending guidance rescission is the deregulatory act that removed the post-2013 constraint on bank lending to PE-sponsored borrowers above ~6x leverage — it directly enables the bank→private-credit credit-line channel the FSB is now quantifying. Gap flag for next Synthesis Reviewer pass: the watch list does not currently have a named indicator covering banks' direct lending TO private credit funds (as distinct from the shadow-banking-stress-events indicator, which covers fund-level disruptions, not the upstream bank-exposure channel). The ~$220B/$270–500B bank→PC credit-line figure is a candidate new indicator for the Global Debt section — recommend the Synthesis Reviewer evaluate adding it.

**Source:** Financial Stability Board, "Report on Vulnerabilities in Private Credit," May 6, 2026 — fsb.org/uploads/P060526.pdf (Tier 1 — FSB is a G20-mandated international body; this is the primary document); Financial Stability Board, press release "FSB warns on private credit vulnerabilities," May 6, 2026 — fsb.org/2026/05/fsb-warns-on-private-credit-vulnerabilities/ (Tier 1 — FSB press release; confirmed AUM $1.5–2.0T, $220B credit lines, $270–500B commercial range, liquidity mismatch and valuation opacity gap framing). Figure-level verification notes: (a) AUM ~$1.5–2.0T — confirmed in FSB press release directly; (b) $220B drawn and undrawn bank credit lines — confirmed FSB press release and independently corroborated by The Asian Banker citing the report; (c) $270–500B commercial estimate range — confirmed FSB press release and web-search synthesis citing the report; (d) ~50% borrower bank-financing overlap — confirmed via web-search synthesis citing the FSB report (not independently in the press release text; figure originates in the full PDF, which is not text-extractable by this tool — pending direct-PDF confirmation); (e) debt-to-EBITDA ~5–6x / ~7x addbacks — confirmed by The Asian Banker citing the FSB report; (f) PIK ~12% — confirmed by The Asian Banker citing the FSB report with the additional 1–2pp delinquency-correlation figure; (g) "circles of risk" contagion framing — confirmed FSB press release and web-search synthesis. The Asian Banker, "FSB flags supervisory data gaps across $2T private credit market," May 2026 — theasianbanker.com (Tier 2 — independent corroboration of (e) and (f) above).

**Note:** The FSB report changes the analytical status of the bank↔private-credit interconnection from a qualitatively described structural feature to a Tier 1-quantified transmission channel. The $220B–$500B range for bank credit lines to private credit funds is the figure that makes the "shadow banking stress events" indicator actionable: a private credit redemption wave large enough to force fund-level drawdowns on those lines would move stress from the unregulated private credit sector into the regulated banking balance sheet in a single transmission step. The current watch list tracks this channel only through the shadow-banking-stress-events indicator, which is calibrated to fund-level events (gates, disruptions); the upstream bank-exposure channel is structurally distinct and not yet named. The Synthesis Reviewer should evaluate whether the bank→PC credit-line exposure (~$220–500B) warrants a standalone Global Debt indicator — distinct from the shadow-banking-stress-events indicator — so that the precursor pathway is monitored before a fund-level stress event fires.

### FDIC and OCC rescind 2013 Interagency Guidance on Leveraged Lending (December 5, 2025) — retroactive entry, event predates log inception; surfaced 2026-05-29

*Note: this entry documents an action that occurred ~December 5, 2025, before the signal log's inception (2026-04-11). It is logged retroactively under 2026-05-29 (the capture date) because the active log is May-only and no December section exists. The true event date is December 5, 2025.*

**Indicators:** Agency rulemaking using "innovation" or "competitiveness" to exempt new asset classes from oversight (named watch list indicator under Regulatory Cycle "Late-stage signals to watch" — the OCC/FDIC rescission removes the post-2013 constraint on bank leveraged lending to PE-sponsored borrowers above the ~6x debt-to-EBITDA threshold the 2013 guidance used as a soft ceiling; the stated rationale invokes banks' "competitive" loss of market share to nonbanks as the justification for removing the guardrail — a textbook Phase 4 deregulatory act framing removal of oversight as a market-competitiveness necessity)

**Sections:** Regulatory Cycle (primary), Global Debt (secondary — the rescission directly enables the bank→private-credit credit-line channel quantified in the FSB entry above; these two entries are structurally linked: the FSB report documents the exposure that the December 2025 deregulatory act unlocked)

**Scenario impact:** On December 5, 2025, the OCC and FDIC issued a joint interagency statement rescinding (1) the March 21, 2013 "Interagency Guidance on Leveraged Lending" and (2) the November 7, 2014 FAQs implementing that guidance. The Federal Reserve did not participate in the rescission and remains party to the 2013 guidance — creating a split-regulator landscape in which OCC- and FDIC-supervised institutions (national banks and state non-member banks) are free from the 6x leverage soft ceiling, while Fed-supervised institutions (bank holding companies, state member banks) are not. The stated rationale is directly on-point for the named watch-list indicator: the agencies said the 2013 guidance was "overly restrictive and impeded banks' application of risk management principles," that it "caused banks to lose market share to nonbanks, moving leveraged lending outside of the regulatory perimeter," and that it "was overly broad, capturing investment-grade company loans not intended to be covered." The GAO finding that the guidance constituted a rule requiring Congressional Review Act submission (never made) gave the agencies procedural cover. Escalation assessment: Level 1 — this is a backfilled Phase 4 deregulation data point, not a new development requiring immediate escalation. It does not advance the Regulatory Cycle past the Phase 4/5 boundary; the cycle is already positioned there. Its analytical value is (a) it fills a gap in the Phase 4 deregulatory record — a named high-leverage-lending guardrail removed by two of the three prudential regulators — and (b) it is the enabling act for the bank→private-credit credit-line channel the FSB quantifies in the entry above. Cross-reference to Entry 1 above: the FSB's $220–500B bank→PC credit-line exposure exists in a regulatory environment where OCC- and FDIC-supervised lenders are no longer constrained by the 2013 guidance's ~6x ceiling. The Synthesis Reviewer should weigh this as a compounding Phase 4 data point: the deregulatory act (December 2025) and the Tier 1 exposure quantification (FSB, May 2026) are best read as a paired signal.

**Source:** Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation, "Interagency Statement on OCC and FDIC Withdrawal from the Interagency Leveraged Lending Guidance Issuances," December 5, 2025 — fdic.gov/news/press-releases/2025/interagency-statement-occ-and-fdic-withdrawal-interagency-leveraged (Tier 1 — FDIC primary press release; confirms date, agencies, scope of rescission, and rationale verbatim); Office of the Comptroller of the Currency, "Interagency Statement on Recission of Interagency Leveraged Lending Guidance Issuances," OCC Bulletin 2025-44, December 5, 2025 — occ.treas.gov/news-issuances/news-releases/2025/nr-ia-2025-119.html (Tier 1 — OCC primary bulletin; independently confirms same date, scope, and rationale). Both sources confirm the Federal Reserve did not participate. Surfaced via Forbes opinion column (Rodriguez-Valladares) on 2026-05-29 — the column is not acceptable as sole source per source-quality standards (Tier 3 opinion); these Tier 1 primary agency documents are the source of record.

**Note:** The December 2025 rescission is a clean Phase 4 deregulation act: a post-crisis guardrail (2013 guidance, introduced after the pre-GFC leveraged lending excesses that contributed to the credit crunch) removed by two of three prudential regulators on the stated grounds that it reduced banks' competitiveness against nonbanks. The Fed's non-participation creates an uneven playing field that may itself accelerate the migration of leveraged lending toward OCC/FDIC-supervised institutions — the opposite of the 2013 guidance's intent to keep leveraged lending inside the regulatory perimeter. Paired with the FSB's May 2026 quantification of the bank→private-credit channel, the December 2025 rescission is the deregulatory precondition that made the FSB's "circles of risk" contagion pathway larger: banks are now unconstrained (by OCC/FDIC) in how much they lend to PE-sponsored borrowers at >6x leverage, and those borrowers are simultaneously the borrowers whose debt is held by private credit funds — completing the interconnection loop the FSB flags as a financial stability vulnerability.

### US strikes near Bandar Abbas Airport; IRGC retaliatory strike on US air base; kinetic exchange breaks deal-proximity narrative; Brent rebounds to $96–97

**Indicators:** IRGC naval activity (named watch list indicator — escalation signal direction: the IRGC fast-craft swarm formations and now retaliatory strike on a US air base represent continuous active IRGC operations; the watch list escalation condition "IRGC drone boats active near US mine-clearance destroyers" and "no corridor declared within 72 hours" both remain in effect; the Bandar Abbas exchange is kinetically deeper than prior IRGC warning-fire events); AIS mine clearance progress (named watch list indicator — de-escalation signal requires "US CENTCOM announces verified safe corridor; commercial insurers re-enter market"; the new kinetic exchange directly delays any mine-clearance corridor announcement and resets the timeline for the de-escalation conditions); Brent crude trajectory (named watch list indicator — Brent rebounded to $96.57–$97.51 on May 28, up ~2.4% intraday on the escalation news; the brief crossing below the $105 de-escalation threshold (logged May 27 at $96–99) is now confirmed deal-narrative-driven and fragile — the bounce on May 28 kinetics validates the May 27 entry's caution about reversal risk)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict, Global Debt (secondary — energy-shock CPI compounding pressure resumes; the deal-narrative Brent decline from May 23–27 partially reverses; structural FOMC June 16–17 Phase 5 test framing is unchanged but the macroeconomic input (energy path to June CPI) just deteriorated)

**Scenario impact:** The US strike near Bandar Abbas Airport and the IRGC retaliatory strike on a US air base are the most kinetically direct US-Iran exchange since the April 19 Touska boarding. The Bandar Abbas event is contextually different: the US action was defensive in stated framing (shooting down four Iranian drones + striking an IRGC ground control station), not an offensive blockade-enforcement action against commercial tonnage. The IRGC retaliation was against a US air base (not a naval asset), with IRGC language ("if repeated, our response will be even more decisive") explicitly threatening escalation. The deal-proximity narrative that drove the Brent decline from May 18 ($116.73) to May 27 ($96–99) — approximately 15% in nine calendar days — is directly contradicted by today's kinetics. Trump's May 27 statement not to "rush into a deal" and the May 28 IRGC retaliation together convert the MOU process from "days away" (May 24 framing) to an actively contested ceasefire with live violations. No Level 4 immediate trigger fires: Brent at $97.51 remains below the $130 threshold, and the action does not meet the "Strait of Hormuz physical infrastructure struck, mined, or declared formally closed" Level 4 criterion. However, this event materially advances the Scenario C framing ("mine or naval incident"): the exchange is not a mine detonation but is a direct state-on-state kinetic exchange inside the Hormuz conflict envelope. DTC axis C is now day 7 with no substantive diplomatic movement (the Bandar Abbas exchange is the opposite of substantive diplomatic movement). The axis C 14-day breach at June 3 is increasingly likely.

**Source:** India TV News, "US-Iran war LIVE Updates: Iran attacks US base in retaliation for strikes near Bandar Abbas airport," May 28, 2026 (Tier 2 — live wire, multiple incidents confirmed); Euronews, "Iran says it targeted a US airbase in retaliatory strikes," May 28, 2026 (Tier 2 — European wire; IRGC statement confirmed); ABC7 New York / Los Angeles, "Iran live updates: IRGC claims attack on US airbase after Bandar Abbas strikes," May 28, 2026 (Tier 2 — ABC News affiliate, datestamped; ABC News is Tier 3 on its own but corroborated by Euronews); PressTV, "Stern warning: IRGC announces retaliatory attack on US base following American aggression," May 28, 2026 (Tier 3 — Iranian state media; used only to confirm IRGC's own public statement, not for factual claims about US action); Fortune, "Current price of oil as of May 28, 2026" (Tier 2 — $97.51 at 9am ET, +2.41% on day). Note: no Tier 1 US CENTCOM or DoD press release confirming the Bandar Abbas strike is available at this entry's filing time; the India TV / Euronews / ABC7 convergence on the same facts constitutes adequate event-confirmation per source-quality standards at Tier 2.

**Note:** This exchange resets the armed-conflict section's internal directionality. The May 27 entry logged the Shamkhani "fantasy" language as a deal-stalIing signal; the May 28 kinetic exchange is categorically different — it is live military action during the nominally active ceasefire, not a diplomatic statement. The key analytical question is whether the exchange remains contained (as the April 18–19 Touska sequence was) or whether the IRGC's "more decisive" language escalates. The escalation watch list indicator "IRGC drone activity near USS Frank E. Petersen or USS Michael Murphy during mine-clearance operations" has been operative for weeks; today's exchange extends the pattern from drone harassment of mine-clearance ships to a state-on-state strike-and-counterstrike sequence involving an Iranian population center and a US air base. The DTC axis C breach date (June 3) is now four working days away.

### MSACSR April 2026: months' supply of new houses rises to 9.4 — named watch list threshold breached for first time

**Indicators:** Residential housing stress — months' supply of new houses above 9.0 (named watch list indicator — the watch list specifies "months' supply of new houses above 9.0 (currently 8.5, March 2026)" as the named threshold; the Census Bureau April 2026 New Residential Sales release reports MSACSR = 9.4, an 8.0% increase from the revised March estimate of 8.7; this is the first confirmed breach of the 9.0 threshold in this monitoring period; see aggregates.csv row 2026-04-01 confirming the new value)

**Sections:** Global Debt

**Scenario impact:** The April 2026 MSACSR print of 9.4 months crosses the named watch list threshold. New home sales fell 6.2% month-over-month (663k → 622k SAAR) and 11.3% year-over-year versus April 2025 (701k). Inventory of unsold new homes rose to 489k (seasonally adjusted), up 1.7% from March. The median sales price held at $422,500 — no deflationary signal yet in price. The months'-supply metric is the ratio of inventory to the current sales pace; the rise to 9.4 reflects both the inventory build and the demand decline simultaneously. The watch list's companion condition — "Case-Shiller national home price index turning negative year-over-year (currently +0.7%)" — has not fired; the May 26 Case-Shiller March print confirmed +0.7% YoY. The threshold breach here is a demand-withdrawal and inventory-accumulation signal, not yet a price-decline signal. The WARN > 9.0 level does not automatically trigger a Level 2 position update, but per the escalation tree, if this breach is confirmed in the next monthly release (May 2026 data, due late June), it will represent a sustained threshold crossing. The housing stress line was added to the watch list on May 19 at 8.5 months (March 2026); the first monthly release after that addition crosses the threshold. This is a Level 1 entry with a Level 2 flag: the watch list's Global Debt section position text should be updated to note the threshold breach when the Synthesis Reviewer next runs.

**Source:** US Census Bureau / US Department of Housing and Urban Development, "Monthly New Residential Sales, April 2026," May 2026 — census.gov/construction/nrs/pdf/newressales_202604.pdf (Tier 1 primary — official Census Bureau release; confirms 622k SAAR sales, 9.4 months' supply, 489k inventory); FRED / St. Louis Fed, Monthly Supply of New Houses in the United States (MSACSR) series — fred.stlouisfed.org/series/MSACSR (Tier 1 primary — confirms series value; aggregates.csv row 2026-04-01 months_supply = 9.4 is consistent with this release). Note: the watch list as of the May 19 update stated "currently 8.5, March 2026"; the April release (data period = April 2026) revises March to 8.7 and reports April at 9.4 — the watch list's March figure was consistent with the then-current data; the April release is the new data point.

**Note:** The MSACSR crossing 9.0 for the first time in this monitoring period changes the housing section of the Global Debt watch from "below threshold, tracking" to "threshold breached, monitoring for sustained crossing." The mechanism is consistent with the framework's Minsky Phase 3 framing: elevated mortgage rates (30-year at 6.51%, per aggregates.csv May 21) are suppressing demand while inventory builds, producing the rising months'-supply ratio. The watch list noted this dynamic in the May 19 position update; the April data confirms it is progressing faster than the March reading suggested. The energy-shock consumer balance sheet compression (fuel costs, CPI at 3.8%) is likely compounding the mortgage-affordability constraint. A sustained MSACSR above 9.0 for two consecutive months, combined with any Case-Shiller negative-YoY print, would constitute a Synthesis Reviewer Level 2 trigger for the Global Debt section.

### Europe jet fuel inventories approaching IEA 23-day critical threshold in June; Goldman Sachs confirms crossing projected for June; Birol six-week clock: no formal public expiry acknowledgment found

**Indicators:** EU aviation fuel strategic reserve drawdown rate (named watch list indicator — "buffer exhaustion timeline"; the watch list names this as a signal to watch under Armed Conflict; the Goldman Sachs estimate that European commercial jet fuel inventories will dip below the IEA critical 23-day shortage threshold "sometime in June" is the first named-bank quantified crossing estimate); Brent crude trajectory (named watch list indicator — the fuel-shortage escalation path is the structural channel connecting the Hormuz closure to European economic disruption; the 23-day threshold crossing would force refinery run cuts and flight cancellations at scale, not merely schedule reductions)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict, Global Debt (secondary — forced airline capacity reduction at scale converts the May 26 LCC liquidity-backstop entry from a US-sector story into a cross-Atlantic fuel-cost transmission; European sovereign fiscal pressure from emergency aviation measures would compound existing energy-subsidy fiscal burdens)

**Scenario impact:** Goldman Sachs estimates European commercial jet fuel inventories will cross the IEA 23-day critical shortage threshold sometime in June 2026. Multiple European carriers have already acted: KLM 160 intra-European route cancellations; Lufthansa grounding 27 short-haul aircraft and retiring four A340-600s ahead of schedule; Transavia cancellations May–June. The IEA's Birol "six weeks" statement (April 16, logged April 20) was not formally acknowledged as "expired" in today's searches — no IEA press release or new Birol statement marking the May 28 date. The buffer-arithmetic-to-July-9 framing established in the May 26 synthesis review is confirmed as the operative framework: the Birol statement was a soft clock, not a hard policy commitment, and its nominal expiry does not produce an IEA action or acknowledgment absent a formal policy trigger. The transition from "soft clock expiry" to "Goldman Sachs June crossing estimate" is the material change: an internal IEA soft-clock statement is now corroborated by a Tier 1/2 sell-side institution's quantified timeline. This advances the DTC axis A framing: the buffer-exhaustion clock is no longer solely IEA-internal data; it is now visible in sell-side European aviation analysis.

**Source:** Fortune, "Europe's jet fuel supplies should fall below the key 23-day shortage threshold in June, so plan your travel accordingly," May 6, 2026 (Tier 2 — Fortune citing Goldman Sachs estimate; Goldman Sachs is Tier 2 institutional); Euronews, "Jet fuel crisis: Who are the latest European airlines to cancel or suspend flights?," April 28, 2026 (Tier 2 — confirms KLM 160-route cancellation and Transavia); France 24, "Summer holidays up in the air as Europe braces for jet fuel shortage," May 2, 2026 (Tier 2 — confirms Lufthansa grounding 27 aircraft); IATA, "IATA Statement on Potential Jet Fuel Shortages," April 17, 2026 — iata.org press release (Tier 1 — IATA is the airline industry's Tier 1 body; confirms the 23-day threshold definition); IEA Oil Market Report May 2026 (Tier 1 — confirms OECD Europe deliveries decline of 380 kb/d expected in Q2 2026). Note: no formal IEA press release or Birol statement marking May 28 as a buffer-expiry date was found; searches returned only the April 16 original statement.

**Note:** The IEA Birol six-week buffer clock (April 16 → May 28) is confirmed to have no formal public expiry acknowledgment. This is analytically meaningful in two directions: (1) the IEA has not escalated its language — no "buffer exhausted" statement, no new emergency release announcement specifically tied to jet fuel on this date; (2) the Goldman Sachs June-crossing estimate provides external validation that the buffer drawdown is proceeding on schedule, suggesting the IEA's silence is operational (the releases are ongoing per the 400mb authorization) rather than a reversal of the exhaustion trajectory. The DTC axis A reading remains BREACHED (~42 days to July 9 window end); the May 28 nominal clock expiry does not change the axis A breach status, which was already in breach based on the July 9 buffer-arithmetic clock established May 26.

### Anderson v. Intel Corp.: oral argument deferred to 2026–27 SCOTUS term; DOL alternative-investment fiduciary rule operative independently of case outcome

**Indicators:** Agency rulemaking using "innovation" or "competitiveness" to exempt new asset classes from oversight (named watch list indicator — the Anderson v. Intel deferral removes the 2026 judicial-check possibility on the DOL proposed rule for ERISA fiduciary standards for alternative investments; the DOL March 31 rule proceeds without a SCOTUS benchmark-standard ruling until 2027 at earliest; this expands the regulatory-arbitrage window for private credit and alternative assets in 401(k) plans); DOL 401(k) safe harbor rule (named watch list indicator — the March 30 / March 31 DOL proposed rule establishing an ERISA safe harbor for alternative investments in DC plans operates independently of Anderson v. Intel, which addresses the pleading standard for excessive-fee litigation, not the safe-harbor rule itself; but the deferral removes a potential judicial narrowing of the DOL's authority before the rule's comment period closes)

**Sections:** Regulatory Cycle

**Scenario impact:** The Supreme Court deferred oral argument in Anderson v. Intel Corp. (No. 25-498) to its 2026–27 term on February 11, 2026. The case will likely be decided in 2027. The analytical consequence for the Regulatory Cycle watch is directional: (a) the DOL March 31, 2026 proposed rule on fiduciary duties for alternative investments in DC plans proceeds without a SCOTUS clarification of the prudence-pleading standard; plan fiduciaries adding private credit to 401(k) menus under the safe harbor face reduced litigation risk in 2026 relative to what a near-term adverse SCOTUS ruling would have imposed; (b) conversely, a plaintiff-friendly ruling in 2027 could retroactively expose plan fiduciaries who added alternatives under the 2026 DOL safe harbor — creating a future regulatory-reversal risk the watch list names as a Phase 5 signal; (c) the deferral itself is neither a Phase 5 indicator nor a deregulatory win — it is a procedural delay that expands the regulatory-arbitrage window. The watch list's "judicial resistance to Phase 4 deregulation remains material (CFPB courts)" framing still holds for the CFPB axis; Anderson deferral removes one judicial check on the DOL alternative-investment axis specifically.

**Source:** PSCA (Plan Sponsor Council of America), "SCOTUS 401(k) Benchmark Case Pushed to 2027," February 2026 — psca.org/news/psca-news/2026/2/scotus-401k-benchmark-case-pushed-to-2027/ (Tier 2 — PSCA is a plan-sponsor industry body, Tier 2 institutional; confirms deferral to 2026–27 term); SCOTUSblog, Anderson v. Intel Corporation Investment Policy Committee (Tier 2 — SCOTUSblog is the standard secondary reference for SCOTUS procedural status; confirms cert granted January 16, 2026); Ropes & Gray LLP, "Update on 401(k) Alternatives: Supreme Court Chooses to Hear Intel and DOL Guidance Expected Imminently," January 2026 — ropesgray.com (Tier 2 institutional — law firm alert; confirms the interaction between the SCOTUS case and DOL rulemaking).

**Note:** The deferral means the earliest possible Anderson ruling is June 2027. The DOL safe harbor proposed rule (March 31, 2026) will likely finalize in late 2026 before any SCOTUS guidance on the pleading standard. This sequencing — rule finalizes before SCOTUS rules — is the Phase 4 regulatory-arbitrage dynamic: the retail capital channel into private credit is institutionalized before the judicial check catches up. The watch list's Phase 5 forward-looking conditions include "judicial reversal of any major 2025 deregulatory measure"; the Anderson deferral delays rather than forecloses that pathway. It does not advance the Regulatory Cycle past the Phase 4/5 boundary; it widens the window over which the Phase 4 deregulatory buildout can proceed unchecked.

### Fed-model equity risk premium compresses to 0.17 pp — second-tightest since dot-com peak; new NDI sub-index N6 added at RED, N5 quantified threshold met

**Indicators:** Narrative-Divergence Index N6 (newly added 2026-05-28 — Fed-model ERP, forward S&P 500 12-mo earnings yield minus 10-yr UST yield; current reading 4.73% − 4.56% = 0.17 pp per Axios May 25; RED threshold <0.5 pp met; CRITICAL trigger at <0.0 pp not yet met but approaching); NDI N5 (argument-rebuttal frequency — strengthened to quantified ≥3 distinct outlets within rolling 60d window; threshold now met by Bloomberg April 7–9 cluster + Fortune April 19 + Axios May 25); cross-check Damodaran DCF-implied ERP at 4.23% (Jan 1, 2026, Tier 1 NYU Stern) — the divergence between the two methodologies is the load-bearing analytical signal (Fed model at dot-com extreme vs. DCF at long-run average means forward-growth assumptions are doing the heavy lifting); Buffett Indicator at 226–232% (already-confirmed N1 record) compounds the ERP signal

**Sections:** Market Behavior (primary); also implicates Regulatory Cycle indirectly via the Phase 5 binary at the June 16–17 Warsh FOMC — a rate cut against the 3.8% April CPI print in a regime where Fed-model ERP is already at 0.17 pp would compress ERP further on the rate leg while equity valuations would be expected to extend on the cuts narrative

**Scenario impact:** The Fed-model ERP compression is a quantitative confirmation of the same narrative-vs-physical divergence the framework qualitatively tracks via N1 (cap-weight concentration) and N5 (argument-rebuttal pattern). Historical context: Dec 1999 dot-com peak saw Fed-model ERP turn outright negative; Dec 2007 pre-GFC was ~3.4 pp; post-GFC peak was 8.17 pp; the 0.17 pp current reading is the second-tightest since 1999. Mechanism behind the compression: an ~10% YTD S&P rally concurrent with a Treasury sell-off (10-yr at 4.56% on May 25 vs. 4.47% currently — modestly lower; the rally drove most of the compression). The Axios framing ("the disappearing premium to own stocks") is the load-bearing N5 signal — a Tier 2 mainstream outlet publishing the bearish thesis as legitimate analysis, three days old. Combined with Bloomberg's April 7–9 "TINA effectively over" / "Stagflation Era Flashbacks" pair and Fortune's April 19 "dizzying new high" piece, this is three distinct Tier 2 outlets running the rebuttal of the bull narrative within a 60-day window — N5 quantified trigger met. The Damodaran DCF-implied ERP at 4.23% (Tier 1) does NOT confirm the same compression signal — Damodaran's methodology uses long-run earnings-growth assumptions that smooth across cycles. The methodological divergence is itself analytically interesting: the Fed model takes today's earnings and today's UST at face value and reads extreme compression; the DCF model assumes mean-reversion of growth and reads "fairly priced." When the two diverge sharply, the framework reads it as a Stage 4 signature (the bull case requires forward-growth assumptions to do load-bearing work; the bear case is visible in the today-vs-today comparison). No Level 4 immediate trigger fires: N6 at 0.17 pp is RED but not CRITICAL (<0.0 pp); no Mag-7 guidance miss attributed to input costs or power yet; no SIFI counterparty failure; no nuclear event; no Hormuz formal closure. Brent $97.51 below $130; 10-yr 4.47% below 5.0%; HY spread 2.72% below 3.5% Stage 5 break condition. The NDI YELLOW→RED zone state was already at RED on structural sub-indices as of 2026-05-26; the N6 addition reinforces but does not advance the zone. Forward escalation flag: N6 sustained <0.5 pp for 30d AND a Tier 1/2 sell-side note explicitly flagging the compression as a risk → Level 2. The Axios piece is the first publication; sell-side desk publication would be the trigger.

**Source:** Axios, "The disappearing premium to own stocks," May 27, 2026 — axios.com/2026/05/27/stocks-bonds-yields-premium (Tier 2 — primary Fed-model ERP source for the 0.17 pp May 25 reading; cites S&P 500 forward earnings yield 4.73% and 10-yr Treasury 4.56%); FRED, S&P 500 forward earnings yield + DGS10 10-year Treasury yield (Tier 1 primary — the underlying series Axios derives from); Aswath Damodaran (NYU Stern), "Data Update 2 for 2026: A Testing Year" — pages.stern.nyu.edu/~adamodar/New_Home_Page/datafile/histimpl.html and aswathdamodaran.substack.com/p/data-update-2-for-2026-a-testing (Tier 1 — DCF-implied ERP 4.23% at Jan 1, 2026; methodology cross-check); Bloomberg, "US Equities' Valuation Premium Brings Stagflation Era Flashbacks" (April 7, 2026) + "US Stocks Aren't Cheap Despite Rising Risk Premium" (April 9, 2026) — bloomberg.com (Tier 2 — paywalled, headlines confirmed; document the April N5 cluster); Fortune, "dizzying new high" / "this time is different" rebuttal piece (April 19, 2026) — fortune.com (Tier 2 — original April N5 trigger, previously logged); NY Fed ACM term premium +0.68% (April 24, 2026) + FRED THREEFYTP10 Kim-Wright +0.83% (May 22, 2026) (Tier 1 — companion macro context; term premium back to positive after years negative).

**Note:** Methodology disclosure matters when escalating off this signal. The Fed-model ERP and Damodaran's DCF-implied ERP can be at opposite extremes simultaneously (current state: Fed model second-tightest since 1999; DCF at long-run average). The watch-list NDI N6 sub-index is defined on the Fed-model methodology specifically because (a) it's the most-cited "ERP" in mainstream coverage and therefore drives narrative-rebuttal cycles (N5 channel); (b) the compression mechanism (high UST yields + stretched equity multiples) is the precise late-Stage-4 dynamic the framework is tracking. The DCF-implied ERP at long-run average is documented as a cross-check; if Damodaran's reading also compresses below ~3 pp in coming months, that would be a stronger structural signal because it would mean the bear case is winning even on long-run-growth assumptions. Forward watch: monitor Damodaran's next monthly print (likely Jul 1, 2026 baseline + crisis-window dailies if the late-July convergence window fires).

This does not yet meet the Level 2 3+ entries within 7 days in the same direction within Market Behavior threshold alone — but combined with the May 22 BDC net-outflow entry and the BCRED non-standard absorption entry (May 26), three entries pointing in the same direction within 7 days in Market Behavior are now logged. ### FOMC April 28–29 minutes (released May 21): majority sees rate hikes appropriate if inflation persists; four-dissent record; easing-bias language opposed by "many participants"

**Indicators:** Phase 5 candidate signal — enforcement-capture axis (named watch list indicator — the Warsh transition context makes this minutes release analytically distinct from a standard FOMC publication: the April meeting was Powell's final meeting; the language debate over the easing bias is the last Powell-era formulation; Warsh inherits a Committee where three of four dissenters were already calling for hike-readiness language and a majority wanted the easing bias removed; this is the institutional state of the FOMC Warsh will chair at June 16–17); 10-year Treasury yield sustained above 4.75% (precursor — the minutes explicitly state "many participants indicated they would have preferred removing the language from the post-meeting statement that suggested an easing bias"; removing easing bias and signaling rate hikes removes the rate-cut support for duration, which is the primary driver of any 10-yr move toward the 4.75% WARN line; 10-yr at 4.51% on May 26, down from 4.67% on May 19, partly on deal-narrative and partly on holiday positioning — the minutes' rate-hike signal is structurally opposed to this yield rally)

**Sections:** Regulatory Cycle, Global Debt

**Scenario impact:** Advances the June 16–17 FOMC watch list binary and raises the rate-hike scenario's structural plausibility. The "policy firming would likely become appropriate" language from the April minutes is the first explicit majority-view rate-hike signal in this cycle. Context: the Committee was holding at 3.50–3.75% against a 3.8% CPI print (April, released May 12) and energy +17.9% y/y; the Middle East conflict is explicitly identified in the minutes as a key driver of inflation uncertainty. The four-dissent structure is analytically important for the Warsh transition: Miran dissented for a cut; Hammack, Kashkari, and Logan dissented against the easing bias (i.e., for hike-readiness). Warsh's first meeting will face a Committee already in internal disagreement about the direction of the next move. The easing-bias debate is the institutional setup for the June 16–17 binary the watch list has been tracking as the Phase 5 confirmation test: a rate cut by Warsh against 3.8% CPI would confirm political capture of monetary policy; a rate hold with hike-readiness language would be consistent with monetary-policy independence. The minutes tell us that the pre-existing institutional consensus was already leaning toward removing the cut signal, making a Warsh-ordered cut *more* politically visible rather than less.

**Source:** Federal Reserve, "Minutes of the Federal Open Market Committee, April 28–29, 2026," released May 21, 2026 — federalreserve.gov/newsevents/pressreleases/monetary20260520a.htm (Tier 1 primary); CNBC, "Fed officials see rate hike ahead if inflation stays elevated, minutes show," May 20, 2026 (Tier 2 — confirms key quotes from minutes); Federal Reserve, FOMC statement April 29, 2026 — federalreserve.gov/newsevents/pressreleases/monetary20260429a.htm (Tier 1 primary — confirms four-dissent structure and rate hold at 3.50–3.75%); Bloomberg, "Fed Dissents: Why 4 Officials Voted Against FOMC Decision," April 29, 2026 (Tier 2 — dissenter identification).

**Note:** The minutes' explicit rate-hike language changes the framing around the June 16–17 FOMC. The prior log analysis described the Warsh-ordered rate-cut as the Phase 5 confirmation test; the minutes now show that a cut would require Warsh to override an April-meeting majority that was explicitly leaning toward hike-readiness language. That makes a cut at June's first meeting an even stronger Phase 5 signal if it occurs — it would represent not just ignoring the 3.8% CPI but overriding the Committee's own stated directional preference from the previous meeting. The most likely outcome (rate hold, dot-plot showing hikes) is a Phase 5 non-confirmation. However, the Hormuz deal-narrative Brent decline and 10-yr rally introduce a complicating factor: if the MOU is signed before June 16–17 and Brent retreats toward $90, the energy component of CPI falls sharply in the June forward projection, and Warsh has a legitimate macroeconomic basis for a more dovish posture — making the Phase 5 test less clean.

### LCC industry: Association of Value Airlines requests $2.5B federal liquidity pool; Frontier, Allegiant, Avelo, Sun Country collectively cite ~100% jet fuel increase since February 2026

**Indicators:** Enforcement actions against major financial institutions revealing compliance failures masked during deregulation (adjacent — this is the sector-level analog of the Spirit wind-down logged May 18: the LCC cohort that survived Spirit's exit is now collectively approaching the government for a liquidity backstop, which converts the May 19 LCC bifurcation analysis from a warning into an observed financial-stress event); Corporate zombie refinancing failures as rates stay elevated (named watch list indicator — the $2.5B request is the LCC cohort's acknowledgment that their operating model is not sustainable at current fuel costs without external support; fuel has increased ~100% since February against margins that assumed $2.24/gallon; the request for warrants in exchange for liquidity is the standard pre-distress government-backstop structure)

**Sections:** Global Debt, Armed Conflict (secondary — the LCC liquidity stress is a direct second-order transmission of the Hormuz energy-shock into the US corporate sector, extending the May 18 Spirit Airlines data point from a single firm to a sector-wide stress pattern)

**Scenario impact:** Advances the existing Global Debt and Armed Conflict framing — this is the sector-level confirmation that the May 19 LCC bifurcation Level 3 addendum's medium-severity path is live. The Association of Value Airlines (AVA) — Frontier, Allegiant, Avelo, Sun Country, and Spirit (now in wind-down) — is lobbying for up to $2.5B from a government-administered liquidity pool, with airlines providing warrants (equity stakes) as collateral. JetBlue is separately hedging: $2.4B liquidity + $500M new aircraft-backed financing + $250M option (reported in the same search results, not AVA-affiliated). The White House "aware of outreach" but no official commitment. This is structurally different from the European aviation response (Lufthansa schedule cuts, national subsidies inside existing frameworks) — the US LCC sector is approaching a direct-government-backstop request with warrant dilution, which has not occurred in commercial aviation since the post-9/11 and COVID-era relief packages. No scenario probability change warranted from this entry alone; but if the White House grants the request, it is a named "agency rulemaking using 'innovation' or 'competitiveness' to exempt new asset classes from oversight" structural analog in the energy-backstop context.

**Source:** ABC News / Good Morning America, "What to know as budget airlines seek $2.5 billion in relief amid rising fuel costs," May 2026 (Tier 2 — ABC News, citing AVA directly); Travel Weekly, "Budget airlines seek $2.5 billion in relief from Trump administration amid fuel price surge," May 2026 (Tier 2); TravelAndTourWorld, "Frontier Joins Avelo, Spirit, Allegiant, and Sun Country Airlines in Negotiations with U.S. Government for Over Two Billion Dollars in Relief Package," May 2026 (Tier 2–3). Note: no Tier 1 primary (Department of Transportation press release or White House announcement) confirmed; Tier 2 adequate for the event itself. The White House "aware of outreach" language is confirmed via ABC News (Tier 2) citing administration officials. The SEC Form 8-K filing for Frontier Group Holdings (FY2026) confirms Frontier's financial position context (Tier 1 secondary).

**Note:** The $2.5B request is the structural evidence that the May 19 LCC bifurcation addendum was correctly calibrated: the Spirit wind-down was not an isolated casualty but a leading indicator for the cohort. The watch list's May 18 analysis established that Spirit's failure was "the first confirmed corporate casualty WITHIN Minsky Phase 3, not a phase advance." The AVA collective backstop request extends that characterization to the sector level — multiple firms in simultaneous financial stress from the same cause. The key escalation question is whether a government backstop approval would represent a policy response that slows or stops the natural Minsky Phase 3 deleveraging process, as occurred with COVID-era aviation relief, or whether the White House declines and the sector proceeds to individual distress events. The warrant-for-liquidity structure is the former; a White House refusal accelerates the latter. This entry should be flagged for the next Synthesis Reviewer pass.

### BCRED Q2 tender offer: no gate; Q1 repurchases ($3.2B) met via cap increase to 7% + $400M Blackstone employee injection; Q2 window opens with $3.7B total Q1 repurchase satisfied

**Indicators:** Private equity NAV markdowns or redemption gates at major funds (named watch list indicator — the watch list explicitly identifies "the first major fund gate (BCRED being the marquee candidate)" as the "next discrete tell" for Stage 4 escalation; this entry documents that BCRED did NOT gate in Q1 — Blackstone raised the repurchase cap from 5% to 7% and injected $400M in employee capital to absorb all requests; the Q2 tender offer (filed May 1, expiring May 29) is the next window in which the stop-gap mechanism either holds or fails); Stage 4 gate-cascade transmission confirmed operational (named indicator — Q1 confirmed net outflow at the BDC asset-class level per May 22 log; BCRED's Q1 non-gate is the individual counterpart: the largest fund held, but only by expanding the absorption mechanism to its near-regulatory-limit)

**Sections:** Market Behavior, Global Debt

**Scenario impact:** Confirms the May 22 log entry's forward-looking framing and clarifies the Q1 outcome. The BCRED Q1 result is a no-gate with a significant structural qualifier: Blackstone used $400M of its own capital and raised the repurchase cap to 7% (maximum without changing repurchase terms) to absorb $3.2B in requests against $1.9B in inflows — a $1.3B net redemption shortfall covered by non-standard mechanisms. The fund maintained $8B+ liquidity and 0.7x leverage (vs. 2x regulatory limit), which means the Q1 hold was genuine from a solvency standpoint, not a distress-gate. The Q2 window (tender offer filed May 1, expiring May 29) is the next observable data point: if the deal narrative drives Brent down and reduces energy-shock-driven redemption pressure, BCRED's Q2 window may close without a gate. If the deal fails and Brent reverses upward, the redemption pressure that required a $400M employee injection in Q1 returns in Q2 without the one-off employee-capital mechanism having been reset. The HY spread at 2.74% (May 22, prices.csv) continues to confirm that the commercial-bank credit channel is not transmitting the private-credit stress — the BCRED situation is Stage 4-consistent and Minsky Phase 3-consistent, not a Stage 5 or Phase 4 signal.

**Source:** SEC EDGAR, Blackstone Private Credit Fund Form 8-K, filed April 29, 2026 — bcred-20260429.htm (Tier 1 primary — confirmed repurchase activity Q1 2026); SEC EDGAR, BCRED Form SC TO-I, May 1, 2026 — tender offer terms and expiration May 29, 2026 (Tier 1 primary); GlobeSt., "Blackstone Answers Redemption Spike With Higher Tender, Fresh Capital," March 10, 2026 (Tier 2 — $400M employee injection detail and cap increase to 7%); Yahoo Finance / Connect Money, "Largest Blackstone BDC hikes share repurchase limit to 7%," 2026 (Tier 2 — corroborating cap increase); BCRED Q1 2026 Update page — bcred.com/q1-2026-update/ (Tier 2 — fund-published investor update).

**Note:** The BCRED no-gate outcome is a key watch list indicator update: the marquee candidate for a gate held in Q1 through a combination of cap expansion and proprietary capital injection. The analytical significance is not that the gate did not happen — it is *how* it was avoided. The $400M employee injection is a one-time mechanism; the 7% cap is the regulatory maximum without restructuring the offer terms. If Q2 redemption pressure matches Q1's $3.2B level, Blackstone would need to either gate, change the repurchase terms (which requires SEC filing and advance notice), or inject more proprietary capital. The Q2 tender expiry on May 29 is three days from this entry's filing date; any gate announcement before then would be a named watch list escalation indicator. The May 29 outcome should be logged immediately upon confirmation.

**Sections:** Global Debt

**Scenario impact:** Confirms existing Global Debt framing — no threshold crossed, no framework phase change. The S&P Cotality Case-Shiller U.S. National Home Price NSA Index recorded a 0.7% annual gain in March 2026. The 10-City and 20-City Composites were +1.4% and +0.8% respectively. This is structurally consistent with the watch list's "post-2022-correction stagnation" characterization: the housing market is neither recovering strongly nor falling into Minsky Phase 3 transmission territory. The energy-shock transmission into housing (via mortgage rates — 30-year at 6.51% per aggregates.csv May 21) and via consumer balance sheet pressure is not yet showing in the price index. The months' supply reading (last confirmed 8.5 in the watch list; aggregates.csv last populated months_supply value from 2025-12-01 = 7.8) is the more sensitive indicator — a months' supply move above 9.0 would warrant a log entry before the price index would. This entry resolves the Case-Shiller aggregates.csv staleness flag (the watch list noted "Tuesday 2026-05-27 — Case-Shiller March print" as a pending data point; it released one day early on May 26).
