**Note:** The Case-Shiller print is confirmatory, not signal-advancing. Its analytical value in this pass is two-fold: (1) it resolves the aggregates.csv staleness identified in the brief and confirms the housing indicator remains below both threshold levels; (2) it provides context for the May 27 first-post-Memorial-Day Treasury auction environment — a stable housing print removes one potential volatility source from the auction-day backdrop. The aggregates.csv should be updated with the March 2026 Case-Shiller value (0.7% YoY, national NSA index); recommend running `uv run scripts/fetch_aggregates.py` to capture this and any other recent releases (mortgage rate at 6.51% per May 21 weekly Freddie Mac survey is already reflected in the file but the Case-Shiller national index value is not).

### IEA May 2026 OMR: global inventories drew 246 mb in March–April at record pace; OECD on-land stocks down 146 mb; 164 mb of 400 mb emergency authorization drawn; buffer window ~July 9

**Indicators:** EU aviation fuel strategic reserve drawdown rate (named watch list indicator — the IEA May OMR is the first Tier 1 publication to quantify the pace of buffer depletion since the Birol April 16 "six weeks" statement; OECD on-land commercial stocks fell 146 mb in two months, equivalent to ~2.4 mb/d drain on the commercial buffer alone; the 400 mb IEA emergency authorization provides a ~2.5 mb/d supplement but with 164 mb already drawn and the release window ending approximately July 9, the residual authorization covers roughly 7 weeks at current draw rates — confirming the Birol clock is not merely a forecast but an observed inventory trajectory); Brent crude trajectory (named watch list indicator — the IEA explicitly warns of "renewed price swings" and identifies peak summer demand as the next stress period; the current Brent decline to ~$103–116 is narrated against a stock draw that is structural, not resolved; IEA demand forecast revised down 420 kb/d to 104 mb/d for 2026, reflecting demand destruction from the energy shock, which is itself a second-order Minsky Phase 3 deepening signal); Ras Laffan LNG restoration timeline (named watch list indicator — the OMR's demand-contraction forecast and record stock draw together imply that the global system is relying on emergency buffer consumption to avoid an acute supply crisis; the resolution timeline for Hormuz is the single variable that determines whether the July buffer window ends in stabilization or emergency deepening)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict, Global Debt

**Scenario impact:** The May OMR is the most important Tier 1 fuel-buffer data point since the April 16 Birol statement. It converts the "six weeks" estimate into an observed realized draw rate: 246 mb drawn in 60 days (March–April) = ~4.1 mb/d net global inventory drain, of which 164 mb of the 400 mb IEA emergency authorization has already been utilized. The remaining ~236 mb of authorized-but-not-yet-released emergency stocks represents approximately 57 days of buffer at the ~4.1 mb/d draw rate if no commercial stock replenishment occurs — placing the structural exhaustion window at approximately late July 2026, one month beyond the IEA's own July 9 release-window end date. This is not yet a Level 4 trigger (no immediate OECD commercial stock exhaustion, no IEA member declaring the SPR authorization insufficient), but it is the first Tier 1 quantification confirming the Birol clock is operating as described. If the US-Iran MOU (logged earlier today) fails to produce an operational Hormuz reopening before the July 9 IEA release window expires, the buffer depletion arithmetic becomes the primary market-forcing mechanism.

**Source:** IEA, "Oil Market Report, May 2026," published May 13, 2026 — iea.org/reports/oil-market-report-may-2026 (Tier 1 primary — IEA official publication; public version PDF at iea.blob.core.windows.net); Euronews, "Oil stocks drain at record pace as IEA warns of renewed price swings," May 13, 2026 (Tier 2 — confirms headline figures from OMR); IranOilGas Network, "IEA oil market report — May 2026 highlights," May 2026 (Tier 3 — confirms demand-contraction figure; not a primary source, included for completeness only); RTE News, "Countries drawing down oil stocks at record pace — IEA," May 13, 2026 (Tier 2 — confirms 164 mb drawn figure and July 9 buffer window).

**Note:** The 164 mb drawn / 400 mb authorized ratio (41% consumed in ~10 weeks) is the single most analytically important number from this pass. The watch list's EU aviation fuel strategic reserve drawdown rate indicator was originally framed around the question of whether European jet-fuel reserves would exhaust before a diplomatic resolution; the IEA OMR reframes it: the exhaustion risk is now a global OECD commercial + strategic reserve arithmetic problem, not merely a European aviation-specific problem. The Birol April 16 clock (six weeks from April 16 = May 28) is not "expired" in the sense of a discrete event; it is "confirmed expiring" in the sense that the observed draw rate validates the trajectory he described. Silence from Birol or the IEA on a follow-up to the April 16 statement since May 13 is itself notable — the OMR is the follow-up, and it does not retract the six-week framing.

### Singapore middle distillate stocks hit nine-month low (week ending May 6): 44.83 mb total; light and middle distillates falling; Middle East imports near zero

**Indicators:** EU aviation fuel strategic reserve drawdown rate (adjacent — Singapore is the Asian middle-distillate benchmark; nine-month lows with Middle East imports near zero is the Asia-Pacific confirmation of the same supply-chain break the IEA OMR documents on the OECD side; Singapore distillate stocks are not a direct European jet-fuel indicator but are the principal forward indicator for Asian aviation fuel availability and for how long Atlantic-basin cargoes will be drawn east); Ras Laffan LNG restoration timeline (named watch list indicator — Singapore's oil product inventory hit nine-month lows because "imports from the Middle East remained near zero," confirming the supply chain disruption from Hormuz extends to the full refined-product complex in Asia, not just crude volumes)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict, Global Debt

**Scenario impact:** Confirms the Asian buffer picture is deteriorating in parallel with the European and US buffers documented in this pass. The 44.83 mb total combined onshore product stock in Singapore (week ending May 6, 2026, Enterprise Singapore data) is a nine-month low. The channel: Hormuz-adjacent crude is not reaching Singapore's refinery complex, causing refined-product drawdown from inventory. This is the Asian analog of the European Birol clock — a different geography but the same structural dynamic. Singapore distillate stocks are the watch list's implicit Asian benchmark; their nine-month low confirms the global buffer depletion is not confined to OECD-region emergency stocks. No Level 4 threshold is tripped: Singapore stocks are low, not exhausted, and there is no Tier 1 confirmation of Asian aviation fuel rationing analogous to the Netherlands/Italy/Australia regimes.

**Source:** Enterprise Singapore weekly data, week ending May 6, 2026 — confirmed via energynews.oedigital.com, "Singapore's oil products stocks fall to a nine-month-low as US-Iran conflict cuts supply," May 7, 2026 (Tier 2 — OE Digital Energy News, citing Enterprise Singapore official data; Enterprise Singapore is a Tier 1 source for this series); QC Intel, "Singapore oil stocks drop as fuel oil, middle distillate inventories fall," 2026 (Tier 2 — corroborating figure); Kpler, "Hormuz escalation puts middle distillates at the center of supply risk," February 23, 2026 (Tier 2 institutional — Kpler blog, provides structural context for why Singapore is the Asian bellwether for this series).

**Note:** The Singapore nine-month low is the Asian confirmation of the IEA OMR's global buffer-depletion narrative. Its analytical value is asymmetric: if Hormuz reopens, Singapore stocks recover quickly as Middle East cargoes resume; if Hormuz remains closed through June, Singapore enters the same exhaustion arithmetic as OECD commercial stocks, adding a third regional buffer (alongside Europe and the US) drawing simultaneously. A Singapore middle distillate stock level that crosses below the 40 mb threshold would be a watch list Level 2 candidate — that level has not been reached as of the May 6 data.

### EIA weekly petroleum status report (week ending May 15, 2026): US distillate inventories 11% below five-year average; +1.7 mb build on week; demand at 3.8 mb/d (+3.5% YoY)

**Indicators:** EU aviation fuel strategic reserve drawdown rate (adjacent — EIA distillate data is the US-side complement to the European and Asian buffer data; 11% below five-year average is structurally below normal for this time of year, confirming the domestic US buffer is not available to absorb export demand from depleted European stocks); Corporate zombie refinancing failures as rates stay elevated (adjacent — distillate demand up 3.5% YoY despite the energy shock reflects that US industrial and transport demand has not yet collapsed, which is consistent with Minsky Phase 3 deepening rather than a demand-destruction recession — the distillate demand signal here is the absence of the recessionary collapse that would otherwise lower energy-price pressure)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict, Global Debt

**Scenario impact:** Confirms the US distillate buffer is below seasonal norms but not in acute shortage. The 11%-below-five-year-average reading is a persistent below-normal level consistent with global draw dynamics, not a new acute shortage event. The 1.7 mb week-on-week build is directionally supportive (stocks modestly recovering), but the structural below-average position means the US distillate buffer cannot serve as the supply source of last resort for European or Asian markets. The 3.5% YoY demand increase is the analytically important element: it indicates the US energy-shock transmission has not produced demand destruction in the distillate complex — US industrial demand is still running above last year, which is a Minsky Phase 3 consistency signal (the crisis is a supply shock, not yet a demand collapse). No watch list threshold crossed.

**Source:** US Energy Information Administration, Weekly Petroleum Status Report, week ending May 15, 2026, released May 20, 2026 — eia.gov/petroleum/supply/weekly/ (Tier 1 primary); StoneX, "EIA Weekly Petroleum Data Recap," May 13, 2026 (Tier 2 — corroborating weekly recap, confirms distillate build and below-average inventory framing).

**Note:** The 11%-below-average distillate figure in the US is the third data point in this pass (alongside the IEA OECD 146 mb commercial draw and Singapore's nine-month low) confirming that global middle-distillate buffers are simultaneously depleted across all three major storage geographies. The directional divergence — a 1.7 mb weekly build in the US against continued depletion in Europe and Asia — suggests some US-specific supply that is not available to global markets (SPR draw policy, domestic refinery throughput patterns). For the watch list, the critical question is whether a US distillate level 11% below average can deteriorate further if the Iran MOU fails and European demand for Atlantic-basin cargoes intensifies. Recommend tracking the EIA weekly distillate figure as the US-side fuel-buffer indicator going forward.

### NWE jet fuel crack spread at $88–$91/bbl premium to Brent: record high; 350%+ above one-year-ago levels; structural supply constraint, not seasonal premium

**Indicators:** EU aviation fuel strategic reserve drawdown rate (named watch list indicator — the jet-Brent crack spread is the market's real-time price signal for physical jet fuel scarcity; $88–$91/bbl premium is approximately 3.5–4x the historical normal range of $10–$25/bbl; this level confirms that the Birol/ACI Europe buffer warnings are not merely logistical — they are being priced by physical traders who cannot locate supply); Brent crude trajectory (named watch list indicator — the crack spread divergence means that even as Brent spot declined from $116.73 on May 18 on the deal narrative, the refined-product premium widened, preserving or increasing the effective cost of jet fuel to airlines; the Brent spot decline is not transmitting to aviation-fuel cost relief)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict, Global Debt, Market Behavior (tertiary — the $88–$91 crack is the price mechanism through which the energy shock is transmitting into the LCC sector stress logged earlier today and the Spirit Airlines failure logged May 18)

**Scenario impact:** The crack spread level is the most direct price signal confirming that the fuel-buffer depletion documented in the IEA OMR and Singapore data is acute at the physical jet-fuel market level. Historical norms: $10–$25/bbl. Early-2026 pre-crisis levels: approximately $20–$25/bbl. Current: $88–$91/bbl, a 350%+ increase above year-ago levels. This spread level is the market's answer to the IEA OMR's buffer-depletion data: physical traders are pricing jet fuel as if supply were structurally scarce, not temporarily disrupted. The NWE jet-Brent crack at this level is the transmission mechanism from Hormuz disruption to the LCC $2.5B backstop request logged in this pass — it is not separately advancing the scenario table but confirms that all three fuel-buffer signals in this pass (IEA OMR draw rate, Singapore nine-month low, EIA distillate below average) are being accurately priced by the physical market. No Level 4 trigger: the watch list's Level 4 threshold for fuel-related signals is Brent above $130/bbl, and the current crack-spread spike is occurring against a Brent level in the $103–116 range.

**Source:** OilPrice.com, "Jet Cracks Soar to Record Highs as Iran War Breaks Fuel Markets," 2026 (Tier 2 — OilPrice.com, citing Platts/S&P Global assessment data; $88–$91 figure confirmed); Euronews, "Flying soon? What the jet fuel crisis means for travellers and airlines," April 17, 2026 (Tier 2 — confirms the crack spread context and 350% above year-ago framing); DiscoveryAlert, "Jet Fuel Price Surge: Aviation Crisis and Market Impact," 2026 (Tier 3 — confirms crack spread record-high framing; used for corroboration only); S&P Global / Platts Jet Fuel Price Assessments (Tier 1 methodology reference for NWE CIF Cargoes vs Brent benchmark — actual current price data is subscription-only; the $88–$91 figure is derived from Tier 2 sources citing Platts assessments).

**Note:** The $88–$91 crack spread is the clearest single number demonstrating that the Birol "six weeks" clock, now at or past its nominal expiry (May 28), has not been rendered moot by the deal narrative. The physical jet fuel market is pricing ongoing acute scarcity even as Brent spot reflects deal-narrative optimism. The divergence between Brent spot (declining on MOU news) and the crack spread (elevated on physical scarcity) is analytically identical to the April 24 curve-vs-physical divergence logged in the watch list: the financial market is pricing a resolution that the physical market cannot locate. This is the fuel-specific restatement of the Stage 4 term-structure diagnostic signature already confirmed in the watch list.

### Italy jet fuel rationing: spread from 4 to 8+ airports by mid-April; Brindisi complete depletion confirmed; supplies "guaranteed until end of May"; Netherlands holding Phase 1; Australia confirmed at Level 2 (National Cabinet April 23)

**Indicators:** EU aviation fuel strategic reserve drawdown rate (named watch list indicator — this entry documents the current status of the three statutory rationing regimes that were active as of April 20; Italy has escalated from 4 to 8 airports; Brindisi has experienced complete on-site depletion; Italy's "guaranteed until end of May" language means the June 1 supply picture is the next hard binary for Italian aviation rationing; Netherlands remains at Phase 1, not escalated to Phase 2; Australia confirmed at Level 2 by National Cabinet on April 23, not escalated to Level 3); AIS mine clearance progress (adjacent — the three statutory rationing regimes are the downstream consequence of the mine-clearance / corridor absence: if the US-Iran MOU produces an operational Hormuz reopening and mine clearance, the rationing pressure reverses; if the MOU fails, the June supply question for Italy and the ongoing Level 2 status in Australia are the next escalation binary events)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict, Global Debt

**Scenario impact:** Mixed picture across the three regimes. Italy escalated beyond the April 20 baseline (4 airports initially capped → 8+ airports affected → Brindisi complete depletion confirmed), with supply "guaranteed until end of May" — meaning the Italian aviation fuel buffer has consumed its current guarantee window. Netherlands holds at Phase 1 with no Phase 2 escalation; the Dutch search results show Phase 2 as an "early warning" level with demand-reduction measures (driving restrictions, public transport incentives) but no Tier 1 confirmation of Phase 2 activation. Australia confirmed at Level 2 by National Cabinet on April 23 — no escalation to Level 3 confirmed in this pass. The non-escalation across the Netherlands and Australia is analytically important: neither has crossed the Phase 2 / Level 3 thresholds that would represent a step-change in mandatory allocation. All three remain in the warning/preparation zone rather than the mandatory-allocation zone. The Italian Brindisi complete depletion is the single most acute new data point — a European commercial airport without any on-site jet fuel is a watch list escalation signal of a qualitatively different character from a 2,000-litre cap.

**Source:** Italy: Euronews, "Jet fuel crisis: Rationing triggered at four airports in Italy," April 6, 2026 (Tier 2 — initial 4-airport report); Traveltourister, "Italy Jet Fuel Rationing April 2026: 7 Airports Cap Flights," April 2026 (Tier 3 — 7-airport count; used for corroboration); NomadLawyer.org, "Italy Fuel Crunch Spreads Across Regional Airports," April 2026 (Tier 3 — 8-airport / Brindisi depletion sourcing; Tier 3 only — Brindisi depletion should be confirmed via Tier 1/2 primary); AtlasPress, "Jet Fuel Rationing Imposed at Four Major Italian Airports," April 5, 2026 (Tier 2 — confirms timeline). Netherlands: DutchReview, "The Netherlands activates phase one of national oil crisis plan," April 20, 2026 (Tier 2 — Phase 1 activation, no Phase 2 upgrade); NL Times, "Cabinet presents €967 million energy relief package," April 20, 2026 (Tier 2 — confirms Phase 1 status and Phase 2 structure); Rijksoverheid.nl, Landelijk Crisisplan Olie 2026 publication (Tier 1 — Dutch government document confirming Phase 1 active). Australia: Heavy Vehicle Industry Australia, "Fuel Security Update: May 1, 2026" (Tier 2 — confirms Level 2 continuation, National Cabinet April 23 confirmation); DCCEEW / Australian government fuel security page (Tier 1 — NFSP structure confirmation).

**Note:** The Italian Brindisi complete-depletion event is a qualitative escalation beyond what the April 20 watch list position anticipated. The April 20 baseline described "Italy jet-fuel caps at seven airports since April 5 (Air BP Italia 2,000-litre cap)" — a supply constraint. Brindisi moving to zero on-site availability is a supply absence, not a constraint. This distinction matters for the Scenario B buffer-exhaustion geometry: caps are rationing; zero availability is the condition the watch list named "statutory rationing plans activated" was designed to detect. The Brindisi event should be tracked; if it spreads to additional Italian airports or appears in other EU member states, it becomes a Level 2 candidate (3+ entries within 7 days in the Armed Conflict section moving in the same direction). The Netherlands' non-escalation to Phase 2 and Australia's non-escalation to Level 3 are both stabilization signals that prevent this entry from meeting a Level 2 threshold — the existing regimes are holding at their April 20 levels, not advancing.

### China-Iran crude flows drop ~20% YoY in May as Shandong port sanctions enforcement tightens; Iran oil exports fall to ~1.1 mb/d; Russian competing grades pressure Iran market share

**Indicators:** Russia oil premium vs. Brent spread (named watch list indicator — the Russia windfall indicator is advancing: Urals traded at approximately $110–112/bbl in mid-May, against a Russian federal budget baseline of $59/bbl; the Urals-Brent spread has narrowed as Russia gains alternative-routing advantage; Russia's windfall is generating an estimated $36–49B in additional oil and gas revenue above budget projections for 2026); IRGC naval activity (named watch list indicator — the ~20% YoY drop in China's Iranian crude imports, if sustained, is a deal-progress proxy: it suggests either (a) Chinese refiners are substituting Russian grades because Iranian supply lines are disrupted by Hormuz enforcement; or (b) reduced Chinese demand for Iranian crude reflects a reduced political premium on the China-Iran relationship at current volumes; in either case, the Iran-China crude volume is a direct leading indicator of whether the PGSA toll regime is generating enough revenue to sustain Iran's strategic posture); Brent crude trajectory (named watch list indicator — Urals at ~$112/bbl in the context of a Brent around $103–116 means the Urals-Brent discount has narrowed sharply from the ~$25–30 discount prevailing in 2022–2023; Russian crude is now approaching parity with Brent on an absolute-price basis)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict, Global Debt

**Scenario impact:** Two partially offsetting signals. The Iran-China flow drop (~20% YoY, Kpler/Iran International data) is a deal-progress-adjacent signal: reduced Chinese offtake of Iranian crude could reflect Shandong port enforcement (Tier 1-adjacent — Chinese customs/port authority decisions) reducing demand for Iranian shadow-fleet cargoes, or it could reflect Chinese diversification toward Russian grades. The IranIntl reporting attributes the decline to (1) Chinese authorities barring sanctioned tankers from Shandong ports since January; (2) teapot refineries operating near record-low rates; (3) Russian Sokol and Novy Port competing on price. This is not a deal-progress signal in the US-Iran diplomatic sense; it is a sanctions-enforcement signal — Chinese port enforcement of US secondary sanctions is tightening, which is a structural change in the China-Iran relationship that the watch list's "China escalation column" framework had not explicitly modeled. The Russia windfall picture confirms the watch list's "Russia oil premium vs. Brent spread" indicator: Urals at ~$112/bbl against a $59 budget baseline = ~$53/bbl above the budget assumption, delivering the Ukraine-war-sustaining windfall the framework identified.

**Source:** Iran International, "Iran crude oil flows to China drop as sanctions bite," published approximately June 4, 2026 (Tier 2 — Iran International is an established Iran-focused Tier 2 outlet; article is dated June 4 but appeared in May 26 search results, suggesting early publication or search-index timing; the underlying Kpler/Vortexa data is Tier 2 institutional); OilPrice.com, "China's Oil Imports from Iran Hit Record High," 2026 (Tier 2 — provides the comparison baseline showing record-high imports in earlier periods, against which the current drop is measured); OilPrice API / TradingEconomics, Urals crude price data, May 2026 — oilpriceapi.com/live/urals-crude-oil-price (Tier 2 — price data provider); The Moscow Times, "Did the Mideast Conflict Just Rescue Russia's War Budget?" March 11, 2026 (Tier 2 — windfall framing and $59/bbl budget baseline); Fortune, "Russia was expecting a windfall from soaring oil prices, but relentless Ukrainian drone attacks are devastating nearly half its export capacity," March 29, 2026 (Tier 2 — supply constraint on Russia's ability to fully capture the windfall, noting Ukrainian drone damage to export infrastructure).

**Note:** The China-Iran flow drop is the first watch list indicator that moves in a direction partially counter to the primary escalation narrative. The watch list's "China escalation column fully met" characterization (April 14) described Chinese state-backed determination to maintain transit access; the Shandong port sanctions enforcement — Chinese authorities themselves barring sanctioned tankers — introduces a new variable: China is enforcing US secondary sanctions at the port level even as its defense minister declares the strait "open to us." This is not a contradiction but a differentiation: the Chinese government is willing to maintain a declaratory military posture on Hormuz transit while allowing commercial compliance mechanisms at the port level. For the Scenario D watch (great-power incident), this differentiation is stabilizing — China is not fully committed to protecting Iranian oil flows regardless of consequences. The Russia windfall data, taken together with the Fortune reporting on Ukrainian drone damage to export infrastructure, suggests Russia's actual windfall realization is constrained by production/export capacity damage, not just price.

## 2026-05-23

### Warsh sworn in as Fed Chair (May 22): crypto reads net-bearish on monetary policy, net-bullish on supervision; BTC at ~$76,800 — muted reaction, no rally

**Indicators:** Phase 5 candidate signal — enforcement-capture axis (named watch list indicator — Warsh's swearing-in is the operational completion of the May 13 confirmation; the supervisory-posture shift from Powell's "cautious observer" to Warsh's "constructive engagement" framing is the watch list's named "agency rulemaking using 'innovation' or 'competitiveness' to exempt new asset classes from oversight" indicator, now at the apex institutional level); Whistleblower disclosures from crypto, private equity, or AI investment products marketed to retail accounts (adjacent — Warsh's $100M+ personal crypto portfolio spanning 30+ digital asset projects, including Bitwise Asset Management, Electric Capital, Polychain Capital, and Polymarket, is a disclosed financial interest in the sector his regulatory posture will govern; this is the regulatory-arbitrage-at-the-apex pattern the watch list names under Phase 4/5 boundary indicators); "Regulatory arbitrage" products appearing in 401(k) menus — private credit, tokenized assets, interval funds (named watch list indicator — Warsh's pro-stablecoin, anti-CBDC supervisory posture, combined with the CLARITY Act moving through Congress, is the institutional architecture for crypto-in-retirement-plans arriving at the exact moment the DOL 401(k) safe harbor rule is active)

**Sections:** Regulatory Cycle, Market Behavior

**Scenario impact:** Confirms existing Phase 4/5 boundary framing and adds a new dimension — the supervisory posture split. The May 13 log entry documented the mechanism (DOJ probe as procedural lever); this entry documents the completed institutional transition and the market's dual read. Crypto is pricing Warsh as: (1) net-bearish on rate policy — QT continuation, smaller Fed balance sheet, zero 2026 rate cuts priced by CME FedWatch; BTC fell from ~$84,000 in early 2026 to ~$76,800 at swearing-in, down ~14% since nomination; $18.7B in Q1 spot Bitcoin ETF inflows occurred *into* the macro disappointment, not out of it; (2) net-bullish on supervision — removal of CBDC threat, private-stablecoin favorability, clearer framework for crypto-bank relationships, CLARITY Act tailwind. The two vectors are operating in opposite directions simultaneously. The market is not yet pricing a net resolution of this split — BTC's muted reaction ($76,772, -0.55% on swearing-in day) is consistent with a market that has already absorbed the rate-policy headwind (priced from confirmation onward) while waiting for supervisory signals from Warsh's first FOMC (June 16–17) and first public statements. The White House swearing-in ceremony — first Fed chair sworn in at the White House since Greenspan in 1987, per multiple outlets — is itself a watch list indicator: it is the institutional-optics confirmation of the Phase 5 political-reversal-of-Fed-independence pattern logged May 13 and May 19. The FOMC gave unanimous backing to Warsh on the day of swearing-in, which removes the internal-dissent scenario that some analysts had flagged as a constraint on political capture.

**Source:** CryptoTimes, "Pro-Crypto Warsh Sworn in as Fed Chair: What It Means for Bitcoin Market," May 22, 2026 (Tier 2 — crypto trade press, confirmed swearing-in date and BTC price at ~$76,772); Bitcoin.com News, "Kevin Warsh Takes Fed Chair Oath as FOMC Gives Unanimous Backing," May 22, 2026 (Tier 2); CoinDesk, "Who is Kevin Warsh: Trump's Fed chair nominee's return sparks bitcoin jitters over rates, balance sheet cuts," January 30, 2026 (Tier 2 — portfolio disclosure and policy stance background); 247 Wall St., "Kevin Warsh Confirmed as Fed Chair: The 5 Things That Could Decide How Bitcoin Reacts," May 13, 2026 (Tier 3 — analysis only); Benzinga, "Bitcoin Sells Off Under New Fed Chairs: Will History Repeat Itself Under Kevin Warsh?" May 2026 (Tier 3 — historical pattern analysis). No Tier 1 Federal Reserve press release or formal supervisory guidance issued at swearing-in.

**Note:** The analytically significant element is not BTC's price level but the bifurcated read: institutional buyers added $18.7B in Q1 spot ETF inflows *during* the rate-policy headwind — treating Warsh-era tighter money as a buying opportunity rather than a structural reason to exit. This is consistent with the watch list's "quiet institutional buying while retail panics" Stage 4 diagnostic inversion — the smart-money direction is long BTC as an inflation hedge against the same 3.8% CPI that is preventing the rate cuts crypto would normally need for a rally. The supervisory-bullish dimension (stablecoin framework, banking access, CLARITY Act) has not yet produced observable regulatory action — it is currently a posture signal, not a policy signal. The June 16–17 FOMC is the next hard binary: a rate cut would be bullish for crypto on liquidity grounds but would confirm Phase 5 political capture; a hold or hike signal would be bearish for crypto on liquidity grounds but would be consistent with monetary-policy independence. The two most important crypto-specific watch items going forward: (1) Warsh's first formal statement on stablecoin regulation or crypto-bank relationships as Fed Chair; (2) CLARITY Act progress in the Senate following Warsh's swearing-in.

### PGSA toll payments confirmed transacting via USDT and Bitcoin — FinCEN Alert FIN-2026-Alert002 (May 11), OFAC $344M CBI freeze (April 24), Tether coordinated action: first Tier 1 confirmation that crypto rails are live for Hormuz toll collection

**Indicators:** IRGC naval activity (named watch list indicator — the toll-collection infrastructure is the administrative and financial superstructure of the IRGC's "strict control" zone; the FinCEN alert explicitly names stablecoin payments by petroleum, shipping, trading, or trust companies as the red-flag typology, directly naming the toll mechanism as a designated-entity payment route); Brent crude trajectory (named watch list indicator — if the PGSA toll regime generates $600–800M/month in crypto receipts at current traffic levels, as public estimates suggest, it creates a durable financial incentive for Iran to maintain the zone-control architecture regardless of ceasefire negotiations, which structurally raises the floor on how cheaply Scenario B can be sustained from Iran's side); AIS mine clearance progress (adjacent — the de-escalation condition "commercial insurers re-enter market" becomes materially harder if the toll regime is confirmed as an operating revenue stream; insurers cannot price a corridor that is simultaneously an OFAC-designated payment route)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict, Regulatory Cycle (secondary — OFAC/FinCEN enforcement actions on stablecoin issuers and exchanges are the regulatory-cycle signal that crypto-financial infrastructure is now being treated as a sanctions-enforcement problem, not merely a compliance advisory)

**Scenario impact:** Materially advances the Armed Conflict framing — the PGSA toll-payment question that the May 22 entries flagged as open is now partially answered. The evidence hierarchy: (1) **FinCEN Alert FIN-2026-Alert002 (May 11, Tier 1 primary)** — issued by FinCEN, explicitly warns financial institutions and crypto firms to monitor for "unusual digital asset payments by petroleum, shipping, trading or trust companies" related to IRGC Hormuz toll collection; names USDT stablecoins as the primary instrument; directs SARs with terrorist-financing designation; names Nobitex, Zedcex, and Zedxion (OFAC-designated January 2026) as the named exchange network; references the USDZ stablecoin associated with Zedxion. (2) **OFAC action April 24 (Tier 1 primary)** — designated two wallets associated with Bank Markazi (Iran's Central Bank) and coordinated with Tether to freeze USD 344.2M in USDT; TRM Labs characterizes the wallets as "sovereign reserve storage" with ~$370M received since 2021 in ~1,000 transactions; TRM explicitly states they are not seeing on-chain evidence that toll payments are occurring *at scale* — the freeze targets CBI reserve infrastructure, not a confirmed live toll-payment wallet. (3) **Chainalysis (Tier 2 institutional)** — IRGC-associated addresses received $3B+ in 2025, representing ~50% of Iran's total crypto ecosystem; confirms USDT/stablecoins dominate over Bitcoin for IRGC commerce; the Chainalysis Hormuz-specific blog is predictive rather than confirmatory on toll transactions specifically. (4) **TRM Labs (Tier 2 institutional)** — confirms Iranian-linked wallet inflows increased since toll system went live but attributes this to broader IRGC commercial activity, not specifically toll payments; states attribution of specific toll-payment transactions remains difficult. **Net assessment:** The FinCEN alert is Tier 1 confirmation that the US government is treating PGSA toll payments via crypto as a live sanctions-evasion typology requiring active monitoring — this is the government's own acknowledgment that the payment rails are live or credibly imminent. The OFAC/Tether $344M freeze is Tier 1 confirmation that USDT is the primary instrument in Iran's sovereign crypto reserve infrastructure. However, no Tier 1 or Tier 2 source has yet produced transaction-level on-chain evidence of specific toll payments clearing through confirmed wallets. The question is confirmed as a live operational problem by the US government; it is not yet confirmed as settled fact by on-chain forensics.

**Source:** FinCEN Alert FIN-2026-Alert002, "FinCEN Alert on Iran's Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps' Use of Digital Assets," May 11, 2026 — fincen.gov (Tier 1 primary — US Treasury Financial Crimes Enforcement Network official alert; confirmed via Elliptic compliance response blog citing full alert metadata); OFAC, designation of Bank Markazi (Central Bank of Iran) crypto addresses, April 24, 2026 — ofac.treasury.gov (Tier 1 primary — confirmed via TRM Labs blog, Chainalysis blog, and multiple Tier 2 corroborators); TRM Labs, "OFAC Sanctions Crypto Addresses Associated with the Central Bank of Iran, Freezes USD 344 Million," April 2026 (Tier 2 institutional — TRM is an on-chain analytics firm; formal published report); Chainalysis, "Iran's Strait of Hormuz Crypto Toll," April 2026 (Tier 2 institutional — Chainalysis is an on-chain analytics firm; formal published blog/report); Fortune, "Iran is demanding tankers in the Strait of Hormuz pay tolls in crypto: What we know so far," April 10, 2026 (Tier 2 — Fortune News, citing Iranian government and IRGC statements); CoinDesk, "Tether's $344 million USDT freeze linked to U.S. 'Economic Fury' against Iran regime," April 24, 2026 (Tier 2); Elliptic, "How crypto compliance teams should respond to FinCEN's IRGC alert," May 2026 (Tier 2 — compliance firm response to FinCEN alert, confirms alert date and field requirements). Note: Circle compliance-failure allegations ($420M+) referenced in one search result but not confirmed via Tier 1 or formal Tier 2 source — excluded pending verification.

**Note:** The FinCEN alert is the single most analytically material signal of this pass. It converts the PGSA crypto-toll question from a press-report inference to a US government-designated enforcement priority. The implication for the watch list's Scenario B geometry is structural: if the PGSA toll system is generating confirmed crypto receipts (even if the exact scale is not yet on-chain-confirmed), Iran has a financial incentive to maintain the toll architecture independent of ceasefire terms — the toll regime is not just a coercive mechanism but a revenue stream. The Rubio "unfeasible" statement (logged May 22) and the FinCEN alert are co-occurring: the US government is simultaneously declaring the toll regime a deal-breaker diplomatically and a sanctions-evasion priority criminally, while the on-chain infrastructure is live enough to produce a $344M CBI reserve freeze. The Tether action is the most important compliance signal: Tether coordinated proactively with OFAC, which is consistent with Warsh-era Fed supervisory posture favoring private-stablecoin compliance frameworks over CBDC — but it also demonstrates that private stablecoins are now the front line of sanctions enforcement, which is a governance constraint the industry will face with every future geopolitical episode. Next Tier 1 data points to watch: (1) OFAC country-specific SDN list updates naming PGSA or additional CBI-linked wallets; (2) TRM Labs or Chainalysis publishing transaction-level evidence linking specific vessel transit records to specific wallet flows; (3) Circle formal response to the compliance-failure allegation (if confirmed, it is a watch list indicator in its own right under "enforcement actions against major financial institutions revealing compliance failures masked during deregulation").

## 2026-05-22

### Iran-Oman permanent Hormuz toll system: Rubio declares any deal "unfeasible" if tolls proceed; Trump rejects; PGSA framework formalization attempt underway

**Indicators:** AIS mine clearance progress (named watch list indicator — de-escalation signal condition: "US CENTCOM announces verified safe corridor; commercial insurers re-enter market" — the toll-system formalization is the structural inverse of this condition; a permanent revenue-based access regime administered by the PGSA is incompatible with the watch list's de-escalation corridor geometry); IRGC naval activity (named watch list indicator — the toll system is the administrative superstructure over the IRGC's declared "vast operational area"; formalizing it with Oman as co-administrator converts the IRGC's tactical zone-control into a durable institutional arrangement); Brent crude trajectory (named watch list indicator — Brent declining from $116.73 on May 18 to ~$103.94 on May 22 on deal-proximity narrative, but the toll-system disclosure introduces a structural obstacle that the Brent decline does not yet price; weekly Brent -6% reflects deal-narrative optimism, not the toll impasse)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict, Global Debt (secondary — if the PGSA toll framework is operationalized, it converts a crisis-induced cost into a structural levy on the 21% of global oil transit passing through Hormuz, repricing energy costs permanently rather than episodically)

**Scenario impact:** Scenario B geometry materially complicated. The Managed Naval Standoff scenario requires an implicit or explicit arrangement under which both Iran and the US accept the strait's operational status without a formal confrontation — the toll-system initiative is directly antagonistic to that equilibrium. Rubio's "unfeasible" statement is the strongest US diplomatic language used against any specific Iranian position since the ceasefire began; it elevates the toll question to a deal-breaking condition from the US side. Iran's Ambassador Mohammad Amin-Nejad disclosed the Oman discussions in a Bloomberg interview (May 21) — this is not a back-channel signal but a public diplomatic statement, binding the Iranian foreign ministry to the position. Trump separately rejected the initiative, stating the US had "total control" of the waterway. The parallel Al-Arabiya "final draft" leak (eight-point ceasefire text, Scenario A/B-directional in form) deliberately omits all nuclear terms and all toll/PGSA terms — the core negotiating gaps are absent from the document, which the House of Saud media analysis noted immediately. Not a scenario probability change from this entry alone; but the toll framework represents a new structural obstacle that does not appear in the current watch list scenario table and should be incorporated in the next Synthesis pass.

**Source:** Bloomberg, "Iran in Talks With Oman Over Permanent Hormuz Toll System," May 21, 2026 (Tier 2 — Bloomberg News, citing Iranian Ambassador Mohammad Amin-Nejad in direct interview); CNBC, "U.S., Iran signal peace progress — but remain at odds over enriched uranium, Strait of Hormuz tolls," May 22, 2026 (Tier 2); The National News, "Rubio says toll system in Strait of Hormuz would make deal 'unfeasible'," May 21, 2026 (Tier 2); Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty, "Trump, Rubio Warn Against Iranian Tolling System in Strait of Hormuz," May 21, 2026 (Tier 2); Times of Israel, "Rubio says Iran talks show 'good signs,' but Hormuz tolls would make deal 'unfeasible'," May 22, 2026 (Tier 2). No Tier 1 State Department press release found; Tier 2 sourcing is adequate for the Rubio and Trump quotations.

**Note:** The toll-system formalization attempt represents a structural shift in Iran's negotiating posture: from a temporary crisis-induced access-control mechanism to a permanent revenue-producing administrative framework. This is categorically distinct from the PGSA toll arrangements logged May 18 (Chinese transits occurring under the fee structure as a fait accompli). The Oman-as-co-administrator framing is designed to give the arrangement multilateral legitimacy — Oman's historical role as the US-Iran back-channel makes its potential endorsement diplomatically significant. Rubio's "unfeasible" statement forecloses the Scenario B equilibrium path that assumes gradual normalization around an informal Iranian zone-control without a formal toll regime. The watch list's scenario table does not currently model a "permanent toll dispute as deal-blocker" condition; this entry opens that variable for the next Synthesis pass.

### Khamenei directive: enriched uranium must stay in Iran — structural block on the primary US demand; deal gap from negotiating position to supreme-leader order

**Indicators:** US-China diplomatic signaling (named watch list indicator — adjacently relevant: Xi's mediation offer (May 14) positioned China as a potential face-saving intermediary on precisely this question — the HEU stockpile disposition; Khamenei's directive forecloses the stockpile-abroad resolution pathway Xi's mediation was designed to facilitate); Brent crude trajectory (named watch list indicator — the Khamenei directive is a structural constraint operating against the deal-proximate Brent decline; the directive was issued May 21 and Brent was ~$108.76 on May 21 before moving to ~$103.94 on May 22 under continued deal-narrative momentum — the market has not yet priced the directive's structural significance)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict

**Scenario impact:** Narrows Scenario A probability; tightens Scenario B constraints. The enriched uranium stockpile disposition has been identified by Israeli officials (per Reuters) as a condition Trump personally assured Israel would be included in any deal. Khamenei's directive — issued through "senior Iranian sources" per Al-Arabiya (May 21) — converts Iran's negotiating position from a tactical concession-to-be-traded into a supreme-leader order, which in Iranian constitutional structure is not reversible by the negotiating team. Before the current war, Iran had signaled willingness to ship out half its 60%-enriched stockpile; Khamenei's post-war directive removes that concession entirely, stating the material must stay because its removal would leave Iran more vulnerable to future US-Israeli attack. The Al-Arabiya "final draft" leaked the same day contains no enrichment provisions — consistent with Khamenei's directive having already been communicated to the negotiating team. The gap between what Trump assured Israel and what Khamenei has ordered is the single highest-probability deal-breaker in the current structure. No scenario probability change warranted from this entry alone, but the directive is the most analytically material signal of this pass for the Scenario A/B convergence question.

**Source:** Al-Arabiya, "Supreme Leader says enriched uranium must stay in Iran, Iranian sources say," May 21, 2026 (Tier 2 — Saudi state-aligned broadcaster; citing unnamed senior Iranian sources; not confirmed by Tier 1 Iranian official press); Daily Sabah, "Iran supreme leader vows to keep enriched uranium in country," May 21, 2026 (Tier 2); Reuters reporting (cited in secondary sources as basis for Israeli officials' confirmation of Trump's assurance — Tier 1 wire service, source chain confirmed via The Week India and Indian Defence News) (Tier 2 secondary). Note: the directive itself has not been published as a Tier 1 official Iranian government document; it is characterized as a supreme-leader position via Iranian sources. Sourcing is adequate for a watch-list log entry but not independently sufficient for a scenario probability change.

**Note:** The Khamenei uranium directive and the Hormuz toll formalization (previous entry) are co-occurring structural obstacles, logged the same day. Together they constitute a pair of new blocking conditions that were not in the scenario table as of May 18: the US has publicly declared the toll regime "unfeasible" (Rubio), and the HEU stockpile removal — which Trump assured Israel would be included — has been foreclosed by supreme-leader order. Neither alone constitutes a Level 4 trigger; together they raise the probability that the "deal-proximity narrative" driving Brent's weekly -6% and the 10-yr's Friday stabilization reflects holiday-window position-squaring rather than a genuine convergence trajectory. This pair warrants explicit attention in the next Synthesis Reviewer pass.

### Al-Arabiya "final draft" leak (May 22) and Rubio "slight progress / good signs": ceasefire-framing document omits all nuclear terms; Brent weekly -6% on deal narrative entering Memorial Day weekend

**Indicators:** Brent crude trajectory (named watch list indicator — directional but requires holiday-window discount: Brent weekly decline from $116.73 to ~$103.94 is substantial; it is occurring on deal-narrative proximity, but the two new blocking conditions (toll regime, HEU directive) were not priced in the Friday session; thin liquidity into Memorial Day amplifies the signal-noise problem); US-Iran diplomatic signaling context (named watch list indicator — the Al-Arabiya leak is the Saudi state-aligned broadcaster's second attempt in 24 hours to frame deal finalization after a retracted "deal reached" report on May 21; Rubio confirmed "slight progress" and "good signs" alongside "gaps remain"; the pattern is identical to pre-announcement framing in the April 8 ceasefire cycle)

The holiday-context flag from the user brief applies: a 5-10bp yield move or $5/bbl oil move on a Friday-before-Memorial-Day is weaker evidence than the same move mid-week. **Source:** Al-Arabiya, "US-Iran draft deal mediated by Pakistan could be announced within hours," May 22, 2026 (Tier 2 — Saudi state-aligned; second attempt after May 21 retraction; explicit sourcing from unnamed Pakistani mediation officials); The Week India, "Final draft of US-Iran deal leaked?", May 22, 2026 (Tier 2); PBS NewsHour, "U.S. says 'slight progress' in Iran talks," May 22, 2026 (Tier 2 — citing Rubio directly); CNBC, "U.S., Iran signal peace progress," May 22, 2026 (Tier 2); Fortune, "Current price of oil as of May 22, 2026," May 22, 2026 (Tier 3 — Brent $103.94–$104.68 range May 22; consistent with prices.csv directional read).

**Note:** The Al-Arabiya retraction-then-re-leak pattern within 24 hours is analytically notable: it indicates active information-management around the deal timeline rather than organic reporting. The Saudi state-aligned broadcaster's framing of a "deal within hours" that omits all nuclear terms is consistent with Saudi Arabia's interest in a rapid Hormuz reopening regardless of the nuclear architecture — Saudi energy economics and navigation security diverge sharply from the Israeli red-line on HEU stockpile removal. The Rubio "slight progress" simultaneous with the Al-Arabiya "hours away" language is the same structural ambiguity the agent-brief's confounding-factor note identifies as Trump-administration messaging volatility. **Indicators:** Private equity NAV markdowns or redemption gates at major funds (named watch list indicator — this is a structural first: non-traded BDC redemptions ($6.9–7.0B accepted) exceeded new capital raised ($4.9–5.0B) in Q1 2026, per Bloomberg / Robert A. Stanger & Co.; no prior quarter on record has seen net outflows from the non-traded BDC segment; this is the asset-class-level structural inflection, not a single-fund gate); Corporate zombie refinancing failures as rates stay elevated (named watch list indicator — the Q1 net-outflow milestone is the aggregate expression of the individual platform gate cascade logged April 13 and May 21; at the asset-class level it confirms that the gate cascade has crossed the fundraising threshold — the vehicles are now net capital destroyers in the retail channel)

**Sections:** Market Behavior, Global Debt

**Scenario impact:** Advances the existing framing — this is the single most analytically material Market Behavior signal of this pass. The May 21 entry logged BofA's Q2 forecast (redemptions likely to peak in Q2); this Bloomberg May 14 headline reports the Q1 outturn as a confirmed structural first. The distinction matters: a forecast is Tier 2 analysis; a data-confirmed Q1 net-outflow milestone reported by Bloomberg citing Robert A. Stanger & Co. is Tier 2 institutional primary data. This milestone is the asset-class analog of a mutual fund sector going from net-creator to net-redeemer — it signals that the retail capital channel into private credit, which the DOL 401(k) safe harbor rule (active watch list indicator, Regulatory section) is designed to expand, is now structurally contracting at the same time the regulatory architecture for its expansion is being built. The Stage 4 and Minsky Phase 3 framing is confirmed and deepened; the HY spread at 2.78% (May 21, prices.csv) still does not show the commercial-bank transmission, but the non-traded BDC net-outflow milestone is the clearest structural evidence yet that the private credit stress is not reversing.

Note: the Bloomberg article is dated May 14, which is within 48 hours from the last log only if the May 21 pass missed it; it was not mentioned in the May 21 log entries, so it is logged here as new material. Tier 1 primary would be Robert A. Stanger & Co. published data report; the Bloomberg citation is Tier 2 institutional.

**Note:** The Q1 net-outflow milestone is the signal the watch list's Kindleberger Stage 4 framework predicts: the "smart money exit" in private credit has now crossed the threshold at which retail inflows can no longer absorb the institutional exit pressure. The DOL 401(k) safe harbor rule is designed to expand the retail channel into this same asset class at the exact moment the asset class is experiencing its first structural net-outflow quarter. That is the direct regulatory-market feedback loop the April 13 convergence report identified as the core Phase 4/5 boundary risk. The BCRED situation (Q1: Blackstone raised cap to 7% and used $400M employee capital to honor all requests, avoiding a gate) remains the critical forward indicator: if BCRED gates in Q2, the one absorber in the system stops absorbing, and the net-outflow dynamic accelerates. The May 22 BCRED SEC filing search returned no Q2 gate announcement as of today.

## 2026-05-21

### Foreign official-sector custody drain: $24B WoW, $170B YoY, lowest since 2012; May 10-yr indirect bidder share falls to 64% from 74.5%; primary yield-move driver remains domestic with forced-sale official-sector contribution

**Indicators:** 10-year Treasury yield sustained above 4.75% (precursor — 10-yr hit 4.67% on May 19 and 4.65% on May 20; still below the 4.75% WARN line but the foreign-official-sector selling dimension adds a second independent transmission channel to the yield move alongside the inflation-expectations and fiscal-supply channels logged May 9 and May 12); Currency war signals: competitive devaluations, G7 FX intervention, or dollar weaponization complaints (named watch list indicator — Japan spent ¥5.01T / ~$32B in two FX intervention bouts in late April and early May 2026 to defend yen at 160; FX intervention at this scale structurally requires reserve liquidation, most likely Treasury sales; this is the "FX intervention forcing Treasury sales" mechanism); Shadow banking stress events — money market fund gates, repo market disruptions (adjacent precursor — 10-year auction tail widened from 0.7bp to 5.5bp in two months, combined with dealer takedown share rising, is the early auction-internals precursor to the repo/basis-trade dislocation pathway); Sovereign credit spread widening in high-debt G7 members (directional — the 20-yr auction clearing at 5.122% on May 20, up 24bp from the April 22 result of 4.883%, is consistent with term-premium repricing on US sovereign issuance, the precursor before spread widening is confirmed)

**Sections:** Global Debt, Armed Conflict

**Scenario impact:** Confirms existing and adds a second transmission channel. The rate move is no longer solely domestic (expectations + fiscal supply); a foreign official-sector selling component is now documented in Tier 1 custody data, though its magnitude relative to the domestic channel is uncertain and it does not yet independently constitute a Level 4 trigger. Fed H.4.1 custody account for marketable Treasury securities held in custody for foreign official and international accounts fell from $2,737,892M (May 6) to $2,713,935M (May 13) — a one-week decline of $24B. Year-over-year the account is down $169.8B (~5.9%) from $2,883,740M on May 14, 2025. Aggregate $82B decline since February 25, 2026; total custody holdings at lowest level since 2012. Deutsche Bank estimate ~$60B net central bank sales over four weeks through March 19; Longbridge Financial estimate $90B+ including quasi-official accounts. TIC March 2026 data (released May 18) shows -$14.9B net foreign official long-term Treasury sales and -$11.4B total official outflows; country breakdown not yet in the March release. Auction internals consistent with softening but not collapsing foreign demand: 10-yr indirect bidder share fell from 74.5% (March) to 64.0% (May 12), tail widened from 0.7bp to 5.5bp, BTC 2.45 → 2.13; 30-yr May 13 auction at 5.046% with indirect ~66.4% and BTC 2.303; 20-yr May 20 auction cleared at 5.122%, up 24bp from April 22's 4.883%. The dominant country drivers are not China or Japan in a strategic-exit sense — leading sellers per Deutsche Bank attribution are Turkey, Thailand, and India, economies under simultaneous FX intervention, energy-import, and defense-spending pressure. This is the "forced reserve liquidation under energy-shock pressure" mechanism, not the "strategic de-dollarization" mechanism. **Important caveat (Reuters / McGeever):** in 2025, a $238B custody decline corresponded to only $34B in actual net sales — the rest was custodian relocation. The current $82B headline figure likely overstates the actual exit by a material margin. The framework distinction between forced (episodic, self-limiting) and strategic (structural, self-reinforcing) official selling is determinative for escalation; current evidence favors the forced/episodic interpretation but the April TIC data (June 18 release) is the next analytically material data point.

**Source:** Federal Reserve H.4.1 release, May 14, 2026 — federalreserve.gov/releases/h41/current/ (Tier 1 primary — custody holdings $2,713,935M on May 13 vs. $2,737,892M on May 6 vs. $2,883,740M one year prior); U.S. Department of the Treasury, TIC March 2026 press release — home.treasury.gov/news/press-releases/sb0499 (Tier 1 primary — -$14.9B net official long-term sales, -$11.4B total official outflows); TreasuryDirect official auction results, May 12 10-yr (4.468%, BTC 2.13, indirect 64.0%, tail 5.5bp) and May 13 30-yr (5.046%, BTC 2.303, indirect ~66.4%) (Tier 1 primary); FRED series WMTSECL1 — Memorandum Items: Custody Holdings: Marketable U.S. Treasury Securities: Wednesday Level (Tier 1 primary); FSB, "Vulnerabilities in Government Bond-backed Repo Markets," February 4, 2026 (Tier 1 institutional — repo/basis-trade transmission pathway); Deutsche Bank four-week flow estimate (~$60B net central bank sales through March 19) via Rankedbrief (Tier 2); Longbridge Financial estimate ($90B+ including quasi-official) via Rankedbrief (Tier 2); CNBC / LSEG / Nikkei Asia — Japan FX intervention ¥5.01T (~$32B) across two bouts April 30 and early May (Tier 2); Bond Buyer, "Weak 20-year auction sends Treasury yields higher," May 21, 2026 (Tier 2); Seeking Alpha / FT — "Foreign central bank holdings of Treasuries at the NY Fed at the lowest level since 2012" (Tier 2); Reuters / Jamie McGeever via Substack — 2025 $238B custody decline / $34B actual sales discrepancy framing (Tier 2); PBOC/NFRA "window guidance" reporting via financial content aggregators, late February 2026 (Tier 3 only — not eligible as standalone primary evidence; flagged for Tier 1 confirmation if PBOC or NFRA issues an official statement).

**Note:** The custody-account series overstates actual net selling. The Reuters/McGeever caveat — that 2025's $238B custody decline corresponded to only $34B in actual sales — applies a heavy discount to the headline $82B figure since February 25. Three pending data points will resolve the strategic-vs-forced driver question: (1) the April 2026 TIC data scheduled for release June 18 will show whether China and Japan accelerated selling in the peak-energy-shock period and is the single highest-priority pending data point; (2) the May 20 20-year auction full internals (indirect bidder %, BTC, tail) will confirm whether the 5.122% clearing yield reflects demand deterioration or expectations repricing; (3) the May 20 H.4.1 custody reading will show whether the $24B weekly drain continued or reversed after the intraday yield reversal on May 20. Until then, the entry is logged at Level 1 with an elevated monitoring flag: if the 10-yr closes above 4.75% (8bp from current), upgrade to Level 2 position update. The Minsky Phase 4 propagation pathway via the Treasury-collateral channel — 10-yr above 5.0% → repo haircuts rise → basis-trade margin calls → forced unwind amplifies yield → repo dysfunction → MMF NAV pressure — is the analytical structure to watch; the FSB February 4, 2026 report on Government Bond-backed Repo Markets is the institutional anchor for that transmission pathway and warrants reading before the next Synthesis pass.

### UK/France coalition Hormuz naval deployment — HMS Dragon pre-positioned; coalition mission contingent on ceasefire sustainability

**Indicators:** AIS mine clearance progress (named watch list indicator — de-escalation signal partially activated: HMS Dragon pre-positioned but coalition mission contingent on "conditions stabilizing further" — not a declared safe corridor; commercial insurers have not re-entered the market; the watch list de-escalation condition "US CENTCOM announces verified safe corridor; commercial insurers re-enter market" remains unmet); US-China diplomatic signaling (adjacent — UK/France coalition entry changes the allied geometry around the blockade; Iran has issued a warning against the deployment, IRGC standard procedural escalation signal); Brent crude trajectory (de-escalation-directional: the coalition framework plus deal-negotiation narrative drove Brent to ~$105–110 range May 20–21, below the April peak of $124)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict

**Scenario impact:** Confirms existing Scenario B geometry and introduces a new structural feature: a UK/France-led multinational coalition as an alternative or parallel mechanism to US-only Project Freedom. This is analytically distinct from the previous framing (US unilateral escort under IRGC fire). The HMS Dragon Type 45 deployment (Sea Viper air-defence, Wildcat helicopters with Martlet missiles) gives the coalition layered missile/drone protection beyond the US DDG escort model. Iran's warning against the deployment is the IRGC's standard procedural escalation signal; it does not itself constitute the watch-list "IRGC naval activity escalation" indicator. The key analytical question this entry opens: does a UK/France-declared safe corridor, if announced, satisfy the watch-list's CENTCOM-corridor de-escalation signal, or does it require a US-named corridor? The watch list names "US CENTCOM" specifically; a NATO/UK-led corridor would be functionally equivalent but nominally distinct. No scenario probability change warranted by this entry alone.

**Source:** Army Recognition / The Defence News / Naval Today — multiple outlets covering UK MoD announcement, May 9–13, 2026 (Tier 2); Royal Navy Joins Hormuz Security Operation, The British Eye, May 13, 2026 (Tier 2); Iran issues warning as UK deploys destroyer, Naval Today, May 11, 2026 (Tier 2). No Tier 1 primary (UK MoD press release) confirmed in current search results; Tier 2 sourcing adequate for event confirmation but not for quantitative claims.

**Note:** The coalition deployment is a structural change the watch list had not explicitly tracked — it introduces a multinational framework as a potential pathway to a ceasefire-adjacent de-escalation architecture. The watch list currently tracks only US operational behavior and Chinese/Indian vessel behavior. The UK/France coalition entry adds a third state actor with declared operational intent to enforce shipping protection, which modestly increases the probability of a Scenario B-sustaining development: a ceasefire framework + multinational corridor could produce the commercial-insurer re-entry signal the watch list names as the hard de-escalation marker. The coalition mission is explicitly conditioned on ceasefire sustainability — meaning this entry does not independently change scenario probabilities but creates the institutional pre-positioning that would allow them to change.

### US-China sanctions friction over Iran missile support — State Dept. designates Chinese entities aiding IRGC ballistic missile and drone programs; concurrent with deal-framework negotiations

**Indicators:** US-China diplomatic signaling (named watch list indicator — the named escalation signal is "PLA Navy deployment orders; Chinese state media escalates rhetoric"; this is a different but related axis — executive-branch sanctions on Chinese entities during active diplomacy is the friction signal between the Trump–Xi Beijing summit de-escalation-adjacent framing and continued Chinese material support for Iran's military programs); Chinese/Indian vessel behavior (adjacent — the sanctions target satellite imagery provision and aerospace materials for IRGC programs, which feeds back into whether China's assurance at the Trump–Xi summit that it "will not supply Iran with military equipment" is being operationally honored)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict, Global Debt (secondary — China-US economic friction pathway)

**Scenario impact:** Directionally ambiguous — the May 8 State Department sanctions action sits between the May 14 Trump–Xi de-escalation summit and the ongoing MOU negotiations, simultaneously. This is the watch list's Scenario D pathway via Chinese material-support continuation: if Beijing's assurance against military equipment supply is not operationally honored (satellite imagery and aerospace materials for Shahed/ballistic programs being the specific allegations), the basis for Xi's mediation role narrows. The sanctions action itself is routine in scope (10 entities, 5 countries) and does not constitute a PLA Navy deployment or a direct Scenario D escalation; it is a diplomatic-friction signal operating in parallel with the deal-framework track. The concurrent-with-deal timing is the analytically notable feature: the Trump administration sanctioned Chinese entities on May 8 and held the Trump–Xi summit on May 14. This is consistent with the "sanctions as negotiating leverage" framing, not the "rupture" framing. No scenario probability change warranted.

**Source:** CNBC, "U.S. sanctions companies and individuals in the Middle East and China for helping Iran," May 9, 2026 (Tier 2); The Hill, "US sanctions firms in China, Middle East for allegedly aiding Iran," May 2026 (Tier 2); Jerusalem Post, May 2026 (Tier 2); State Dept. press release on ballistic missile sanctions — state.gov/releases (Tier 1 primary — confirmed via CNBC and The Hill's Tier 1 sourcing attribution).

**Note:** The parallel structure — sanctions during negotiations — is the same Trump negotiating-style pattern logged since April (messaging volatility confounding factor in the agent-brief). The analytically material question is whether the sanctioned entities are distinct from those Xi's assurance covered, or whether sanctioned entities are inside the "military equipment" category Xi's assurance addressed. Search results do not resolve this; satellite imagery and Shahed/ballistic materials are ambiguously inside or outside the "military equipment" boundary depending on interpretation. Until the April TIC data (June 18) and the China-side operational behavior on Hormuz transits are both available, the China-as-mediator and China-as-continued-supplier framing remain in tension.

### US–Iran one-page MOU framework: 14-point structure near completion but unsigned as of May 20–21; nuclear enrichment gap unresolved; Brent falls on deal narrative

**Indicators:** Brent crude trajectory (named watch list indicator — de-escalation signal direction: Brent declined from ~$116 on May 18 to ~$105–110 on May 20–21 on deal-framework reporting; this is the "Brent retreats below $105 on mine clearance progress" direction but the watch list threshold condition — mine clearance progress — is not met; the retreat is on MOU negotiation narrative, not operational mine clearance); US-China diplomatic signaling (adjacent — MOU framework would require Hormuz reopening within 30 days of signing; China's transit objectives are partially aligned with this); IRGC naval activity (structurally relevant — the ceasefire-framework framing keeps the ceasefire nominally in place during negotiations, which is the Scenario B "managed standoff" condition)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict, Global Debt (secondary — deal-driven Brent decline removes some pressure from the energy-shock-CPI spiral logged May 12)

**Scenario impact:** De-escalation directional but not a confirmed signal. The structure of the MOU (14 points, 30-day negotiation trigger, uranium removal from Iran, 12–20 year enrichment moratorium, US sanctions relief and naval blockade withdrawal) is the most detailed and advanced framework publicly described since the conflict began. The "closest the parties have been" sourcing (multiple Tier 2 outlets citing unnamed officials) is the standard pre-deal-announcement framing used in prior rounds (the April 8 ceasefire was preceded by identical sourcing). The critical unresolved element — uranium enrichment duration (Iran proposed 5 years, US demanded 20; reporting suggests a landing spot of 12–15 years) — has been the structural gap since February talks. The Brent decline is the same narrative-driven whiplash pattern the agent-brief flags as a confounding factor: April 17's $98 Brent print on Araghchi's "completely open" statement reversed within 24 hours on IRGC fire. Until the MOU is signed, this entry does not constitute a scenario probability change — it is the deal-proximity narrative operating at its highest reported fidelity to date. The Pakistan-as-direct-mediator role alongside Oman is a new structural feature the watch list's Oman-only mediation framing should incorporate.

**Source:** Axios, "US, Iran closing in on one-page memo to end war," May 6, 2026 (Tier 2); Al Jazeera, "What we know about Iran's response," May 8, 2026 (Tier 2); CNN live updates, May 6 (Tier 2–3); The Hill, "What's in the US's 1-page proposal," May 2026 (Tier 2); House of Commons Library, US-Iran ceasefire briefing (Tier 2 institutional); Fortune, May 19–20 Brent price articles (Tier 3 — corroborated by prices.csv for directional consistency).

**Note:** This entry should not be logged as a scenario probability change. The MOU framework has been in advanced-but-unsigned status since at least May 6, which is before the current 48-hour window. What this entry captures is the Brent market's response to the deal narrative on May 20–21, which is a watch-list-relevant signal against the de-escalation condition threshold: the move takes Brent from $116 to ~$108, still above the $105 de-escalation threshold and far above the $95 WARN line. The structurally important pending data point is whether the MOU is signed before the next pass, which would fire the Scenario A/B probability adjustment the May 14 Trump–Xi entry introduced as a possibility. If the MOU is signed before the next pass, recommend an immediate Synthesis Reviewer run.

### Q2 2026 private credit redemption window opens — BofA forecasts peak quarter for BDC requests; Blackstone BCRED expected to gate for first time; Apollo Debt Solutions at 15% projected

**Indicators:** Private equity NAV markdowns or redemption gates at major funds (named watch list indicator — Q2 window now open with BofA projecting peak; Blackstone BCRED, which did not gate in Q1, is expected to gate in Q2; Apollo Debt Solutions Q1 11.2% → Q2 15% projection; Blue Owl funds remain gated from Q1); Corporate zombie refinancing failures as rates stay elevated (named watch list indicator — Q2 gate projections extend the elevated-redemption-pressure period through June; the gate mechanism operates in the same Minsky Phase 3 dynamic the Q1 data confirmed)

**Sections:** Market Behavior, Global Debt

**Scenario impact:** Confirms existing and extends temporal duration. The Q1 2026 gate cascade was documented in the April 13 entry (Blue Owl OCIC 40.7%, OTIC 21.9% redemption requests; five platforms simultaneously gated). The Q2 window is now open with BofA forecasting that this will be the peak quarter for BDC redemption pressure. The new structural element is the BCRED dynamic: Blackstone did not gate in Q1 (it raised the cap to 7% and honored all requests with $400M in employee capital). If BCRED gates in Q2, it would be the first time since the gates began, and it would convert the narrative from "Blackstone is the one major platform absorbing rather than restricting" to "all major platforms are now restricting." That is an escalation within the Stage 4 private-credit-stress framework. The BofA projection (Tier 2 institutional) is a forecast, not a reported fact — actual Q2 gate decisions will be observable in May–June fund communications.

**Source:** PitchBook, citing Bank of America, "Private credit BDC redemption requests likely to peak in Q2 2026," 2026 (Tier 2 institutional — BofA as primary dealer research); Ferrante Capital Advisors, "Private Credit Q1 Scorecard: Who Paid, Who Gated" (Tier 2 institutional); Investment Executive, private credit recap (Tier 2). Tier 1 primary would be individual fund disclosures and 8-K/6-K filings when Q2 redemption decisions are announced; those are not yet available for the current window.

**Note:** The BCRED situation is the single most analytically important element. In Q1, Blackstone's decision to honor all redemptions by raising the cap and injecting employee capital was the signal that the framework's strongest player was absorbing rather than restricting, which cut against a cascading dynamic. If BCRED gates in Q2, the BofA projection reads as confirmation that the Q1 episode was a temporary absorption rather than a structural resilience signal. The analyst forecast is Tier 2; the actual gate announcement would be Tier 1 and should be logged immediately when it occurs. The 20–35% NAV discount to obtain secondary liquidity (cited in one search result for October 2026) is context for the secondary-market pressure dimension, not a current logged data point.

### JetBlue government-aid posture; Frontier and Avelo seek $2.5B federal package from DOT — AerCap Q1 2026 clean keeps lessor-impairment break condition unmet

**Indicators:** EU aviation fuel strategic reserve drawdown rate — buffer exhaustion timeline (named watch list indicator — the LCC sector's government-aid request formalizes the distress signal documented in the May 19 LCC addendum; it is operational evidence that the fuel-cost transmission has reached the government-intervention threshold at which public fiscal support is being solicited); Corporate zombie refinancing failures as rates stay elevated (named watch list indicator — JetBlue as the second US carrier disclosing material financial stress now signals a government-aid posture, the escalation from "guidance withdrawn" to "seeking public support"); Private equity NAV markdowns or redemption gates at major funds (adjacent — aviation lessor impairment break condition from May 19 addendum)

**Sections:** Armed Conflict, Market Behavior, Global Debt

**Scenario impact:** Advances the May 19 LCC addendum's framing — the addendum documented a bifurcation without a second failure; the government-aid solicitation is the next step on the distress spectrum. JetBlue's CEO described the fuel crisis as "the biggest headwind since the pandemic" and declined to rule out government support. Frontier and Avelo met with Secretary Duffy and FAA Administrator Bedford seeking a $2.5B federal package. This is the second US carrier (JetBlue) with a publicly stated government-aid posture, alongside a formal $2.5B lobbying effort by the ULCC tier. Analytically this is below the break condition named in the May 19 addendum (a lessor disclosing material impairment); it remains at the carrier-balance-sheet level. However, the government-aid request creates a new forward-looking watch item: a denial or delayed approval of the $2.5B package — which is the more likely outcome given the fiscal environment — would accelerate Frontier and Avelo's path toward failure-or-consolidation and increase the probability of the lessor-impairment trigger firing. The May 19 addendum's AerCap break condition is still unmet: AerCap Q1 2026 results show record basic lease income ($1.7B), a $54M asset impairment charge (routine), and strong share buyback continuation — no material Hormuz-related impairment disclosed.

**Source:** Aviation Week Network, "JetBlue: Fuel Crisis Biggest Headwind Since Pandemic, Aid Not Ruled Out," May 2026 (Tier 2); One Mile at a Time, "US Budget Airlines Demand $2.5 Billion In Government Assistance To Stay Afloat" (Tier 2); FlightGlobal, "Discount airlines not giving up on bid to secure government aid: Avelo CEO," May 2026 (Tier 2); AerCap Q1 2026 press release via PR Newswire, April 2026 (Tier 1 primary — 286 asset transactions, record lease income, $54M impairment charge; no Hormuz-related material impairment disclosed).

**Note:** The government-aid request formalizes the political-economy dimension of the fuel-shock transmission: the LCC tier is now soliciting public fiscal intervention, which puts the aviation-sector stress on a path toward congressional or executive-branch decisions about whether to provide relief. A refusal produces continued distress; a provision delays but does not cure the structural mismatch (fuel at $4.13–$4.28/gallon for Q2 vs. $2.40 prior year for JetBlue). The AerCap Q1 data is the most important single data point for the May 19 break condition: no material Hormuz impairment was disclosed, which keeps the aviation transmission at the operational-sector level and not the financial-system-propagation level. The break condition remains open and unmet as of today. This entry is *negative evidence* against the lessor-impairment break condition and should be preserved on the record alongside future AerCap / Air Lease / BOC / Avolon quarterly results.
